when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師時 , 她有做一些 , 但真正的事情是 , 說未來會比這個要好得多 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百多年後 , 這個人出現了alanturing在1936年重新發明了電腦
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器完全是機械的
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器完全是理論上
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩個人都是從數學的觀點來的 , 但turing告訴我們一些非常重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他為電腦科學奠定了數學的基礎 , 說: 「 不論你怎麼做電腦 , 都無所謂 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不管你電腦的機械原理 , 像是babbage的電腦 , 或是電子 , 就像現在的電腦 , 或是未來的電腦 , 或是細胞 , 又一次的 , 機械式的 , 一旦我們進入了奈米科技 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 把它變得很小 。 所有這些東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	在某種意義上 , 計算的本質
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這就是所謂的教堂-圖靈論 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	所以 , 突然間 , 你就有了這個連結 , 你說這東西是babbage建造的 , 是一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它能夠做到今天我們用電腦所做的一切 , 只是緩慢而已 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	給大家一個概念 , 它有多慢 , 它只有1k的記憶體 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它使用打孔卡 , 也就是放進去它的速度比第一台zx81要慢一萬倍
it did have a ram pack .	它確實有一個拉姆派克 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	想要加入大量額外的記憶體
so , where does that bring us today ?	那麼 , 這帶給我們什麼呢 ?
so there are plans .	所以有計畫的話 ,
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在swindon , 科學博物館的檔案庫 , 有上百個計劃 , 還有上千頁的筆記 , 由charlesbabbage寫的 , 關於這個分析引擎 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中有一組計劃我們稱之為計劃28這也是我和doronswade所創立的一個慈善機構的名稱它是科學博物館的管理者也是驅動這個計劃建造出一個不一樣引擎的人我們的計劃就是把它做出來
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在肯辛頓南部 , 我們會建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個計劃有許多部分
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	一是掃描babbage的檔案
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這已經完成 。 第二個是對所有計劃進行的研究 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是一個模擬那台機器的電腦最後一部分 , 是把它在科學博物館中做出來的 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它完成時 , 你終於能夠理解電腦是如何運作的 , 因為與其在你面前有一片小晶片 , 你必須看著這個巨大的東西 , 然後說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶體在運作 , 我看到cpu在運作 , 我聽到cpu在運作 。 我大概聞到了 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在這兩者之間 , 我們會進行模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	babbage自己寫到 , 他說 , 一旦分析引擎存在 , 它一定會引導未來科學的走向 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從未成功過 , 因為他總是在微笑著新的計畫 , 但當它真的在1940年代被建立起來 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我來讓你們看看影片中它的動作看起來是什麼樣子 , 用影片顯示cpu運作的一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	這只是三組齒輪它準備做加法 。 這是加法的運作機制 , 所以你可以想像這個巨大的機器
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年時間
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年代以前 , 我們將會有
thank you very much .	非常感謝 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這個填滿圖像的演講中 , 尤恩•阿爾伯特蘭展示了他三個最近關於人性的計畫 , 我們的棲息地--驚人的空拍照片--拍攝了他《從天而降》裡頭拍攝的《從天而降》的個人採訪 , 拍攝在他的網上 , 拍攝了《還有六十億人》 , 他很快就推出了《家園》 , 記錄了人類對於環境的影響 , 透過呼吸的影片 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、未來、人類、媒體、攝影 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	yannar-husbertrand在寬視角中捕捉到脆弱的地球
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球有很大的影響 , 可以乘飛機來到這裡 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣排放九噸二氧化碳 , 那是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來到這裡是為了談談生態學 , 我在一年中所排放的二氧化碳含量和法國人一樣多 。
so what do i have to do ?	那我該怎麼辦 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	我必須殺一個法國人 , 當我回家時 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我得要用另一種方式來處理我的碳排放 , 就像我每次都這樣 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上我的工作就是展示我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我會給你們看一些例子 , 最近我在過去一年拍的照片 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	亞伯達省的油砂 , 大量的污染 ,

in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在亞伯達省 , 每七小時便能提煉出24小時的石油
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油終結
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	油沙不是一個長期的解決方案
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們的石油使用量每年開採量的三倍
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的
coral reef in new caledonia .	新赫里多尼亞的珊瑚礁
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	在2050年以前 , 珊瑚中有100%會因為全球暖化而被消滅掉 。
and you know how coral are very sensitive to temperature , and are very important for the biodiversity of the sea .	你知道珊瑚對溫度非常敏感 , 對海洋的生物多樣性也非常重要 。

video: this earth is four and a half billion years old .	影片:地球已經有四十五億年歷史了
these plants , several hundred million years old .	這些植物 , 有好幾億年的歷史 。
and we humans have been walking upright for only 200 thousand years .	而我們人類能直立行走的歷史僅有二十萬年 。
we've managed to adapt , and have conquered the whole planet .	我們已經成功地適應 , 並已經征服了整個地球 。
for generations , we've been raising our children , not unlike millions of other species living beside us .	世代以來 , 我們養育自己的孩子 , 不像在我們身邊的數百萬其他物種那樣生活 。

our life is tied to the wellbeing of our planet .	我們的生命與地球的福祉緊緊相扣 。

fishing , breeding , farming are still the world's foremost human occupations .	漁業、育種、農業 , 仍然是人類最重視的職業 。

we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們都對於地球的天賦同樣的需求 , 希望超越我們自己 , 變得更好 。

in less than 50 years we've altered it more thoroughly than in the entire history of mankind .	在不到50年間 , 我們已經徹底地改變了它 , 勝過了整個人類歷史中 。
half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界上一半的森林已經消失殆盡 。
water resources are running low .	水資源的流失很低 ,
intensive farming is depleting soils .	集約農業正在耗盡土壤 。
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源來源並不永續 ,
the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們正在危害我們自己 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	我們只想改善我們的生活
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但貧富差距越來越大

we know that solutions are available today .	我們知道解決方案在今日都是可行的 。

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在這場tedxboston的演講中 , richardresnick的演講中 , 顯示出將健康照護顛倒過來有多便宜和快速的基因組排序 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、健康照護、科學、科技、
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	richardresnick:歡迎來到基因組革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	女士們先生們 , 我向你們展示人類基因組
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 左上角
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下方則是性染色體
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女性有兩份大的x染色體 ; 男性有一份x染色體 , 當然 , 還有那份小的y染色體 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	對不起男孩 , 但這只是一個小東西 , 會讓你與眾不同 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以 , 如果你放大這個基因組的圖片 , 當然 , 你看到的是這個雙螺旋結構--生命的編碼被拼出 , 裡面有四個生化字母 , 或者我們稱之為基對:a , c , g和t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組中有多少 ? 30億 。
is that a big number ?	這是個很大的數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 大家都可以隨便亂丟 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但實際上 , 如果我把這1280像素點的每一個基對放在800個解析度的螢幕上 , 我們需要3000個螢幕來檢視基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	所以它真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	或許是因為它的大小 , 一群人--順便一提 , 有y染色體的人決定--他們想將它定序 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	所以15年後 , 花了大約40億美元後 , 基因組排序和出版了 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	2003年 , 最終的版本發表 , 他們繼續對它的研究 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這一切都是在一個像這樣的機器上完成的 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	以非常慢的速度 , 每一塊錢是大約一塊錢 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我來這裡告訴你們 , 世界完全改變了 , 你們都不知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	現在我們做的就是把一個基因組複製50份然後把這些複製品切成50基對接著我們將它們排序 , 大量平行排列
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	接著 , 我們把它帶入軟體中 , 重新組合 , 告訴大家這個故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	給大家看看這個樣子人類基因組計劃中的3gb , 對 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	一周內有2000億位元組 ,
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	今年夏天將會改變到6000毫無跡象地減速
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以一個基對的價格 , 一個基對排序的價格已經下跌了一億倍
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	等同於你在1998年用氣體填充燃料等到2011年現在你可以開車去木星兩次
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口 , 電腦容量 , 所有醫學文獻的存檔 , 摩爾定律 , 古老的排序方法 , 這裡有所有的新東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是對數尺度 , 你通常不會看到這樣向上走的線條 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以全球大量排序人類基因組的能力在今年大約是五萬到十萬個人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	我們根據被放置的機器知道這點 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	這預計會在可預見的未來每年增加一倍、三倍 , 或四倍 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 有一間實驗室 , 代表了所有能力的20% 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	叫做北京基因組學院 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	順道一提 , 中國在對抗新的月球上絕對是贏家 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學又有什麼意義 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	所以一個女人37歲了
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她患有階段二的雌激素受體性乳癌 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受了手術 , 化療和放射線治療
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後她又患上c階段3的卵巢癌
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次接受手術和化療
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後 , 她42歲時再度罹患卵巢癌 , 更多化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她又患上了急性骨髓性白血病 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她進入呼吸衰竭 , 8天後死去 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這個婦女接受的治療 , 在短短的十年內 , 看起來就像是放血一樣 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	而是因為我的同事rickwilson在華盛頓大學基因研究院工作的同事rickwilson決定看看這個女人的遺體
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他拿了皮膚細胞定序 , 健康的皮膚 , 癌症的骨髓基因序列 , 幾週後他把兩人的基因組排序 , 沒什麼大不了的 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	接著 , 他在軟體中比較這兩組基因組 , 他發現 , 在其他東西當中 , 有一組兩千個鹼基 , 涵蓋了三十億個鹼基 , 一個叫做tp53的基因組 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你有這種基因上的不振動 , 你生命中有90%的可能性會罹患癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	不幸的是 , 這對這位女士沒有任何幫助 , 但這對她來說確實有很大的影響 , 這對她的家人也有很深刻的影響 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果他們有相同的突變基因 , 然後他們得到這個基因檢測 , 然後他們就可以去定期的檢測 , 及早發現癌症 , 可能可以過上明顯更長的壽命 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	讓我來為大家介紹beery雙胞胎 , 在2歲時被診斷出腦性麻痺 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的母親是一位非常勇敢的女子 , 她不相信這些症狀的出現不符合 , 透過一些英勇的努力和大量的網路搜尋 , 她能夠說服醫學界相信他們其實還有別的東西 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們有分離式肌張力不全症
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們得到了左旋多巴 , 他們的症狀的確改善了 , 但他們並沒有完全症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	結果 , 這張照片上的那位先生是joebeery , 他很幸運成為一家叫做生命科技的公司 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	它們是兩家製造大量全基因組測序工具的公司之一 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	他的做法是 , 讓他的孩子接受定序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現一個基因有一系列突變 , 叫做spr , 負責產生血清素 , 和其他的東西 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以在左旋多巴的基礎上 , 他們給這些孩子使用血清素前導引藥物 , 現在他們很正常 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	如果沒有全基因組定序 , 這件事就永遠不會發生 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	而在幾年前--這需要10萬美元
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	今天的價格是一萬美元 。 下一年是一千美元 。
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	用100元的年份 , 捐贈或花上一年 。
that's how fast this is moving .	這是進展的速度 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	像蝙蝠俠和水槍 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	最後 , 尼克來到兒童醫院 , 帶著這種遙遠的肚子 , 就像個饑荒的受害者 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	他不是在吃東西 , 而是在吃東西的時候 , 他的腸子基本上會打開 , 糞便向外噴出到他的腸子中 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	所以一百多次手術之後 , 他看著他的媽媽說: 「 媽 , 請祈禱 。 我承受太多痛苦了 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的兒童科醫師恰巧有臨床遺傳學的背景他完全不知道發生什麼事但他說 " 讓我們把這個孩子的基因組定序好 "
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	而他們發現一個控制細胞死亡的基因突變
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	所以 , 理論上來說 , 他對食物的產出有一些免疫反應 , 這是自然的反應 , 造成一些程序性的細胞死亡 。
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但是管控下降的基因卻出了問題 。
and so this informs , among other things , of course , a treatment for bone marrow transplant , which he undertakes .	所以 , 這告訴我們 , 當然還有治療骨髓移植的病人 , 他也接受了治療 。
and after nine months of grueling recovery , he's now eating steak with a1 sauce .	經過九個月的努力復原 , 他現在用a1醬汁在吃牛排 。
the prospect of using the genome as a universal diagnostic is upon us today .	今天使用基因組來作為普遍診斷的前景已經來到我們身邊 。

so it turns out that the very same technology is also being used to grow new lines of corn , wheat , soybean and other crops that are highly tolerant of drought , of flood , of pests and pesticides .	所以 , 結果發現 , 同樣的技術也被用來種植新的玉米、小麥、大豆 , 及其他能夠容忍乾旱、洪水、害蟲、殺蟲劑 。
now look , as long as we continue to increase the population , we're going to have to continue to grow and eat genetically modified foods , and that's the only position that i'll take today .	現在 , 看 , 只要我們繼續增加人口我們將不得不繼續增長和食用基因改造食物這是我今天要唯一的選擇

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	丹尼爾克拉夫特展示了他骨髓採取的一種新裝置 , 很快採用拯救生命的骨髓 , 將其減輕到捐贈者身上 。 他強調 , 在骨髓中發現的成人幹細胞 , 可以被用來治療許多條件 , 從帕金森氏症到心臟病 。
biology , biotech , health , health care , medicine , science , technology	生物學、生物科技、健康照護醫學、科學、科技
daniel kraft invents a better way to harvest bone marrow	danielkraft發明了一個更好的方法來採集骨髓 。
so i am a pediatric cancer doctor and stemcell researcher at stanford university where my clinical focus has been bone marrow transplantation .	我是一個小兒科癌病醫師 , 也是史丹佛大學研究幹細胞 , 我的臨床研究專注是骨髓移植 。
now , inspired by jill bolte taylor last year , i didn't bring a human brain , but i did bring a liter of bone marrow .	去年我受到jillboltetaylor的啟發 , 我沒有帶一個人的大腦 , 但我確實帶了一公升的骨髓 。
and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	而骨髓其實就是我們用來拯救數萬名病患的生命 , 其中大部份患有較為先進的惡性腫瘤 , 例如白血病和淋巴瘤 , 還有一些其他的疾病 。
so , a few years ago , i'm doing my transplant fellowship at stanford .	所以 , 幾年前 , 我在史丹佛做移植手術 。
i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室 。 我們這裡有bob , bob , 她是志願捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他的骨髓送到全國各地 , 拯救出患白血病的孩子 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以實際上 , 我們要如何收成這塊骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一整個歐盟團隊、麻醉醫師、護士 , 還有另一位醫生從我身邊看過 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	bob躺在桌上 , 然後我們拿起這根小針 , 你知道的 , 不會太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	基本上 , 我們採用的方法是 , 將它穿過軟組織 , 將它射入硬骨 , 插入tuchus , 每次用針筒吸出約10毫升骨髓 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	然後把它交給護士 。 她將它注射到一個錫 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把它交還給我 。 我們一次又一次地這樣做 。
about 200 times usually .	大約二百次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	到最後 , 我的手臂酸痛 , 手掌一通電話 , 更不用說bob了 , 他的尾端看起來更像這樣 , 像瑞士起士 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道的 , 這手術40年來並沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	這樣做可能有更好的辦法
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想到一種微創的方法 , 一種新裝置 , 我們稱之為 「 骨髓採取器 」 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	而骨髓採取器 , 這裡顯示的
our standard seethrough patient .	我們這名 「 看破 」 的病人
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	我們不是一次性地進入到臀部前或臀部後面
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有一個柔軟、有動力的導管 , 用特殊的電線圈套 , 固定在骨髓內部 , 然後跟著臀部的輪廓移動 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以它讓你能非常快速的志向 , 或吸乾 , 富有的骨髓 , 非常迅速地通過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以多次通過同一個入口
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快地 , bob只要刺穿一個卡片 , 局部麻醉 , 就可以當門診病人 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了幾個原型 , 在史丹佛得到一筆小額獎金 。
and played around with this a little bit .	這玩意兒和其他玩意兒 。
and our team members developed this technology .	而我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們有了兩隻大型動物還有豬的研究
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	令我們驚訝的是 , 我們不只得到了骨髓 , 而且我們還從骨髓採取了十倍的幹細胞活動 , 相較於正常的裝置 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置在去年剛被美國食品藥物管理局批准
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這裡有一個活的病人 。 你可以看見它隨著有彈性的曲線到處跑 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	這裡有兩次通過 , 在同一個病人 , 同一個地點 , 同一個洞 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在局部麻醉下進行的 , 作為一個門診病人 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	同樣的 , 我們取得的幹細胞數目是同一個病人的標準方式的三到六倍 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	所以 , 你為什麼要在乎呢 ? 骨髓是非常豐富的成體幹細胞 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力 , 但還未進入臨床試驗階段 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人幹細胞遍佈我們身體各處 , 包含在骨髓內的血型幹細胞 , 我們採用的是一種幹細胞療法 , 已經超過40年之久 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去十年 , 骨髓幹細胞被大量使用 , 用來治療病人的其他疾病 , 如心臟病、血管疾病、組織工程、甚至神經系統 , 來治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛走出來 , 今年我們正在商業化 , 第二代的骨髓採取器 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望能得到更多幹細胞 , 轉化成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	可能會鼓勵更多人登記 , 成為能拯救生命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	甚至可能讓你可以去掌握你自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 當你年紀越來越小 , 健康的使用 , 在未來你應該需要它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最終這張照片是我們骨髓移植的倖存者 , 他們每年會在史丹佛聚會進行一次聚會 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術可以讓我們在未來有更多這樣的存活者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪者garretlissi提出了一個爭議性的新宇宙模型只能解答所有的大問題 。 如果沒有其他 , 它是你見過最美麗的基礎粒子與力的8度空間模型 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、技術等 ,
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	garrettlisi在他所有的理論上
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 , 老兄 。 看看那些殺手方程式 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	其實 , 在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我會盡我所能 , 去描述微粒物理學的美妙 , 而不用方程式 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	事實證明 , 從珊瑚身上我們能學到很多 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗且不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每個珊瑚都由成千上萬的珊瑚組成 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些珊瑚會持續發芽 , 分裂成基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這樣做是超級聰明的珊瑚 , 我們就能單獨挑出其中的一個人 , 問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問 , 他到底是如何在與鄰居相比 , 如果只是機會 , 或著是命運 , 或者是什麽 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	在我們表達過把溫度調高之後 , 他會告訴我們我們的問題很蠢 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可以算是相當大的意思 , 你看 , 我衝浪時的疤痕是要證明這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這珊瑚會繼續跟我們說他的鄰居也很明顯地跟他一模一樣
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也在這些其他地點 , 但卻體驗到他們是不同的個體 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分支出不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	和我們不同的是 , 超聰明的珊瑚將會有獨特的準備 , 來了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學非常準確地描述我們的宇宙如何運作 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實是不斷地分支出不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	對我們人類來說 , 將心靈包裹起來是一件很奇怪的事 , 因為我們只能經歷一種可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子力學的奇特現象最早是由薛丁格和他的貓提出來的 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓更喜歡這個版本
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	通過量子力學原理 , 薛丁格待在一個有放射物質的箱子裡 , 通過量子力學的法則 , 分支進入一個為輻射狀態 , 一個沒有放射性的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	樣本會散發出去 , 會引發一連串反應 , 釋放毒藥和薛丁格必死無疑 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實的另一個分支 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	這些真實被各自獨立的體驗 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	另一種可能看得出來 , 另一種可能不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說很奇怪 , 因為我們每個人都只能體驗個別的存在 , 而看不到其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	這就好像我們每個人 , 像薛丁格一樣 , 是一種珊瑚分支 , 分為不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們這就是微小世界的運作方式 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	可以用一句話來總結:所有可能發生的事 , 做 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不表示所有事情都會發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	其餘的物理原理就是描述什麼可以發生 , 什麼不可以 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們一切都可歸結到幾何學以及基本粒子的相互作用
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	只有在這些互動是完美平衡前 , 事情才有可能發生 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我將講述我們對這些粒子的認知 , 它們是什麼以及這個平衡如何運作 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中 , 質子和反質子都被加速到接近光速的距離 , 並在碰撞中聚集在一起 , 產生出一股單純的能量 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量會立即轉換成亞原子粒子的噴射 , 使用偵測器和電腦來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這台巨大的機器 , 位於日內瓦的歐洲核子研究中心的大型強子對撞機周長有17英里 。 當它運作的時候 , 所產生的能量是蒙特雷全市的5倍 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法精確的預測哪些粒子會在每次對撞中產生
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性都已被實現 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理學告訴我們有哪些粒子可以產生
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子的質量和能量必須與質子和反質子相同 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何比這個能量極限更大的粒子都沒被產生出來 , 且對我們來說仍然是看不見的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這個新型粒子加速器如此興奮的原因 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	能量極限將超出先前的7倍所以很快我們將看到新的粒子
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談我們可能看到什麼之前 , 先讓我描述一下我們已知的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	亞原子粒子的整個動物園
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部分人都很熟悉電子 。
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在場的很多人都過得很好的生活把他們推來推去
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也是一個中立的夥伴叫做中子不帶電且帶有極小的質量
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相對的 , 上下的夸克有很大的質量 , 三者結合在一起 , 形成原子裡面的質子和中子 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	這些物質粒子來到左旋和右旋的品種 , 並且有攜帶相反電荷的反粒子夥伴 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子還有我們不太熟悉的第二代和第三代電量和第一代相同但質量更高
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子都會和各種力量粒子產生交互作用 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力通過光子 , 與帶電的物質相互作用
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	另外還有一種非常微弱的力量叫做弱作用力它只會和左撇子物質相互作用
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克這種強力帶來不同種類的載荷稱為色荷分三種紅綠藍
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪murraygell-mann因為這些名字是他的錯
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後是重力通過質量和旋轉與物質相互作用
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是每一種力都各有不同種類的載荷
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種力根據各自粒子所攜帶的載荷和物質相互作用
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個還沒被發現的粒子但我們很確定它存在就是希格斯粒子它給予所有其他粒子質量
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是觀察希格斯粒子我們幾乎確定它會發生
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最大的謎團在於我們還能看到什麼 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	我將向你們展示一種美麗的可能性正是這場演講的結尾 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們用不同的自旋和載荷計算所有這些粒子 , 總共有226種 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	那是很多粒子來追蹤
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	大自然會有好多基本粒子 , 這很奇怪 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們根據它們的載荷把它們畫出來 , 會出現一些美麗的圖案 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的載荷是電荷
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有一個負電荷而夸克擁有1/3的電荷
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以 , 當兩個上夸克和下夸克結合在一起製造出質子時 , 它有一個完全電荷 , 再加一個 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子還有反粒子 , 帶有相反電荷
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現電荷實際上是另外兩種載荷的結合超荷和弱荷
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把超荷和弱荷分開在這個二度載荷空間上畫出粒子的載荷電荷就在這些粒子的垂直方向上
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力通過超荷和弱荷與物質相互作用而形成這個圖案
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這叫做統一的電弱模型於1967年組裝起來
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	原因是 , 我們大多數人只熟悉電荷 , 而不是電荷 , 原因是希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的希格斯粒子質量很大破壞了電弱型式的對稱性
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	通過給弱子較大的質量使弱力變弱
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	由於大量的希格斯粒子在圖中沿著橫向坐標而電磁體的光子仍然不變而且在載荷空間中與電荷相互作用
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力被這種粒子載荷的型式描述在二維空間中
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以把強力沿兩個載荷的方向表示出來然後把載荷用夸克形式沿這些方向畫出來
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四維空間中畫出來然後投影到二維空間以便我們能觀察到
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	無論粒子相互作用 , 自然界在這四個載荷方向上都能保持完美的平衡 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果粒子和反粒子相撞會產生能量四個載荷方向的載荷總量為零
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	在這個時點 , 任何東西都能被創造出來 , 只要它擁有同樣的能量 , 並保有完全的零電荷 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	比如說這個弱子和它的反粒子可以在碰撞中產生
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在更遠的相互作用中載荷必須保持平衡
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	一個弱子可以衰退成一個電子和一個反中微子 , 這三個粒子的總載荷仍然是零 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些電荷的型式不僅漂亮
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	它們告訴我們什麼樣的互動是允許發生的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四度空間中旋轉載荷空間 , 看看強相互作用 , 它有很好的對稱性 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強相互作用中強力粒子比如這個粒子和有色夸克相互作用比如這個綠色的夸克讓夸克帶上不同的色荷這個紅色
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強相互作用每秒鐘會在我們身體的每個原子裏發生上百萬次使原子核互相作用
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但對應三種力量的這四種載荷並非故事的終點 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還可以把兩個載荷對應到重力場 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	納入時 , 每個物質粒子有兩種不同的旋轉載荷、旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以它們都會分開 , 在六度載荷空間中給一個不錯的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中旋轉這個圖案 , 看出它是相當漂亮的 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	目前 , 這個圖案與我們目前所知的大自然在這些基本粒子的微小尺度下是如何建造的 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們所知的確定 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	其中的一些粒子在實驗中能到達的極限
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個圖案 , 我們已經知道這些微小尺度的粒子物理了 。 宇宙用這些微小尺度運作的方式是非常美麗的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要來談談關於我們還不知道的事物的一些新舊想法 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要把這個圖案只用數學方法來拓展 , 看能不能把我們的手放到整個enchida上 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們希望找到構成我們宇宙的所有粒子和力量
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想用這張圖片預測新的粒子 , 當實驗達到高能階時 , 我們將會看到 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	所以在粒子物理學上有這樣一個古老的概念就是這個已知的載荷圖案不對稱的圖案可以從一個更完美的圖案中得到突破就像希格斯粒子如何突破心電圖案賦予電磁作用
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了達成這個目的 , 我們需要引進新的載荷方向的新的力量 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們導入一個新方向時 , 我們要猜測在這個方向上粒子帶有什麼樣的載荷 , 接著再讓它和其他粒子一起旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果猜對的話我們就可以在六度載荷空間中構建標準載荷集作為更完美的七度載荷空間圖案的毀壞對稱
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這個特別的選擇是1973年由帕蒂和薩拉姆介紹的一個大統一理論 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看到這個新的統一模式時 , 我們可以看到一些粒子似乎遺失的空隙 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這是統一理論運作的方式 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	一個物理學家將已有的結構作為子集來找尋更大更對稱的型態
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的圖案可以讓我們預測從未見過的粒子存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這個統一模型預測出了這兩種新力粒子的存在 , 它應該有很大的作用力 , 就像弱力 , 只是比較弱 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以在七度空間中旋轉這組載荷而且考慮一下關於粒子的奇怪事實:在六度載荷空間中物質的第二代和第三代擁有和第一代物質在六度載荷空間中相同的載荷
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並非獨特的六種載荷
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	在標準載荷空間上彼此坐著
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間裡工作就可以對應每個粒子都有獨特的新載荷
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	然後在八度空間中旋轉看看整體的樣子
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	這裡我們可以看到物質的第二代和第三代 , 現在通過一種叫 " 三重性 " 對稱和第一代相關聯 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	在八度中的這個特殊的載荷圖案是數學中最為漂亮的幾何結構之一
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	是最大的例外型李群e8的圖案
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言小組是個平滑、彎曲的形狀 , 由248維度組成 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	這個圖案的每一點都對應到這個極其複雜而美麗的形狀的對稱性 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	e8中的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論的彎曲時空解釋重力
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	與量子力學一起 , 這個形狀的幾何學可以描述宇宙是如何在最小的尺度下運作的 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	在八度載荷空間中這個形狀的型式非常美麗 , 它總結成千上萬種這些基本粒子之間的可能互動 , 每一個都只是這個複雜形狀的一個平面 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們轉動它時 , 我們可以看到其中許多錯綜複雜的圖案 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	通過某種旋轉我們可以在八度空間沿一個對稱軸方向觀察這個圖案並且一次看盡所有粒子
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	這是個非常漂亮的物體 , 如同任何統一物體 , 我們可以看到某些孔洞 , 在那裡 , 新粒子會被這個圖案所需要 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	在這有20個空格需要新粒子來填補其中兩個已有帕蒂薩拉姆粒子填補
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從圖案中的位置我們知道這些新的粒子應該是稀少的像希格斯粒子一樣但有顏色載荷而且和強力相互作用
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填入這些新粒子使這個圖案完整讓我們得到完整的e8
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8圖案有著深厚的數學根基 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被許多人認為是數學中最漂亮的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這是個很棒的前景這個偉大數學美的物體可以用最小的尺度來描述粒子相互作用的真相
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	而這個用數學來描述大自然的概念一點也不新 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	1623年伽利略寫道: 「 大自然的宏偉書 , 代表著不斷地向我們敞開的注視 , 是用數學的語言寫的 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形 , 圓形和其他幾何形狀 , 沒有這些形狀 , 人類無法理解它的單字 ; 沒有這些 , 一個在黑暗的迷宮中徘徊 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我曾嘗試按照伽利略的指導只用三角形圓形和其他的幾何形狀去描述粒子物理的數學性 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當其他物理學家和我開始研究這東西時數學就像一個黑暗的迷宮
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但可以放心 , 在這數學的核心是純粹美麗的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	加入到量子力學中 , 這個數學將我們的宇宙描述為一個在成長的e8珊瑚 , 粒子在每個可能的位置依據一個美麗的圖案來相互作用 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	使用大型強子對撞機之類的新型機器時 , 我們也許可以看出自然是不是使用e8圖案 , 還是種不一樣的 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個探索過程是一個奇妙的探險
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果對撞機發現了符合e8圖案的粒子那就太酷了
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果對撞機發現了新的粒子但不符合這個圖案那會非常有趣但對e8理論不利
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我個人也不好 。
now how bad would that be ?	那到底有多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 相當糟糕 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但預測大自然如何運作是很冒險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其他類似的理論都是在拍照時
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個人確實做了很多努力 , 知道這些想法大多可能最後都不會成立 , 不符合大自然的形象 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理就是這樣子的:有很大量的擦傷 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新的物理理論跟新創公司很像 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	如同任何大型投資 , 當失敗時 , 要在情感上無法棄置一連串的研究 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學界 , 如果某樣東西不行 , 你得要丟掉它 , 再試試別的 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	現在 , 在這種不確定中 , 唯一能夠保持理智並獲得幸福的方法就是在生活中保持平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我已經竭盡所能去過平衡人生 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著在物理愛情和衝浪中尋找平衡我三個載荷方向
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這麼一來 , 即使我所工作的物理也沒有任何作用 , 我仍然知道我過得很好 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	而我試著住在美麗的地方 ,
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十年我大部分時間都住在毛伊島一個非常美麗的地方
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	這對我父母來說 , 這是宇宙中最大的謎題之一 , 我是怎麼能夠一直活下來的 , 卻沒有參與任何和全職工作類似的事物 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我將要讓你進入這個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在毛伊島上的家庭辦公室的景象
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能已經注意到 , 這些美麗的觀點都很相似 , 但在稍微不同的地方 ,
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為這曾經是我在毛伊島的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了一種非常不尋常的生活 ,
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不擔心房租讓我把時間花在自己喜歡做的事情上
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	流浪的生活有時是很艱難的 , 但這讓我能生活在美麗的地方 , 在我的生活中保持平衡 , 這讓我很開心 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	讓我可以花很多時間和超級聰明的珊瑚在一起
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級聰明的人的公司
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	所以我很高興能被邀請來到ted 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我可能理解其中百分之二的部分 , 但是我還是很喜歡 。 所以我要聽起來很傻 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你的萬物理論我很習慣用珊瑚
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克:是的 。 它讓幾個人至少感到興奮的原因是因為 , 如果你正確的話 , 它會把重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以 , 你是不是說 , 我們應該把宇宙想成 , 最小的宇宙 , 有可能有e8的物體 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 在最小的尺度下 , 還是...
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	高爾:我剛給你們看的圖案是對應我們所知的基本粒子物理而且已經對應到一個非常美麗的形狀
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	這也是我說的我們能肯定知道
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	而那個形狀和e8的圖形有著驚人的相似處 , 而它符合e8圖案的途徑 , 可能是其餘的照片 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我為你們展示的這些點狀圖案實際上代表著高維物體的對稱性這些圖案在我們經歷的時空中 , 會扭曲、移動、跳舞
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這就說明了我們看到的所有基本粒子
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克:但是弦理論家 , 在我理解它的同時 , 用比較小的弦來解釋電子 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論的震動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該如何看待e8模型的電子
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	不 , 它會是這個e8形狀的對稱之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 當這個形狀在跨越時空移動時它會扭曲 。 當它移動時它扭曲的方向就是我們看到的粒子是什麼 。 所以它會是克里斯:e8形狀的大小 , 它跟電子有什麼關係 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	它變大了嗎 ? 變小了嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	格林:就我們所知 , 電子是尖端粒子 , 所以 , 這會是最小的尺度 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以在量子場理論中 , 這些東西的解釋方式是所有的可能性都同時展開發展
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這也是我為什麼拿珊瑚作比喻 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	這樣說來 , e8進入的方式將是一個可以在時空中任意連結的形狀
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	如我所說的形狀在經過這個彎曲的表面時會扭曲的方向就是基本粒子本身
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	所以通過量子場理論 , 它們將自己呈現為點 , 以此方式互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道能不能再說得更清楚 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克:這真的不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它喚起了一種驚奇感 , 我肯定想了解更多這種感覺 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但是非常謝謝你們的到來 。 這太棒了 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳奇性的黑猩猩研究者珍.古德爾談到坦尚尼爾和她的其他社區計畫 , 協助非洲大鎮和受到威脅的動物並肩生活在一起 。
