jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍古德幫助人類和動物住在一起
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 隨便什麼
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以去 , 嗯 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 !
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這是黑猩猩的叫聲 , 他們晚上要去睡覺前 ,
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到它從山谷的一端傳到另一端 , 從這一端傳到下一區 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	我今天晚上要從zeray昨天離開的地方 , 挑起我的演講 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他談到這個神奇的三歲小孩 , selam
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也曾聽說過透過dna遺傳資料 , 人類的歷史、族譜 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	這是一位古生物學家 , 最近的路易斯.李奇 , 他讓我走上研究黑猩猩之路 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	在以前那段時間真是不尋常 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	現在已經算是常見的狀況了 , 但他的論點是 , 因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	各位可以從化石中得到許多訊息 , 看出那些人的長相 , 看出肌肉附著的形狀 , 看出他們如何和他們一起生活 , 來自各式各樣的人造物 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但他們的行為呢 ? 這是他想知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為也不能化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張-現在已經是相當常見的理論了如果我們發現行為模式在我們現存最接近的近親人猿身上或與今日的人類相似的行為模式 , 那麼也許這些行為會出現在七百萬年前人類祖先身上
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們從那古老、古老的過去 , 帶來了那些特徵 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你看今天的教科書處理人類進化的過程 , 你經常會發現人們依據黑猩猩的行為來推測早期人類的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	牠們跟我們很像比其他生物都多 , 在這次ted大會中我們也聽說過 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以這對我來說還是要評論黑猩猩在某些方面是如此地與我們相似
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每一隻黑猩猩都有他或者她自己的個性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我會給牠們取名字 。 牠們可以活到六十年以上 。 雖然我們認為大部份的牠們在野外應該不會活到六十歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	wurzel先生 。 母羊在十一或十二歲時就生了她的第一個寶 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那裡 , 她只有五到六年期間有一位嬰兒 , 在孩童哺育期時 , 有一段很長的童年依賴期 , 晚上和母親同睡 , 騎在背上 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信這段長時間的孩童對黑猩猩很重要 , 就像對我們來說一樣 , 對學習也是一樣 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在不同形式的動物進化時期變得更加複雜所以我們發現到學習在個體的生命史中扮演著一個更重要的角色
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩會花很多時間觀察長者會做的事 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道他們有能力模仿他們看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 正是這樣 , 不同使用工具的行為 , 如今在非洲各地研究不同的黑猩猩族群 , 如何透過觀察、模仿與實踐 , 來將這些使用工具的行為描述成原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口語語言 , 我們已經談過了
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	牠們的確有非常豐富的姿勢和姿勢 , 其中有許多是類似的 , 甚至跟我們有一模一樣的 , 在同樣的情境下成形 。 要迎接擁抱的就是黑猩猩 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	他們也會親吻、牽手、拍另一個背 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	它們會大搖大擺 , 會扔石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩的社會中 , 我們發現了很多很多關於同情心、同情心的前導者 , 以及真正的利他行為 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 它們和我們一樣 , 也有天性黑暗的一面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	它們有極度的殘酷 , 甚至一種原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些非常有侵略性的行為 , 大多數來說 , 都是針對鄰近的社會群體 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	他們非常地有侵略性 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	我相信黑猩猩們 , 比起其它的生物 , 已經幫助我們了解到 , 畢竟 , 人類與動物王國之間並沒有一條明顯的界線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這是一條非常模糊的線 , 當我們做更多的觀察時它變得更加的模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我在1960年開始進行的研究至今仍持續到今天 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	而這些生活在野外的複雜社會生活的黑猩猩們 , 幫助我們認識到 , 我們是其中的一份子 , 而非分開 , 那些與我們共享地球的令人驚嘆的動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 和世界上許多其他生物一樣 , 發現黑猩猩也蠻可悲的 , 正在喪失牠們的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是一張從空中拍攝的照片 , 它呈現出岡貝的森林高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	那是我十六年前飛越整個區域時 , 發現這片森林在公園之外 , 在1960年時 , 這個森林幾乎沒有碎裂痕 , 沿著坦尚尼卡湖的東岸 , 也是30平方英里的岡貝國家公園所在之處 , 有一個問題出現在我的腦海中 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	" 我們怎麼能試著拯救這些知名的黑猩猩 , 當居住在國家公園附近的人民正為了生存而苦苦掙扎時 ? "
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	比起那片土地能支援的更多人居住在那裡 ,
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	被從蒲隆地湧入的難民數增加 , 及來自剛果的湖覆蓋 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	和其他地方買不起的窮人 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了一個計劃 , 我們稱之為坦尚尼亞.
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	這是個很全面的方法 , 來改善在公園附近村莊的人們的生活 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	它從小在12個村莊開始 , 現在已經24歲了 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間深入討論 , 但它包含了像是樹木哺育計畫 , 農業最適合這種方法現在已經非常退化 , 幾乎是沙漠般的土地 , 就在這些山上 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制的方法 , 預防土壤流失
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	收回過度使用的農地讓兩年內能再度生產
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	協助村民們從井裡取得淡水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	也許建造一些學校 。
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的 , 我相信 , 是要和一小群婦女合作 , 提供她們微額貸款的機會 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	如同全世界的情況那樣 , 95%的貸款都回報了 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	授權女性、和教育工作 , 提供獎學金給女孩子 , 讓他們能完成中學 , 能清楚了解 , 在全世界 , 女性教育能改善 , 家庭規模也會下降 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	提供家庭規劃與愛滋病的相關資訊
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	這個計畫的成果 , 是發生在保育上的事 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育正在發生的是 , 在這24個村莊的農夫 , 與其視我們為一群白種人來研究一大群猴子 , 順帶一提 , 很多工作人員現在是坦桑尼亞人 , 但當我們開始坦桑尼亞造林計劃時 , 那是一個坦桑尼亞人入鄉的團隊 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是一個坦桑尼亞的團隊 , 和村民對話 , 問他們對什麼有興趣 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育感興趣嗎 ? 絕對不是 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 ; 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間過去 , 他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始更了解保育的需求 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始明白當山的高層都被樹木破壞 , 所以你得到這可怕的土壤流失和土石流 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	今天 , 我們正在發展一個叫做岡貝生態系統的東西 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這個區域遠離國家公園的範圍 , 向這些非常墮落的土地向外延伸 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村落擁有更好的生活標準時 , 他們其實同意將百分之十到二十的高地邊緣的土地放到一邊 , 如此一來 , 隨著樹木再長回來 , 黑猩猩們就會擁有帶狀走廊去旅行在國家公園外面與其它殘存的團體進行基因活動 。
so tacare is a success .	所以坦尚未成功 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們也在非洲的其他區域複製 , 在其他荒野上面對極端人口壓力的區域 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 非洲的問題 , 如同我們這前幾天在ted討論過的 , 都是重大問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	貧窮的問題很嚴重 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你有大量居住的土地時 , 並不是那麼肥沃 , 特別是當你砍掉樹木 , 離開土壤 , 進入侵蝕風化 , 絕望的人口砍掉越來越多的樹木 , 如此一來他們就能試著種植食物給自己和家人 , 會發生什麼事 ? 一定要捐出些什麼 。
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	而另外的問題 , 不僅是非洲 , 其他國家的發展中國家也確實如此 , 不管我們對我們的地球做什麼 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道的 , 著名的科學家 , 愛德華.威爾森曾說過 , 如果地球上的每個人都生活的水準 , 平均歐洲或美國人 , 我們需要三個新的星球 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們說四個 。 但是我們沒有 。 我們有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	發生了什麼事呢 ? 我的意思是 , 這裡的問題可以說是這裡我們有最聰明的生物 , 可以說是有史以來走行地球的 , 擁有這非凡的大腦 , 可以用這些ted會議來說明 , 但是我們卻毀掉了我們唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	全世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做出重大決定之前 , 習慣了身邊坐下來問自己: 「 這個決定是如何影響我們前七代子孫的 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	現今 , 重大的決定 , 在這裡我並不是特別談非洲 , 而是世界上已開發國家的重大決策 , 涉及數百萬美元 , 數百萬人 , 通常都基於 「 這會如何影響下一次的股東會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	而這些決定會影響非洲
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲各地旅行 , 談論黑猩猩面臨的問題 , 以及他們消失的森林 , 我發現越來越多非洲的問題能夠擺在先前的殖民地開採之門 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始在非洲之外旅行 , 到歐洲演說 , 在美國演說 , 到亞洲 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	不論在哪裡 , 都會遇到這些糟糕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	你們也知道我說的那種 , 我指的是污染 ,
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們所呼吸的空氣毒害著我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水資源 , 也許是本世紀最關鍵的議題之一 , 不論何時水都是被污染的 , 包括農業、工業、家庭使用的化學物質 , 這些化學物質 , 還在全世界被噴灑出來 , 似乎是對於過去的經驗無法獲利 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林被砍伐 ; 海嘯之類的影響變差 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們談過土壤流失 ,
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們有輕率的燃燒石化燃料 , 同時也有其他溫室氣體 , 稱為 「 導致氣候變化 」 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 世界各地都有人開始相信 , 我們的氣候出了問題 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	全世界的氣候都混雜在一起 ,
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	而且是受到更差影響的窮人 。
it's africa that already is affected .	是非洲已經受影響 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南的非洲許多地區 , 乾旱的情況更加嚴重 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當下雨真的來了 , 通常會造成洪水和苦惱 , 還有貧窮、飢餓及疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	而居住在陸地上無法支援的人們 , 卻因為太貧窮而無法購買食物 , 無法搬走 , 因為整片土地都惡化了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以你會看到沙漠化 , 爬行 , 爬行最後一棵樹 , 被砍伐 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這種事不只發生在非洲 , 全世界都有
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 我並不驚訝 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇到了好多失去希望的年輕人 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 失去了原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為這種非比尋常的聰明的大腦之間有某種聯繫 , 這種ted科技所表現出的聰明才智 , 而人類的心 , 是嗎 ? 以非科學的角度來討論這件事 , 從愛和同情的角度來看 , 是不是有某種聯繫 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	而這些年輕人 , 當我跟他們說話時 , 基本上他們是那樣的沮喪或者是冷漠的 , 或痛苦的或是生氣的 , 他們或多或少都說了同樣的話 , 「 我們會這樣想 , 因為我們覺得你已經在消費我們的未來了 , 而我們卻無能為力 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經危及了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每次我看著他們 , 想著我們從我小時候就如何傷害這個美麗的星球 , 我就感受到這種絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這也促成了我們所謂的根與芽計畫 , 開始於坦尚尼亞而現在也擴及全世界97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	這是象徵性的 。 根是堅定的基礎 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	芽看起來似乎很微小 , 接近陽光-它們可以穿過磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆視為地球上所有我們面臨的問題 , 環境和社會問題 。 這是關於希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	世界各地成千上萬的年輕人能突破這些困擾 , 讓所有生物的世界變得更美好 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根與芽想傳遞的最重要的訊息是:我們每一個人 , 每一天都有所不同 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有選擇 。 在座的每一位 , 我們都能選擇我們想要做出什麼樣的改變 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	非常貧窮的人別無選擇 。 這要由我們來改變事物 , 讓貧窮的人也能選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根與芽計畫團體們選出三個項目 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	這取決於他們年紀多大 , 及哪個國家不論在城市或鄉村 , 都取決於他們在什麼樣的專案計畫 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們現在有從幼稚園到大學的計畫 , 有越來越多的成人在他們自己的根與芽團隊中工作 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	每個小組都能選擇 , 在他們之間 , 有三種不同的專案計畫 , 來讓這個世界更美好 , 了解到這些不同的問題是緊密相連的 , 互相衝突的 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	所以 , 他們的其中一個計畫就是協助他們自己的社區 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	然後 , 如果他們能夠的話 , 他們可能會為了幫助世界上其它地方的社區而募款 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	他們的其中一個計畫是幫助動物不僅是野生動物也包括家畜類的動物
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	他們的其中一個計畫將是幫助這個我們所共享的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	而把這些編織在一起就是一個訊息:學習在我們自己、在我們的家庭、在我們的社區、在國家之間、在文化之間、宗教之間、還有在我們與自然界間共存 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然界 。 我們不能以我們本身的速度繼續破壞它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們的地球不只一個 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	只要挑選一個或者兩個在非洲的項目 , 那些根與芽的團體正在進行的 , 一兩個或者一兩個項目 , 都在坦桑尼亞、烏干達、肯亞、南非、剛果 , 獅子山共和國、喀麥隆和其他團體 。 如同我說的 , 目前有97個國家在進行 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們種樹 , 種有機蔬菜
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營中工作 , 有雞和雞在賣雞蛋 , 賺了一點錢 , 或只是用來餵飽他們的家人 , 感覺到一種自豪感和賦權感 , 因為他們再也不需要用他們種的蔬菜和雞隻來幫別人 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達上 , 給予一些心理上的幫助 , 給予軍人一些 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	進行這樣子的計畫 , 是讓他們脫離自我 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次 , 他們是社會中很有用的成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們在監獄中也有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 現在根本就沒有時間做更多根與芽 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也在研究愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	那是根與芽很重要的組成部分 , 讓年長的孩子和年輕的孩子說話 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	而且不希望懷孕之類的 , 年輕人會傾聽其它年青人的心聲 , 而不是成人的心聲 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 。 我在世界各地被問到這個問題: 「 珍 , 你看過太多可怕的事 , 你看過你的黑猩猩數量從一百萬隻在世紀末的數量下降 , 到現在不超過十五萬隻 , 其他許多的動物也如此 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失了 , 曾經是森林的沙漠
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? 」 嗯 , 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能來參加ted會議 , 沒有希望 , 可以嗎 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然還有希望 。 其一是這令人驚嘆的人類大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	我的意思是 , 想一想這些科技
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	最後 , 我實在太激動了 , 能到人們面前談論堆肥式的公廁 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	它是我的嗜好之一 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們只是把所有的水沖到馬桶上 , 真的很糟 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	接著談到再生能源極其重要 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們是否關心地球給我們的孩子
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	我們有多少人有小孩 , 或孫子 , 姪子 , 姪子 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們是否關心他們的未來 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們關心他們的未來 , 我們身為這世界上精英份子 , 我們可以為它做點什麼 。 我們可以為我們每天的生活做出選擇 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買些什麼 。 我們穿什麼 。
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	並選擇用這些問題來做選擇 , 這會如何影響我周遭的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	他長大後會如何影響到我孩子的生活 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或我的孫子 , 或其他什麼的 。
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	所以人腦 , 與心相處 , 我們聯手於世界各地 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	這也是ted的幫助 , google幫助我們 , 亦幫助我們 , esri也幫助繪製岡貝國家公園的地圖 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有這些我們能使用的科技
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在我們把它們連結起來 , 開始發生了 , 不是嗎 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	今天下午你們已經聽說過了 。 事情已經開始發生 。
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這樣的改變 , 這樣的改變 。 如果我們關心未來 , 就會看到我們必定的改變 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	而下一個原因 , 讓大自然擁有驚人的恢復力 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以把一個完全被摧毀的區域 , 只要有時間或許還可以幫助它再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	而其中一個例子就是禁忌計劃
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我說過 , 這裡看似已經死了的樹木殘骸 , 如果你停止用石頭砍伐它們 , 這是無需的 , 因為你有木造地 , 然後在五年之內就可以生出一棵30英尺高的樹 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	而動物 , 幾乎在滅絕的邊緣 , 可以有第二次機會 。 這是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	這很鼓舞人心 。 這也帶領我最近一類的希望 , 在過去兩天中我們已經聽過太多這種不屈不撓的人類精神 。 這種人類決心的決心 , 人類精神的恢復力 , 如此一來那些你想被窮困 , 疾病 , 或其他 , 能讓自己從這當中拉上力量 , 有時只要用一隻手 , 並且讓他們成為社會的一份子 , 讓他們成為改變世界的一部分 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	想想那些真正鼓舞人心的非洲人物
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以列出一長串的名單 , 但顯然是納爾遜•曼德拉在十七年的辛苦勞力中浮現出來 , 23年的監禁 , 用這驚人的寬恕 , 讓他國出身種族隔離政權 , 沒有流血打仗 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	在奈及利亞的沙羅維瓦採用了巨大的石油公司 。 雖然全世界的人盡了最大努力 , 但被處決了 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人是如此地鼓舞人心 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人 , 是我們需要年輕非洲人的典範 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	而且我們也需要一些環境的榜樣 , 今天我已經聽到了其中的一些 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	所以 , 我真的很感激這個機會 , 能再次與ted的所有人分享這個訊息 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望我們當中的一些人可以聚在一起討論這些事 , 特別是根與芽的計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	最後我要說的是 , 管理這整個會議中心的年輕女子 , 我今天碰到她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她拿著證書 , 實在是太興奮了 。 她是根與芽成員 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她在daressalaam的領導下
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說這幫她做到她正在做的事情 。
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	這對我來說是非常令人振奮的 , 可以看看年輕人如何當他們被賦予力量時 , 給予他們機會去採取行動 , 讓世界變得更美好 , 真正是我們明天的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家黛安娜柯恩 , 在海洋中和在我們的生活中都有一些關於塑膠污染的艱難事實 , 以及一些關於如何將自己從塑膠垃圾漩渦中解放出來的思想 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色、使命藍、海洋、塑膠等 ,
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	diannacohen:關於塑膠污染的艱難事實
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是一個視覺藝術家 , 我也是塑膠污染聯盟的發起人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我一直在和塑膠袋合作 , 我剪下又縫合起來 , 過去二十年來我做藝術的主要材料 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成二維立體塊 , 雕塑和裝置藝術 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	在大約八年後 , 我開始用塑膠工作 , 我有些作品開始變得裂縫 , 分解成更小的塑膠塊 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 太好了 ,
it's ephemeral just like us . "	和我們一樣 , 它具有短暫的時間 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	一旦對塑膠有了進一步的教育我發現這是件壞事
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	塑膠被分解成小塊的壞東西因為它總是有塑膠
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	而我們發現的是在海洋環境中很多
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	接著 , 在過去幾年 , 我了解到太平洋垃圾帶和垃圾漩渦 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	而我的初始反應──我認為 , 很多人第一次聽到這個反應是: 「 我的天啊 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們得去那裡清理這些東西 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以我真的提出了一個計劃 , 要和一艘貨船一起出去 , 還有兩艘退縮的漁船拖網 , 一座起重機 , 一座磨碎機 , 一台冷模機 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	而我的意圖是 , 出門到垃圾漩渦 , 提高對這個議題的認知 , 開始把塑膠撿起來 , 晶片化成一小塊碎片 , 冷模將它放到磚塊中 , 在未開發的社區中 , 可能被用來建材 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始跟實際去過垃圾漩渦並研究海洋環境裡的塑膠問題接著我發現把塑膠清理乾淨會是非常小的一滴效果相較於全世界每天產生的塑膠我需要回顧並檢視更大的畫面
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更大的情況是:我們得要找到一種方式 , 把水龍頭關掉 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要削減單次使用及丟棄的塑膠 , 這些塑膠每天以全球性的規模進入海洋環境中 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	所以 , 看著這些 , 我也發現我真的很生氣 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我擔心的不只是你試著想像在太平洋中間我學到了 , 有11個塑膠垃圾漩渦可能是全世界五大海洋中的塑膠 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	我關心的不只是這間塑膠垃圾的漩渦而是超市裡塑膠的漩渦
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 所有的食物都是塑膠包裝 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的飲料都是用塑膠包裝的 , 即使是在健康食品市場也一樣 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也很擔心冰箱裡的塑膠還有從塑膠流入我們體內的毒素
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和一群其他的人一起 , 他們都在研究這個議題 , 我們建立了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有許多倡議 , 但有一些是非常基本的 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	其一是:如果我們所發現的海洋中有百分之八十到九十都是塑膠那何不稱它為原本的海洋碎片
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	資源回收 , 每個人的書都是以永續和綠化的方式結尾再利用資源回收的概念 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	你把某個東西放進一個桶子裡 , 不用再想它 。
what is the reality of that ?	這到底是甚麼樣的結果呢 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 塑膠回收的比率不到7%
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你真的仔細觀察 , 尤其是當涉及到塑膠瓶時 , 大部分只會被降級回收 , 或是燒毀 , 或是運到中國去 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它被降低了 , 轉變成更小的東西 , 而玻璃瓶可以再次成為玻璃瓶 , 也可以再次使用一個塑膠瓶 , 永遠不能再用塑膠瓶了 。
so this is a big issue for us .	所以這對我們來說是個大問題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	另一件我們關注並要求人們考慮的事情是把第四個r增加到 " 減少、再利用、回收 " 的r " 上而這就是拒絕
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	任何時候 , 都拒絕使用單次和用過即丟的塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案是存在的 ; 有些是很老派的 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我現在在收集二氧化碳 , 用的是大麻和微軟的容器 , 來將食物存入其中 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我對自己和家人的服務
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	要拿起一個不銹鋼瓶或玻璃瓶是很容易的 , 如果你在旅行中 , 而你卻忘了帶個不銹鋼瓶裝水 , 用水或過濾水 , 與購買塑膠瓶裝水 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我猜我想對在場的各位說的──我知道你們對這個議題有很大的了解──在海洋中 , 這是個很大的問題 , 但身為消費者的我們 , 卻可以解決這個問題 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們能解決這個問題 , 做法是提高對議題的意識 , 並教導大家選擇的替代方案 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 若可能的話 , 要選擇用過的塑膠的替代品 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把這一大堆東西都切成海洋來做這件事 , 拯救我們的海洋、拯救我們的地球、拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	這位在麻省理工學院的pattiemaes的實驗室成員 , 帕納•密特里是ted的頭腦 。 它是一個可穿戴的裝置 , 配上一個投影機 , 為我們環境進行深度互動 。 想像一下 「 關鍵報告 」 , 然後一些 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	示範、設計、界面設計、科技、
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	帕特蒂馬斯和帕納•密絲莫六感的示範 。
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我一直對這個問題很有興趣:我們能否進化或者發展出第六感 。 一種能讓我們無縫接觸並容易獲取信息的感覺 , 用更簡易的方式取得信息 , 或現存的信息 , 來幫助我們做出正確的決定 , 決定我們要面對的是什麼 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	你們有些人可能會爭論 , 嗯 , 不是現在的手機已經有了嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會說不 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted碰到一個人的時候 , 這是最頂尖的網路場所 , 當然 , 那年你不和某人握手然後說: 「 你能不能暫時把手機拿出來用google查詢你 ? 」
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或是當你到超級市場 , 站在那一大排不同的衛生紙 , 你不會拿出手機 , 打開瀏覽器 , 然後到一個網站上 , 試圖決定各種不同的衛生紙中哪一種是最環保的做法 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以 , 我們真的無法很容易取得所有這些相關的資訊 , 這些資訊能夠協助我們做出最佳的決策 , 決定下一步要做什麼 , 以及要採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以我在媒體實驗室的研究小組正在研發一系列的發明 , 讓我們能輕鬆地取得這些資訊 , 並且不需要使用者改變他們的行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我來這裡向各位揭開我們最新的努力目前為止 , 最成功的努力 , 這仍是過程中的一個成果 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	其實我現在穿著這個裝置我們把它和架子外的零件結合在一起......順帶一提 , 這個裝置現在的價格只有350美元
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我戴著一台攝影機 , 只是一個簡單的網路攝影機 , 一個攜帶電池電力的投影系統 , 配備一個小鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些組件會在我的口袋裡跟我的手機溝通 , 這些手機的功能是通信與計算設備 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在這段影片中 , 我們看到我的學生帕納•密絲利 , 他真的是執行和設計這整個系統的天才 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們看到這個系統讓他走到任何平面前 , 用他的雙手開始與他面前投射的資訊進行互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	系統會追蹤這四個重要的手指
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個案例中 , 他戴著你可能認得的簡單的筆蓋 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要比較時髦的版本你也可以把指甲塗上不同顏色
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	攝影機基本上能追蹤這四隻手指並且能辨識出他做的任何手勢 , 舉例來說 , 長灘的地圖 , 放大和縮小等等 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	這個系統還能辨識出具象徵性的手勢 , 例如 「 拍照 」 的動作 , 然後在你面前拍照 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	當他走回媒體實驗室的時候 , 他可以走到任何一面牆前將他拍下的所有照片投影出來 , 整理它們 , 放大 , 等等 , 同樣是使用自然的手勢 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	兩年前你們有些人可能也來過這裡看到傑夫•漢的示範你們有些人可能會想: 「 這不像微軟的平面電腦嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	是的 , 你也用自然的手勢互動 , 雙手等等 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	但差別在於 , 你可以用任何表面 , 你可以走到任何表面上 , 包括你的手 , 如果沒有其他表面可用 , 並與這些投影出來的資料進行互動 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	這裝置是完全可攜帶 , 而且可以是...
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	所以 , 其中一個重要的不同點是它完全是流動的 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另一項更重要的不同點是 , 量產時 , 這種成本不會比今天的手機更高 , 實際上 , 包裝的更大 , 看起來會比我脖子上穿的這個版本更時髦 。
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	除了讓你們其中一些人活出你的幻想之外 , 在《關鍵報告》中 , 湯姆•克魯斯的幻想 。 我們之所以對這個裝置感到很興奮 , 是因為它真的可以成為這六感裝置的其中之一 , 給你關於你面前事物的重要資訊 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	所以我們看到帕納進入超級市場準備購買一些紙手巾 。
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起一樣產品-系統可以辨識出他撿貨的產品 , 用的是影像辨識或是標記技術 , 給他綠燈或橘燈 。
he can ask for additional information .	他可以要求額外的資訊
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	所以 , 基於他個人的標準 , 這個特別的選擇是特別好的 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	有些人可能會想要有最多漂白劑的衛生紙而不是最環保的選擇 。
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿起一本書 , 他能取得亞馬遜書局的評分 , 它會直接投影在書的封面上 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是胡安的書 , 我們之前的講者 , 順帶一提 , 在亞馬遜這個地方得到很棒的評分 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , 帕納翻閱了這本書的頁面 , 可以看到更多關於這本書的資訊--讀者評論 , 可能是他最喜歡的評論家等等--
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他翻到特定的一頁他可以找到我們朋友的註解然後給他一點外顯的資訊關於那一頁的任何東西
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀報紙時 , 它不必過時 。
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你可以收到關於你閱讀到的影片註解可以獲得最新的運動分數等等 。
this is a more controversial one .	這是比較富爭議的一個
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你在ted與某人互動時 , 也許你能看到一團團團的標籤 , 那些與那個人相關的字在他們的部落格和個人網頁裡 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這個案例中 , 學生們對照相機有興趣等等 。
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你前往機場的路上 , 如果你拿起你的登機證 , 它可以告訴你飛機誤點了 , 登機門已更改等等 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	而且 , 如果你需要知道現在的時機是什麼時間 , 就像在你的手臂上畫著手錶一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	研發出第六感能夠讓我們無縫接觸到關於我們可能遇到的事的所有相關資訊 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生帕納 , 像我說的 , 他是這背後的天才 。
he does deserve a lot of applause because i don't think he's slept much in the last three months , actually .	他確實應該得到很多掌聲因為我認為在過去的三個月中他睡的不多
and his girlfriend is probably not very happy about him either .	他的女朋友可能也不太高興他 。
but it's not perfect yet , it's very much a work in progress .	但目前它還不是很完美 , 還只是在進行中的工作 。
and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	誰知道呢 ? 或許再十年我們就會有植入腦內的終極第六感了 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	phyllisrodriguez和aichaelwafi都有一個強大的友誼-是出自於無法想像的損失 。 rodriguez的兒子在世界貿易中心被殺死了 。 2001年9月11日 , 埃爾瓦菲的兒子伊的兒子-zacariasmoussaui在那些攻擊中被判有一個角色 , 並在服刑 。 希望能找到和平的人 , 這兩位母親得以理解另一個尊重 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	911治癒了:那些找到寬恕、友情的媽媽 ,
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	我們今天來到這裡 , 是因為我們擁有大多數人所認為的不尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	然而 , 現在這對我們來說很自然 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次知道我的兒子在世界貿易中心在2001年9月11日的早上 。
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他是否已經死了 , 直到三十六小時之後 。
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道那是政治化的 。
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們很害怕我們的國家將會做些什麼 , 以我們兒子之名---我的丈夫 , 我和我們的家人 。
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	當我看到---雖然如此 , 很震驚很可怕的驚嚇還有我們生命裡的可怕的爆炸簡直就是我們沒有報復性
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾週後當zacariasmoussaoui被指控六項恐怖攻擊的陰謀時 , 美國政府要求對他有死刑如果他被定罪 , 我和我丈夫在公開場合反對這件事
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過這些和人權團體 , 我們與其他受害者家屬組織起來 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我在媒體上看到aicha , 她的兒子被起訴時 , 我心想: 「 真是一個勇敢的女人 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	我希望有一天 , 當我強壯一點的時候 , 能見到那個女人 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我還在深深的悲傷之中 ; 我知道我沒有這份力氣 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道我有一天會找到她 , 或我們會找到對方 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當別人聽到我兒子是受害者時 , 我馬上就同情了 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們學她的兒子被指控的事時 , 她卻沒有得到同情 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她所承受的痛苦與我的相同 。
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	所以我們在2002年十一月相識 , 現在aicha會告訴你這一切是怎麼來的 。
aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	aichaelwafi:午安 , 各位先生女士
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是zacariasmoussaoui的母親 。
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	並請人權組織讓我去接觸那些受害者的父母
so they introduced me to five families .	所以他們介紹我認識五個家庭
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	我看到phyllis , 我看著她 ,
she was the only mother in the group .	她是這群裡唯一的媽媽
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他都是兄弟姊妹
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我從她的眼睛看到她是位母親 , 就像我一樣 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	我作為一個媽媽很痛苦 。
i was married when i was 14 .	我14歲時結婚
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我在十五歲的時候失去了一個孩子 , 第二個孩子 , 那時我十六歲 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	所以 , 薩卡莉亞的故事太多了 。
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	而我依然受苦 , 因為我兒子就像是被活埋了一樣 。
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她真的為兒子哭了
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪裡 。
my son , i don't know where he is .	我的兒子 , 我不知道他在哪裡 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他是否還活著 , 我不知道他是否受到折磨
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生什麼事 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	所以 , 這就是為什麼我決定要說我的故事 , 讓我的痛苦是其他女性能很正面的東西 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	對所有的女人 , 所有賦予生命的媽媽 , 你可以回饋 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	這取決於我們女人 , 因為我們是女人 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們一定要手牽手一起做些什麼 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	這不是反對女性這是為我們 , 為我們女人為我們的孩子
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我說的是反抗暴力 , 反抗恐怖主義 。
i go to schools to talk to young , muslim girls so they don't accept to be married against their will very young .	我去學校跟年青的穆斯林女孩談話 , 這樣她們才不會接受自己非常年輕的意志結婚 。
so if i can save one of the young girls , and avoid that they get married and suffer as much as i did , well this is something good .	所以 , 如果我能拯救其中一位年輕女孩 , 並且避免她們結婚並且受盡我所能 , 嗯 , 這是件好事 。
this is why i'm here in front of you .	這是我站在你們面前的原因 。

and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	然後aicha開始講起 , 她說: 「 我不知道我的兒子是有罪還是無罪 , 但我想告訴你 , 我是多麼遺憾 , 為了你家人的遭遇 。

and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	接著發生的事 , 我們都說了自己的故事 , 我們都以人的身分來連結 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	到了午餐結束時--大概是午餐後的三小時--我們覺得好像彼此認識了一樣 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的是 , 一個女人 , 不僅僅是她可以在現在的處境和當時的情況下如此慷慨 , 還有什麼對她的兒子所做的事 , 還有她曾擁有的生命 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有見過一個擁有如此辛苦生活的人 , 來自如此全然不同的文化和環境 。
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有一種特殊的聯繫 , 我非常重視這個聯繫 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我想這一切都是為了害怕對方 , 但下了那一步 , 然後意識到: 「 嘿 , 這並沒有這麼難 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	我還能碰到誰呢 ? 我不知道 ? 或我和這麼不同 ? 」

i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了lifesaver濾水瓶 , 因為我很生氣 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我和你們一樣在2004年聖誕節後的隔天 , 我在看電視報導亞洲海嘯摧毀性的新聞 , 在電視上不斷播放 。
the days and weeks that followed , people fleeing to the hills , being forced to drink contaminated water or face death .	接下來的日子和數週 , 人們逃到山丘上 , 被迫喝下被污染的水 , 或是面對死亡 。

before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在lifesaver濾水瓶之前 , 最好的手動過濾器只能過濾小至200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌大約是200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以一個200奈米的細菌將穿過一個200奈米大的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒大約是25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	所以這絕對會穿過那些200奈米大的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	lisaver濾水瓶的孔隙只有15奈米大小 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以沒有任何東西可以通過 。

traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統上 , 在危機中 , 我們該怎麼做 ?

instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	與其運送水和使用人造過程去做 , 不如直接使用大自然 。 她有一個很棒的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從那裡取水 , 免費下鹽 , 運送到山上 , 河流和溪流 。

paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	帕迪阿什唐聲稱我們正處於歷史中 , 權力正在以前所未有的方式改變 。 在tedxbrussel的一個拼寫演講中 , 他指出了他所看到的三大全球轉變 。
foreign policy , global issues , politics , world cultures	外交政策 , 全球議題 , 政治 , 世界文化 ,
paddy ashdown: the global power shift	paddyashown:全球權力移轉
there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	有一首詩這麼寫道這是一位很有名的英國詩人在十九世紀末寫的
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	據說 , 邱吉爾在1930年代時的大腦會迴盪 ,
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	這首詩是這麼寫的: 「 夏天的鑽石山上 , 隨著溪流而死 , 我聽到遠方的鼓聲 , 鼓聲就像夢裡的聲音 , 遙遠而低 , 低沉 , 低沉而高聲在路上 , 親愛的對象是朋友和食物給粉筆 , 士兵遊行 , 很快就死了 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩很感興趣的人 , 這首詩是《shropshirelad》由a.e.豪斯曼所寫 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但是豪斯曼所理解的你也在尼爾森交響曲中聽過就是十九世紀那漫長 , 炎熱 , 沉浸於穩定的夏季正要臨近這兩種當權力改變時我們正要進入那段駭人的歷史時期之一
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	各位先生女士這些日子總是伴隨著騷動偶爾也有血緣關係
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我給你的訊息是 , 我相信我們被譴責 , 如果你願意 , 只活在歷史上的那些時刻 , 當已建立的權力秩序開始改變時 , 世界的觀點新的權力存在時 , 便開始形成了 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	這些是----而且我們今天清楚看到了--幾乎總是高度動亂的時刻 , 高度困難的時期 , 很多時候都非常血腥 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順帶一提 , 它每世紀都會發生一次 ,
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你可能認為它最後一次發生 , 那就是豪斯曼的感受 , 和邱吉爾也感受到的 , 就是當權力從舊時的國家流過 , 歐洲的舊權力 , 跨越大西洋 , 到美國新興崛起的美國 , 早在美國這個世紀初 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在真空中 , 歐洲人過時的權力被捲入兩個血腥災難中 , 在上個世紀 , 第一部份和第二部份:兩次世界大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	毛澤東曾經稱它們為歐洲內戰這或許是個更正確的形容方式
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士 , 我們住在其中一個時代 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 今天我想談三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	第一 , 前兩種 , 是關於權力的移轉 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二是關於一個新的維度 , 我想要講的是一個從來沒有像現在這樣發生的
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但 , 咱們來談談向世界轉變的權力 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	今天發生的事在某種意義上嚇人因為它從來沒有發生過
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們已經看到橫向的權力移轉 , 希臘的權力移轉到羅馬 , 以及歐美文明時所發生的權力移轉 , 但我們看到稍微不同的東西 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	權力不只是國與國之間橫向移轉 ,
it's also moving vertically .	它也是垂直移動的 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現今發生的狀況是 , 被包容的權力 , 受到責任的牽制 , 受到法律的牽制 , 在國家的機構內 , 現在已經大規模地移居到全球 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	全球化的權力我們談到全球化的市場 , 但事實上 , 是全球化的權力 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國家的層級裡 , 權力被責任的權力受到法律的牽制 , 在國際舞台上則否 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和全球舞台的權力浮現:網際網路的權力 , 衛星廣播的權力 , 貨幣改變的權力 , 這種大筆的金錢交易所傳遞的金錢數目是現在的32倍 , 對於交易所應有的金錢交易所應有的金錢交易 , 如果你願意的話 , 就是那些最近把我們大家帶到我們的膝蓋的財政管理者手推車的力量 , 相當於跨國企業的強大 , 現在也經常發展中國家推出的總計 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些人生活在一個全球化的空間 , 沒有受到法律規範的規範 , 並且人們可以自由地行事 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	現在那符合強權到達一個時刻 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	總是適合那些最有權力的人在沒有限制的場所操作 , 但歷史的教訓是 , 遲早 , 沒有受到法律規範的空間被充斥 , 不只是被你所想要的國際貿易 , 網路等等 , 還包括你不想要的國際犯罪者 , 國際恐怖主義 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	9•11事件的啟示是:即使你是地球上最強大的國家 , 無論如何 , 那些太空人也可以在你最具代表性的城市中攻擊你甚至在九月的早晨中攻擊你 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	有人說 , 四百萬美金中大約有百分之六十拿去資助911恐怖攻擊那次恐怖攻擊的機構已經通過雙子星大樓 , 而911摧毀了 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	你看 , 我們的敵人也使用這個空間就是大眾旅行、網路、衛星廣播的空間 , 能夠繞過他們的毒害 , 也就是破壞我們的系統和方式 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	不久之後 , 不久後 , 歷史的規則便是權力歸入何處 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	如果是這樣 , 正如我相信的 , 我們這個時代的一個現象就是全球化的權力 , 那麼我們這個時代的一個挑戰就是把統治者帶到全球 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信在我們眼前的這幾十年 , 會是大或小的動亂 , 或多或少有機會達成目標:把統治權帶上國際舞台 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	現在請注意 , 我不是在說政府
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是在說設立一些全球民主機構
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順道一提 , 我自己的看法是 , 各位先生女士 , 這是不太可能是由於產卵更多的聯合國機構來進行的 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 我們就得要發明 。
the world needs an international forum .	世界需要一個國際論壇
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一種方法 , 讓你可以合法化國際行動 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但當談到全球空間的統治時 , 我的猜測是 , 這不會發生 , 透過創建更多的聯合國機構來實現 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	實際上 , 強大的力量團結在一起 , 建立合約的系統 , 合約的基礎協議 , 來統治這個全球空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你看 , 你可以看到它們發生 , 已經開始出現 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:合約為底的組織 , 完全以合約為基礎 , 然而 , 強大到能夠容忍最強大的權力 , 即使是必要的權力 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	京都:掙扎著創造一個合約為底的組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	二十國集團:現在我們知道 , 我們必須組建一個機構 , 這個機構有能力將統治權帶到金融空間 , 做理財猜測 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	這就是二十國集團因而創立的 。
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有個問題了 , 我們等一下會再回來談 , 就是如果你把最強大的力量集合起來 , 讓規則以條約為基礎的機構 , 來填補統治空間 , 那還剩下的弱國會怎麼樣呢 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這是個大問題 , 我們等一下就會回歸到這個主題 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以我要傳達的第一個信息是 , 如果你正經歷這些動盪時代 , 或多或少令人不安 , 那麼 , 我們在做的成功將取決於我們把合理的統治權帶上全球 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	並觀察這會開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二點是 , 我知道我不用跟這樣的觀眾談這件事 , 但權力不只是垂直移轉 , 還能橫向移轉 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你也許會主張這個故事 , 文明的歷史已經聚集在海洋上 , 和第一批出現在地中海的文明聚集在一起 , 在大西洋的西方後裔中 , 較近期才出現 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	在我看來 , 現在我們看到的 , 是權力的根本轉移 , 廣義來說 , 遠離那些被大西洋棋盤聚集在一起的國家 , 遠離太平洋岸邊到處都是 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	這始於經濟實力 , 但始終如一 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外國政策的發展 , 軍事預算的擴增 , 在世界上其他越來越大的強權國家中 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	其實 , 這從西方移轉到東方並不多 , 不一樣的事情正在發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我的猜測是 , 對於它的價值 , 美國在接下來的十年、十五年 , 仍然是世界上最強大的國家 , 但她握有權力的背景現在已經徹底改變了 ; 它已經徹底地改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們正走出歷史的五十年當中 , 最不尋常的是 , 歷史上我們有著完全獨立的世界 , 每一根指南都要被指定為 , 華盛頓所指定 , 一個被單一巨人所包圍的世界 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但在歷史上這並非常見的情況 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在正在興起的是歷史上較常見的案例 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你開始看到多極化世界的出現
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	到目前為止 , 美國一直是世界的主導特徵 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們會保持是最強權的國家 , 但在越來越多的世界 , 他們會是最強大的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	然後你會開始看到其他的權力中心在中國建立 , 當然 , 不過我個人猜想的是 , 中國的偉大中心並不光滑 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	因為中國在自由經濟後開始將她的社會民主化而變得相當痛苦 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但那是另一個主題 。
you see india , you see brazil .	你看到印度 , 巴西
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	你逐漸發現 , 對我們歐洲人而言 , 世界看起來越來越像十九世紀的歐洲 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	十九世紀的歐洲:一名偉大的英國外交大臣坎寧曾形容它是 " 歐洲人的權力協奏會 " 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	曾經有一個平衡 , 一個五面的平衡點 ,
britain always played to the balance .	英國向來是平衡的 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林合作 , 英國和維也納和羅馬會面 , 提供一個反平衡點 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	現在請注意 , 在這段期間 , 由大富翁統治的時期 , 北約組織 「 華沙情節 」 主導 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	一個固定的權力對立意謂著 「 固定聯盟 」
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但有多個對立的權力意味著要轉移和改變結盟 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	這就是我們即將進入的世界我們會看到日漸增加的同盟國並非固定不變
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	傑出的英國外交部長坎寧曾說過: 「 英國有共同的利益 , 但沒有共同的盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們會看到 , 即使我們身在西方 , 也要伸出援手 , 跨出大西洋的舒適圈 , 可以和他人結盟 , 只要我們想在世界中把事情做好 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	要注意 , 當我們進入利比亞時 , 光靠西方國家一個人是不夠的 ; 我們要把其他人拉進來 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	在這個案例中 , 我們必須引進阿拉伯聯盟
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我的猜測是伊拉克和阿富汗 , 是西方國家最近一次嘗試自己做這件事 , 我們還沒有成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我的猜測是我們已經到達400年末的開端了 。 我說400年後 , 因為那是鄂圖曼帝國的結束 , 西方的權力、西方的機構和西方的價值觀 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道嗎 , 直到現在 , 如果西方國家共同採取行動 , 就可以在世界各個角落提出和反駁 。
but that's no longer true .	但現在不再是如此了 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	把二次世界大戰後最後一次金融危機
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方國家集合了布雷頓森林機構、世界銀行、國際貨幣基金--問題解決了 。
now we have to call in others .	現在我們必須號召其他人
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們必須創造二十國集團 。
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在我們必須超越西方的舒適圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我為各位做個預測 , 這可能還更驚人 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我懷疑我們已經到了400年後 , 西方的權力已經足夠了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	有人對我說: 「 中國人 , 當然 , 他們永遠都不會參與全世界的和平調停 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	喔是嗎 ? 為什麼不 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊在藍色貝雷特下服役 , 在藍色旗下服役 , 在聯合國的命令下服役 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 十一人
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	能處理索馬利亞海盜最大的海軍陸戰隊在哪裡 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國的海軍陸戰隊的內容
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	他們當然是 , 他們是位商人主義國家 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	他們想要維持航道的開放
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	漸漸地 , 我們得要和我們沒有共享價值觀的人做生意 , 但對於誰 , 目前 , 我們有共同的利益 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	這是一種全新的角度來看這個正在興起的世界 。
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	第三個因子 , 也是完全不同的 。
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	今天 , 在我們的現代世界 , 因為網路 , 因為人們一直在談論的各種事物 , 一切都和萬物相連 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在相互依賴 ,
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們之間的聯繫 , 作為國家 , 作為個體 , 以前所未有的方式 , 曾幾何上市 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國與國之間的相互關係 , 嗯 , 它一直都存在 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交就是要管理國家之間的相互關係 。
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在 , 我們密不可分地被關在一起 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	你會在墨西哥得到豬流感 , 24小時後對charledegaulle機場來說是一個問題 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟倒閉 , 全都倒塌了 。
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	俄羅斯的大草原發生火災非洲的糧食暴動
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都深刻、深刻、深切的相互關聯 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	這就意味著一個國家單獨行動 , 不與他人建立聯繫 , 不和他人合作 , 也不再是個可行的提案 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為一個國家的行為既不侷限於自己 , 也不足以讓國家自己去掌控自己的國土 , 因為國內外的影響現在開始影響到國內的狀況 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我當時是個年輕的軍人 , 在英國最後一次的小型帝國戰爭中 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我的國家的防衛是一回事 , 只有一件事:我們的軍隊多強 , 我們的空軍多強 , 我們的海軍多強 , 和我們的同盟國多強 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	當時敵人就在城牆外
now the enemy is inside the walls .	現在敵人就在城牆內
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在 , 如果我想談談我們國家的防衛 , 我必須和衛生署談談 , 因為大流行病對我們的健康造成威脅 , 我必須和農業部談談 , 因為食物安全對我的安全造成威脅 , 我必須和工業部談談 , 因為高科技基礎設施很脆弱 , 對於我們的敵人的攻擊 , 如同網路戰爭所見 , 我必須和內政部談談 , 因為那些直接在我的祖國 , 我們的房子裡發生了什麼事 ?
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	一個國家的安全不再僅僅是它的軍人和國防部的問題 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	能夠將自己的機構團結在一起的能力 ,
and this tells you something very important .	而這告訴你一件很重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴你 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直建構 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模型上 , 縱向層級結構 , 分工業結構的專門化 , 已經完全搞錯了結構 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	在企業你們知道我們時代的典範結構女士們先生們就是網路
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	重要的是你網絡的能力無論在你的政府內部或外部都有影響
so here is ashdown's third law .	這是ashown的第三定律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	對了 , 別問我第一條法則和第二法則因為我還沒發明出來不過 , 第三法則總是比較好聽 , 不是嗎 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	縮小法則就是在現代 , 所有事物都和一切相連 , 最重要的是 , 你能和他人做什麼 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	關於你的結構 , 最重要的一點是 , 不論你是政府 , 不論你是軍隊 , 不論你是企業 , 都是你的吸點 , 你的內部 , 你和他人建立網路的能力 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你懂的 , 在工業上 , 政府是不行的 。
but now one final thing .	但現在 , 最後一件事
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這樣 , 各位先生女士──我們現在是被鎖在一起 , 以一種前所未有的方式鎖在一起 , 那也是我們和彼此有著相同的命運 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 這也是第一次 , 集體防禦 , 支配我們國家安全的概念已經不足夠 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	過去 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落更強大 , 我就安全了 ; 如果我的國家比他們的國家強 , 我就安全了 ; 我的結盟 , 就像北約組織 , 比他們的聯盟更強大 , 我安全了 。
it is no longer the case .	不再是如此 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	大規模毀滅性武器的相互連結以及大規模毀滅性武器的出現 , 意味著我與敵人分享我的命運 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我還是外交官的時候 , 我和日內瓦的蘇聯在談判協定 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們了解我們和他們有著共同的命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全是不夠的 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平也來到北愛爾蘭因為雙方了解 , 零和遊戲是行不通的
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們和敵人有著共同的命運
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	阻礙著中東和平的其中一個強大的障礙就是以色列與巴勒斯坦人都不了解他們共同的命運
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以 , 各位先生女士 , 過去有願景的主張和詩人的年齡已經變成了我們必須要認真看待公共政策 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 以一首
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰•多恩的偉大詩作
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 不要為鐘聲的人送命 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 " 沒有人是孤島 "
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	它是這樣說的: 「 每一個人的死亡都影響著我 , 因為我和人類有關 , 請不要問鐘聲為誰響 , 反而是為別人的 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	對johndonne而言 , 道德建議
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為是方程式的一部分 , 代表著我們的生存 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到漫長的生命和健康的途徑 , 丹•布埃納和世界團隊研究 「 藍寶地 」 , 他們的長者與病毒同居 , 記錄年齡在tedxtc的年齡 。 他共有9個共同的飲食和生活方式的習慣 , 讓他們能活到100歲以上 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物學、文化、探索、食物、健康、生命、科學 。
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuettner:如何活到100++
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	有個丹麥雙胞胎的研究證實在某種生物限制下 , 人平均只能活多久只有百分之十在我們的基因上
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	另外百分之九十是由我們的生活方式主宰
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以 , 藍寶地的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式 , 我們就能得出一個事實──長壽的公式 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一般美國人 , 長壽的最佳公式是什麼 , 他們大概都說不出來 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽說過南海灘飲食 , 或阿金斯飲食 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國農業部的食物金字塔
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們的是
there is what doctor oz tells us .	奧茲醫生告訴我們
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實是 , 人們對於真正幫助我們活得更好的事 , 感到困惑 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該跑馬拉松還是做瑜珈 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	應該吃有機肉還是豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	當談及補充物時 , 你該服用嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	至於這些荷爾蒙或佛陀呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	而且目的性還會影響到它嗎 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	靈性 ? 還有我們如何社交 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們尋找長壽的方法是與國家地理還有國家老化研究院合作找出四個人口確定地理界線分明的區塊
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	然後帶進一組專家去有條理地去體驗這些人的所作所為 , 提高了跨文化的精華 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	演講最後我會告訴你們精華是什麼
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先我要揭開一些常見的迷思長壽的迷思
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是 , 如果你很努力就能活到一百歲
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 美國只有五千分之一的人能活到一百歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會很低
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使這是美國成長最快的人口結構還是很難達到一百歲
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是 , 我們並非長壽的程式 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們生而為一種叫做繁衍成功的東西 。
i love that word .	我愛這個字眼 。
it reminds me of my college days .	它讓我想起大學時
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家把這個詞稱為 「 成功 」 , 意思是你有孩子的年齡 , 接著是另一個世代 , 當你的孩子有了孩子時的年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在那演化的效應完全消失後
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	假如你是哺乳類 , 假如你是一隻老鼠 , 或是一隻大象 , 或是人 , 在兩者之間 , 都是一樣的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	要到一百歲時 , 你不僅得有個很好的生活方式 , 你還得中了基因樂透 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有治療可以幫助緩慢、逆轉、甚至停止衰老 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	仔細想想 , 有99件事可以讓我們老化 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	只要你的腦袋缺氧幾分鐘腦細胞就會死 , 從不復返
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	玩網球太辛苦了 , 膝蓋破了你的軟骨 , 軟骨永遠不會回來了 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈會堵塞 。 我們的大腦會用斑塊砸住 , 我們就能得老年癡呆症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事會出錯了 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有三十五兆個細胞 , 用 " t " 的兆來解釋 。 我們在這裡說的是國債 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	那些細胞每八年轉動一次
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當它們自身就會造成一些損害 , 造成損害 。
and it builds up exponentially .	並以指數方式增進
