it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	這有點像是當我們都擁有披頭四或老鷹合唱團的唱片專輯而我們會在錄音帶上複製那一錄音帶讓朋友複製那些錄音帶不久後就錄製出成功的世代膠帶聽起來很像垃圾
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事情也發生在我們的細胞上
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的人 , 比一個125歲的人老化的速度快125倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有你能做什麼減緩衰老或停止衰老我在這裡幹什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	嗯 , 事實上 , 最好的科學告訴我們 , 人體、身體、身體的容量 , 大約是90年 , 還多一點女人 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但這個國家的平均壽命只有78歲
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以 , 在生命的某個階段 , 我們在桌子上留下了大約12年的美好 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年來我們可能得到
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究也顯示多年來不用得慢性病、心臟病、癌症和糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為收到這些消失年齡最好的方法就是看看世界各地實際體驗的文化那裡的人們可以活到一百歲比我們多出十倍的地方那裡的壽命多出十倍而中年死亡率則是這個國家的一小部分
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們發現的第一個藍寶地是在義大利海岸外約一百二十五英里處 , 薩丁尼亞島上 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整座島 , 整座島約有一百四十萬人而是在高地上 , 一個叫努奧羅省的地方
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡我們有一區男性最長壽百歲人瑞的年齡大約是美國的十倍
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這裡的人不僅活到一百歲而已他們還擁有非凡的活力
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	一百零二歲的老人仍舊騎腳踏車去工作砍柴 , 還能打敗比他們年輕六十歲的小夥子
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史實際上可以回溯到大約基督的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	其實是與世隔絕的青銅器文化
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為這片土地是如此地不孕 , 它們大多是牧羊人 , 這種土地是規律且低強度的身體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食多以植物為主 , 多半以他們能帶到田地的食物為中心 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出一種未發酵的全麥麵包叫做cartamatamatamaywatsmet是一種乳酪肉類來自青草餵養的動物所以這種乳酪富含omega-3脂肪酸而不是omega-6脂肪酸由玉米餵養的動物製成並且有一種葡萄酒量比任何已知葡萄酒都高三倍
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但是我認為真正的秘訣在於他們組織社會的方式 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	而薩丁尼亞社會最突出的元素之一就是他們對待老年人的方式 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到 , 在美國 , 社會平等在24歲左右似乎達到巔峰 ?
just look at the advertisements .	只要看看那些廣告
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞這裡 , 你越長越平等 , 就有越多的智慧 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你走進薩丁尼亞的酒吧你看到的不是運動畫刊的泳裝日曆而是看到百歲人瑞的月曆
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	結果發現 , 這不僅對你年邁的父母有益 , 讓他們與家人更親近 , 還會有大約四到六年額外的預期壽命研究顯示 , 對那些家庭的孩子也是有益的 , 他們的死亡率比較低 , 疾病的比率也比較低 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	這就是所謂的祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們發現我們的第二個藍寶地在地球的另一端 , 在東京南方大約800英里 , 在琉球的群島上 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	琉球實際上是161個小島
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	而在主島的北端 , 這是世界長壽的起點 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這個地方住著最老的女性人口 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	這個地方的殘疾人均壽命是世界上最長的 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	他們的壽命很長 , 往往在睡覺時很快就死了 , 我可以告訴你 , 性過後 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們比一般美國人多活七年
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	五倍於美國的百歲人瑞
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	得結腸癌和乳癌的比率五分之一 , 在美國這裡的大殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病比例的六分之一
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	這種文化已經產出這些數字的事實 , 很明顯他們有可以教我們一些東西 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 植物為主的飲食 , 含有大量顏色的蔬菜 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	而且他們吃大約八倍多的豆腐比起美國人來說
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比他們吃的食物更重要
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各種小策略 , 可以避免過度飲食 , 如你所知 , 在美國是大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略 , 是用較小的盤子吃掉一些 , 所以每次用坐的方式都比較少吃卡路里 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其像家人一樣的服用方式 , 不如如如你說話時那樣無心地吃 , 他們在櫃台上服用 , 把食物放遠 , 然後再帶到餐桌上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們還有一句三千年的格言我認為是最棒的飲食建議
it was invented by confucius .	是孔子想出來的
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	而那飲食就是大家所知的哈拉哈拉、哈蒂奇、布丁
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	簡單來說 , 這些人在用餐前說 , 提醒他們在吃到80%的食物時 , 不要再吃 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	那感覺要花上一個半小時才能從肚子傳到腦袋
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	藉由記住要到百分之八十的停下來有助於讓你不用再做那些事
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但是 , 像薩丁尼亞 , 琉球有些社會結構讓我們可以與長壽相關
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立無援會導致
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	15年前美國人平均有三個好朋友
we're down to one and half right now .	目前我們只剩下一個半 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你夠幸運生在琉球你會生在一個系統裡讓你自動擁有半打朋友與他們同行
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱它為 " moai " 。 如果你在moai中 , 會期待看到運氣好 , 如果情況不好 , 孩子生病 , 父母去世 , 你總是有人背負著你的背 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這位特別的moai , 這五位女士相處了97年 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國我們已經把成人生活分成兩段
there is our work life , where we're productive .	有我們的工作 , 我們有生產力 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 碰 , 我們退休
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	通常這代表要退休給簡單的椅子 , 或是到亞利桑那州去打高爾夫 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在琉球語中甚至沒有退休這個詞
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	取而代之的詞語 , 沉浸在你的一生 , 那個詞就是 「 生存 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	粗略的翻譯是 「 早上起床的理由 」
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對這位一百零二歲的karate大師來說他的生存價值就是推動這項武術
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這位一百歲的漁夫來說 , 他的家人每週要捕三次魚 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	國家老化研究院也問了我們一份問卷調查員送這些百歲動物
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題 , 他們在文化上相當的敏銳 , 就是擺出問卷的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的生存是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為什麼早上起床時
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對這位一百零二歲的女人來說 , 她的生存只是她的曾曾曾曾曾孫女而已 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩個女孩在101歲半的年齡就被分開
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她感覺如何抱著一個曾曾曾曾孫女
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她回過頭說: 「 感覺就像飛躍上天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得這想法太棒了
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理的編輯要我去找美國的藍寶地 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一陣子 , 我們檢視明尼蘇達的草原在那裡 , 百歲人瑞的比例非常高 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有年輕人都離開了
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們再次轉向資料 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現了美國最長壽的人口 , 其中七天的推特人 , 集中在加州的羅瑪林達市 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	基督復臨派是保守的衛理公會教徒
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們在星期五日落慶祝休息日落到星期六日出時
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	他們稱之為 「 二十四小時的庇護 」 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循五個小習慣 , 相對來說 , 傳達給他們非凡的長壽行為 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均每位婦女平均壽命是八十 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對一個佛教女性來說 , 她們的平均壽命是89 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	男性之間的差異更明顯他們預期能多活十一年比起美國同伴來說
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這個研究追蹤了大約七萬人三十年
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	很傑出的研究 。 而且我認為這可以很清楚地說明這個藍寶地計畫的前提
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是一個異質族群 ,
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	是白人、黑人、西班牙裔、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一共有的是一套非常小型的生活習慣 , 他們一生中都遵守著這樣的習慣 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接從聖經來的飲食
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	創世紀第一章第二十九節上帝談到豆子和種子多在一塊的詩篇談到綠色植物很明顯少了肉
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們非常認真地看待這個避難所 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時 , 不論多忙 , 工作壓力多大 , 孩子需要驅動 , 他們停止一切 , 專注於他們的上帝、社交網路 , 接著 , 在宗教裡 , 天性就是個散步的大自然 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	強大之處不在於偶爾為之而在於它每個禮拜會完成一生
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	一點都不困難 , 一點都不花錢
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	基督復臨派教徒往往和其他高級教徒來往
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一個冒險家的派對你不會看到有人在搖曳jimbeam或滾動關節
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	相反地 , 他們在討論他們的下一次自然走路 , 交換食譜 , 是的 , 他們禱告 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們以很深遠且可測量的方式互相影響 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這個文化造就了埃爾斯沃•偉倫
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	埃爾斯沃•偉倫九十七歲
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是千萬富翁 , 但當包商想要六千美元來建造隱私圍籬時 , 他說: 「 用那種錢我自己來做 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以接下來的三天他都在外頭鏟水泥把欄杆拖來拖去
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可以預料的是 , 或許在第四天 , 他最後到了手術室 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是手術台上這個人而是在動開心手術的那個人
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	九十七歲時 , 他每個月都要做二十次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	艾德•羅林斯 , 現在一百零三歲是一個活躍的牛仔 , 早上就開始游泳
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	在週末時 , 他喜歡踏上衝浪板 , 拋出雲霄飛車尾 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實住在雙子都市 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她每天從舉重開始 ,
she rides her bicycle .	她騎著腳踏車
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	接著 , 她進入了她的根管 , 那是1994年的卡迪拉克賽維爾 , 在聖博納迪諾高速公路上流下淚 , 在那裡 , 她仍然是七個不同組織的志工 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我已經參加過十九次遠征 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我大概是唯一你認識的人裡不塗防曬油還在撒哈拉沙漠上騎腳踏車
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但是我要告訴你們 , 沒有任何探險比坐著攝影機的馬奇•戴頓更恐怖的了 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 一個陌生人是我還沒遇見的朋友 ! 」 她對我說:
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	那麼 , 這三種文化中有什麼共同點呢 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們都在做什麼 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們成功的把它歸結為九項
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 自從這之後 , 我們又做了兩個藍寶地探險 , 這些共同點也同樣為真 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	第一個 , 我將要在這裡演講 , 沒有一個是運動 , 至少是我們對運動的看法 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	反之 , 他們建立起的生活 , 使得他們不斷地被捲入身體的活動中 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些百歲的琉球女人每天坐在地上30到40次 ,
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在直立的房子裡 , 樓梯上下 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次去商店或教堂或去朋友家都要走路
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何的便利
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有按下一個按鈕可以做院子或房子的工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想攪拌一塊蛋糕 , 他們會用手
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	和跑步機一樣能燃燒卡路里 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們有意地做動作時 , 就是他們所享受的東西 。 他們走動是唯一證實能延遲認知活動下降的方法 , 他們都傾向有一個花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何以正確的方式生活所以他們有正確的人生觀
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	這些文化中每一種都花時間在降低
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 , 祈禱七天
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	琉球人的祖先有這種
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你匆匆促促促或焦慮不安會引發一種發炎反應這反應跟每一件事相關從老年痴呆到心血管疾病
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你一天放慢十五分鐘 , 你就會把那個發炎狀態轉變成更加抗炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們有語彙 , 目的地 , 像琉球人那樣的詞彙
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你生命中最危險的兩年就是你出生的那一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率和退休那年
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道自己的使命感 , 並在他們的生命中啟動 , 那價值大約七年多的預期壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽飲食
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天都喝一點酒 , 對美國人口來說不難 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	往往吃植物為主的飲食
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不代表牠們不吃肉 , 而是大量的豆類與堅果
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	而他們有策略防止過度飲食 , 小事在對的時間把他們推開 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	所有這些的基礎是他們彼此連結的方式 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把家人擺第一照顧好小孩跟年邁父母
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都傾向屬於一個以信仰為基礎的社群 , 價值四到十四年的預期壽命假如你每月做四次 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	而這裡最大的是他們也屬於合適的部落
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們不是生來就有 , 就是他們主動圍繞著對的人 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從佛明罕研究中得知如果你三個最好的朋友都胖你有一半的機會會超重
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人來往 , 隨著時間就會有顯著的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反的 , 如果你朋友的休閒行為是體力活動 , 保齡球或打曲棍球 , 騎腳踏車或園藝假如你的朋友會喝點酒 , 但不過量他們吃得恰當 , 全心全意信任和值得信任 , 那將會隨時間產生最大影響
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	節食沒用 , 世界歷史上從來沒有減肥成功過百分之二的人口
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計畫通常一月開始 , 通常是十月才會做 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	長壽沒有短期固定藥物或其他東西
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你想想看 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 也許是你能做的最重要的事 , 可以為你的生活增加更多年 , 並且在你多年的生活中保有 。 非常謝謝你 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	墨水能導電 ; 一扇窗 , 從明確轉向不透明轉盤 ; 一顆製造樂曲的果凍 。 所有東西的確存在 。 卡塔琳•莫塔提說:該是和它一起玩的時候了 。 mota帶領我們到一個驚喜且酷的新材料上 , 暗示我們要找出它們有什麼好處 , 是做實驗、做玩樂的 。
creativity , design , technology	創意、設計、科技、
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:玩智慧型材料
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我在葡萄牙有位朋友他的祖父用腳踏車和洗衣機改建了一台車以便運送他的家人
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他會這麼做 , 是因為他買不起車 , 但也是因為他知道如何建造一個
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾經我們了解事物如何運作以及它們是如何被製成的所以我們可以建造並修理它們或是在購買什麼的情況下做出最不可知的決策
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	許多這些diy的做法在20世紀下半葉失真 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 製造業和開放原始碼模型正把這類知識帶回我們的生活中 , 我相信我們需要把這些知識帶到下一個階段 , 讓組成的東西上 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大多數的情況下 , 我們仍然知道紙和紡織品等傳統原料是由什麼製成的 , 以及如何生產的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有這些了不起又有未來感的複合材料 , 可以改變形狀 , 可以導電的油漆 , 可以改變顏色的顏料 , 可以發亮的布料 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以導電油墨讓我們不用傳統印刷電路或電線來作畫電路或電線 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在我舉的這個小例子中 , 我們用它來建立觸控感應器 , 藉由開啟這個小燈 , 來對我的皮膚產生反應 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	藝術家用到導電油墨 , 但最近的發展顯示 , 我們很快就能將它用在雷射印表機和筆上面 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	而這塊丙烯酸鹽附著在無色的散光粒子上 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	意思是說 , 雖然普通的丙烯酸只會在邊緣散光 , 但這顆在我開燈的時候 , 整個表面都會發出光 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這類材質的應用已知有兩個包括室內設計及多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	熱變色顏料則會在特定溫度下變色
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	我要把這個放到溫度杯子上只會稍微高過音調 , 大家可以看到會發生什麼事
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	所以這個材料的其中一個原則是 , 在嬰兒奶瓶中 , 在嬰兒奶瓶中 , 它可以顯示內容物是否涼了可以喝了 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是眾所周知的智慧型材料中的一小部分 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年後 , 它們將成為我們日常生活中使用的物品和技術 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒辦法擁有科幻小說中會出現的飛天汽車但我們可以有能隨著溫度改變顏色的牆壁可以捲起來的鍵盤一關就能變不透明的窗戶
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	我是社會科學家所以我在這裡談智慧型材料呢 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是一個製造家
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我對事物的運作及組成方式感到好奇 , 也因為我相信 , 我們應該要對組成我們這個世界的元件有更深的了解 , 而現在 , 我們對於我們未來的這些高科技的複合材料了解程度不足 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧型材料難以獲得小量 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	怎麼用這些資料 , 幾乎沒有人可以取得的資訊 , 只知道它們是如何生產的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以目前 , 它們幾乎都存在於交易機密和專利的領域中 , 只有大學和公司能夠取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	大約三年多前 , 我和kirstybotle開始一項我們稱之為材料公開化的計劃
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	這個網站是我們 , 和任何想要加入我們的人 , 分享實驗、發佈資訊、鼓勵他人隨時作出貢獻 , 以及像我們這樣的自造者 , 投入研究論文及輔助等資源 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它成為一個以智慧型材料為主題的集體自行生成的大型資料庫 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但是為什麼我們要關心智慧型材料的運作及組成呢 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法塑造我們不了解的東西 , 而我們不了解、不使用的東西 , 最終塑造了我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們用的物品 , 穿的衣服住的房子 , 都對我們的行為健康和生活品質有著深遠的影響
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以 , 如果我們的世界是由智慧型材料所構成 , 我們應該要了解、了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二點 , 也同樣重要 , 創新一直都是由東克人所推動的 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘人士 , 而非專家們 , 一直都是發明者和改進者 , 從山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機等 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰在於材料科學很複雜且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但也不總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾大學有兩位科學家就這樣理解了 , 當時他們發表了一篇論文 , 用較簡單的方法製作導電油墨 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	喬登邦克 , 在那之前完全沒有任何化學經驗 , 讀到這篇論文 , 並在他的自造者空間進行實驗 , 只用現成的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤箱 , 甚至根據另一位科學家的說明書而做出了自己的旋風混音器 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	約旦接著在網路上公佈他的結果 , 包括他所有嘗試過、沒用的事 , 這樣其他人就可以在線上研究、繁殖 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	所以 , 約旦的創新主要形式是把在有裝備的大學實驗室所做的實驗放到芝加哥的車庫中 , 利用他自己製作的廉價材料和工具 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在 , 他發表了這個作品 , 其他人可以知道他離開哪裡 , 還可以設計出更簡單的處理和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另外一個我想要提的例子 , 讓她專案的目標是要突顯出材料的表現質 , 同時把焦點放在建造者的創造力和技巧 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子設備非常強大 , 能教我們實物如何運作 , 但其設計的限制影響了我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	另一方面 , 漢娜的做法是要組成一系列的技術 , 用來創造出不尋常的物體 , 藉由教導我們材料本身 , 來解放我們不受限制 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	在漢娜的許多令人印象深刻的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的一個 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[紙喇叭]我們現在看到的只是一張紙上面貼了一些銅片 , 連到mp3和磁鐵上
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	根據麻省理工學院的瑪賽羅柯爾霍的研究 , 漢娜用各式各樣的材料做出一系列的紙喇叭 , 從簡單的銅膠帶 , 到導電布和油墨 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	正如約旦還有許多其它的製作者漢娜將她的食譜出版 , 讓任何人可以複製、繁殖 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子是我們最有希望的材料科學其中一個分支 , 讓我們能創造出較便宜且有彈性的電子 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	因此漢娜的手工藝成果 , 以及她分享她的發現的事實 , 開啟了一系列新的可能性 , 這兩者兼具美學上訴與創新的可能性 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以 , 製造者有趣的地方在於我們是以熱情和好奇創造出來的 , 我們不怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們經常從非傳統的角度來處理問題 , 在過程中 , 最後發現了替代方案 , 甚至更好的方式來做事情 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以越多人在材料上做實驗 , 越多研究人員願意分享他們的研究成果 , 並製造出他們的知識 , 我們就有更好的機會去創造出能服務所有人的技術 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	所以我覺得泰德•尼爾森必定在1970年代早期 , 他寫道: 「 現在你一定要了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	在那時 , 電腦是只有科學家在乎的大型主機 , 沒有人夢想能在家裡裝一個 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡說: 「 你現在必須要了解智慧型材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	別忘了 , 新興科技的知識是確保我們在創造我們的未來時 , 能夠發表言論的最佳方式 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會進入一個玻璃泡 , 鎖住房門 , 按下加速器 , 仰賴我們的眼睛來引導我們 , 即使我們只能看到前方和後方的少數幾輛車 。 但如果汽車能互相分享彼此的位置和速度 , 並使用可預測的模型 , 來計算每個人在道路上的安全路徑 ? 珍妮佛.喜利 , 想像一個沒有意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	jenniferhealey:如果車子能說話 , 車禍可能會被避免 ,
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	面對現實吧開車是危險的
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡思考的事情之一 , 但事實上 , 宗教代表以及好運的魅力出現在世界各地的儀表板上 , 背叛了我們知道這是真的 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是美國16至19歲青年死亡的主因車禍是導致死亡的主因而其中百分之七十五的車禍和毒品或酒精無關
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人能肯定 , 但我記得我的第一次意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我還是個年輕的司機在高速公路上 , 前面的車 , 我看到煞車燈亮了 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我想: 「 好吧 , 好吧 , 這個人在放慢速度 , 我也會放慢速度 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踩到了剎車 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這個傢伙沒有慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙正在停車 , 停在高速公路上 , 停車 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	剛好是65比0 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我緊急煞車 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我感覺到abs打進來 , 車仍然向前 , 它不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 空氣袋子會壞了 , 車子完全壞了 , 幸好沒有人受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全不知道車子停了我認為我們可以做得更好
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我想 , 我們可以轉變駕駛經驗 , 讓車子彼此對話 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只是想讓你們想想現在駕駛的體驗是什麼樣的 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	上你的車 , 關上門 , 你在一個玻璃泡裡
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感受你周圍的世界
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的軀殼裡
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是在看不見的路上行駛在其他金屬巨人和超人的高速行駛
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	懂嗎 ? 你只需要指引你兩個眼睛
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好了 , 這就是你所有的眼睛 , 眼睛雖然不是設計來的 , 但後來卻有人要你做像是車道的改變 , 他們要你做的第一件事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	不看路面的情況 , 沒錯
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	別看你要往哪裡去 , 轉彎 , 檢查你的盲點 , 然後在路上開車 , 不看你要往哪裡去 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人都一樣 。 這是安全的駕駛方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須做個選擇 , 看這裡 , 還是我看這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們在路上採取、選擇我們想要什麼 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們也會出錯 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們會意識到做錯了或太遲 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	在無數的意外中 , 司機們說: 「 我沒看到它來了 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	而我相信 , 我相信這點
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看得見這麼多
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現在這個技術的存在卻可以幫助我們改善這個狀況 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 有了車輛互相交換資料 , 我們不僅能看到前面三部車 , 後面三輛 , 右邊和左邊三輛車 , 同一時間 , 鳥瞰圖 , 實際上我們能看到這些車 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們將能看到前面車輛的速度 , 看到車子開得多快或停下來 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那個人下降到零 , 我就會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	有了計算、演算法和預知模型 , 我們將能夠預見未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你們可能認為這不可能
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你怎麼能預測未來 ? 那真的很難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	其實不 。 有車子 , 這不是不可能的 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	車是立體的有固定的位置和速度
they travel down roads .	它們在道路上行駛 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	往往在突出的路線上旅行
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	要合理地預測車子在不久的將來會去到哪裡 , 真的並不難 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使 , 當你上車 , 遇到了一些機車騎士過來 , 每小時八十五英里 , 車輛停下來 , 我知道你有過這樣的經驗: 「 出沒沒了 。 」
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那傢伙可能在前半小時路上
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	是吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人看過他
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10哩前20哩前30哩前有人見過他只要有一部車看到那個人然後把他放到地圖上他就在地圖上的位置上順利估計他會以每小時85英哩的速度持續前進
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為那另一輛車會在他的耳邊低語一些東西 , 比如 , 「 順便一提 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車騎士 , 小心 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以合理地預測汽車的行為 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 它們是牛頓式的物體 。
that's very nice about them .	對他們而言那是非常棒的 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們要如何達成 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的事情開始分享我們車子間的位置資料只要分享gps
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我的車子裝有gps和攝影機 , 我就會知道我在哪裡 , 以及我要多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我車子的位置 , 估算一下它們的方向 。
and same with the other cars .	和其他車一樣
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們能精確的知道自己身在何方也能想出其他車子在哪裡
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩部車子共用那些資料 , 如果它們彼此交談會怎麼樣 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你們確實發生了什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	bobwang教授和他的團隊做了一些電腦模擬 , 計算出當毛茸茸的估計加上後會發生什麼事 , 甚至是輕型交通 , 當車子只是共用gps資料時 , 我們把這個研究從電腦模擬移出 , 移到裝有真正的感應器的車床上 , 裝在這些機器人身上:立體攝影機、gps和2d立體雷射測距儀──這些都是共通的備用系統 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們還裝上一台短距的無線電機台 , 機器人彼此交談 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些飛行器互相飛來時 , 它們能精準地追蹤到彼此的位置 , 它們能避開彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在在混合當中加入越來越多的機器人 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	有個問題 , 當你的聊天太多時 , 就很難去處理所有的包裝 , 所以你得要優先處理 , 而那是預測模型能協助你的地方 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的飛行車都在追蹤那些預知的軌跡 , 你就不會太注意那些資訊封包 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你把一個看起來有點偏離航道的傢伙列為優先順序
that guy could be a problem .	那個人可能會是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	並且可以預測新的軌跡
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他要偏離航道了還知道他要怎麼偏
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	知道哪個駕駛需要警告 , 才能離開路 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想要做到最好警告每個人的行為嗎 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車要怎麼小聲警告: " 你得趕緊離開這裡 "
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 這取決於兩件事:一 , 汽車的能力 , 二 , 司機的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果有一個人有一部很棒的車 , 但他們是用手機 , 或者 , 你知道 , 做點什麼 , 他們可能沒有在緊急狀態中做出最佳的反應 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以 , 我們開始一條不同的研究 , 做一些駕駛者的國家模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 使用三台攝影機的一系列攝影機 , 我們可以偵測到駕駛人是否有在看前面、在看遠方、在電話上或者在喝咖啡時 , 來檢測 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預知意外 , 還可以預測是誰 , 哪一輛車 , 最好的位置是要搬出去 , 為每一個人計算最安全的路線 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 現今的這些技術
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面臨的最大問題是我們自己的意願去分享資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我認為這是一個非常讓人不舒服的想法 , 認為我們的車會在監視著我們 , 和其他車聊聊天 , 說我們會在一條流言的大海中走下去 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信它可以用一個保護我們隱私的方式來做事 , 就像現在一樣 , 當我看著你的車子從外面看 , 我不知道你是怎麼做的 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看一下你的牌照號碼 , 我不太知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以談論在我們背後的我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	而我認為這將會是很棒的事情 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我希望你們考慮一下如果你真的不想讓那些分心的青少年在你身後知道你在煞車知道你要停下來
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	藉由意願分享我們的資料 , 我們可以做到對每個人最好的做法 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以讓你的車去八卦你 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	能讓道路使用更為安全
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprize的創辦人彼得•戴曼迪斯談到他如何幫助史蒂芬•霍金完成了他前往太空的夢想 , 通過一起飛向上層大氣層 , 體驗到無重力 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、短暫的演說、空間、科技、宇宙
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	peterdamandis在stephenhawking零年時
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	認識我的人都知道 , 我對於打開太空邊境有多麼熱衷 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給這位世界重力專家無重力的經驗時 , 那真是不可思議 。
and i want to tell you that story .	而我想要告訴你們那個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次見到他 , 透過基因體學archonxprize 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們所舉辦的競賽 , 第二個xprize , 將十天內第一個完成100個人類基因組定序的團隊 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有所謂的基因組-100人-也就是我們定序的一部分 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特的椅子 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇到了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想是上太空旅行 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你去那裡 , 但我可以帶你去無重力進入無重力狀態 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他當場接著說: 「 絕對可以 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	嗯 , 要體驗地球上唯一的無重力飛行的方法 , 其實只有利用拋物線飛行 , 無重力飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你搭飛機 , 飛到頂端 , 25秒都無重力 ,
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	再下來 , 體重的兩倍
you do it again and again .	一而再 , 再而三
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以有8到10分鐘的無重力經驗nasa如何訓練太空人長久之久
we set out to do this .	我們打算這麼做 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們也宣佈要讓史蒂芬•霍金上市 。
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一個政府部門和一個公司經營者說 , 你瘋了 , 不要這樣做 , 你們會殺了這個人 。
and he wanted to go .	而他也想去
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們努力地取得所有許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們在甘迺迪太空中心坐下 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們召開了記者會 , 我們宣佈了自己的打算要做一個無重力拋物線 , 給他25秒的無重力 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果一切順利 , 我們可能會做三台拋物線飛行 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	我們問他為什麼他想上去做這個 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	而他所說的 , 對我來說是非常感人 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生物面臨著不斷增加的危機 , 被災難所消滅......
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我覺得人類如果不上太空 , 就沒有未來 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	因此我想要鼓勵公眾對於空間的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們帶他去甘迺迪太空中心 , 在nasa的車子裡 , 進入zero-g飛機的後方 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們有約20個人捐款我們捐了15萬美元給那些陪伴我們的兒童慈善機構 。
a few tedsters here .	幾位tedsters在這裡
we set up a whole er .	我們設立了一整間急診室 。
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四位急診室醫生和兩位護士 , 登上飛機 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們監測他的血液、心跳、血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	萬一緊急事件發生時 , 天知道 , 你並不想傷害這個世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落場起飛 , 在那裡 , 太空梭起降 , 降落 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	而我和我的夥伴byronlichtenberg小心地將他懸掛在無重力 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他在那裡 , 我們就讓他去體驗無重力的真正樣子 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	經過第一個拋物線飛行之後 , 你知道 , 醫生說一切都很棒 。 他在微笑 , 我們就說開始了 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物線飛行 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們真的讓一顆蘋果漂浮到艾薩克.牛頓爵士 , 因為霍金教授在劍橋拿著和艾薩克.牛頓相同的椅子 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四、第五和第六次 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	第七次和第八次 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這個人看起來不像一個65歲輪椅男子 。
he was so happy .	他好高興 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們住在珍貴的首飾 , 正是在我們有生之年 , 逐漸遠離這個星球 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請與我們一同參加這偉大的冒險之旅 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫學動畫師大衛•博林斯基現在展示了驚人的動畫 , 呈現出細胞裡面熱鬧的生命 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計 , 娛樂 , 電影 , 健康 , 醫學 , 科學 , 科技 , 視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky動畫出一個細胞
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是一個醫學繪圖師 , 我從一個稍微不同的角度
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	我一直在觀察 , 自從我長大以來 , 藝術中真與美的表現方式 , 以及科學中的真與美 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	儘管這些都是他們自己想的美好事物它們都有一些美妙的東西給它們成為可以被科學或是數學所檢視的理想事物就像是科學家們會想要與他約會的完美雙胞胎
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些是 「 真 」 的表情 , 所謂 「 敬畏之物 」 。 意思是 , 它們是你可以崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是有力的理想 。 它們是不可思議的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們很獨特 , 有時很有用 , 通常要等很久才會這麼做 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	現在你真的可以滾出其中一些照片了 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看到我 ,
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真與美 , 對科學不在的人來說 , 往往是不透明的東西 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們是用描述 「 美 」 的方式來描述美的事物 , 通常只能用你懂的語言和語調 , 來描述研究主題的真與美 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你看宇宙常數 , 那裡存在一個人類學的理想 , 在那裡你會看到生命需要從描述宇宙的數字演化出來--這些都是非常難理解的事物 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我接受醫學插圖教學以來 , 我試圖作出一個醫學插畫家的訓練從我父親的動畫 , 他是一個雕塑家和視覺導師我想要想出一個方法幫助人們了解生物科學中的真與美藉由動畫 , 通過運用圖片 , 說故事以便讓那些不見得見的東西可以被帶給人們並且可以被傳授並且可以被理解
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今的學生常常沉浸在一種環境中 , 他們所學的就是內在真與美的事物 , 但教導他們的方式是具體化的 , 並歸根究底 , 真與美並不總是顯而易見 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	就像是雞湯的老食譜 , 讓雞肉肉沸騰 , 直到香味通散去 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想這樣對我們的學生
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們才有機會真正開放教育
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	幾年前 , 我接到哈佛大學分子與細胞生物學系的robertlue的電話 。 他問我我和我的團隊是否有興趣而且有意願改變哈佛的醫學與科學教育方式 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始了一項探索細胞的計畫 , 探究分子與細胞生物學中固有的真與美 , 讓學生了解更大的圖片 , 可以把所有的事實都掛在上面 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們可能腦海中浮現一個細胞的樣子 , 是一個巨大、繁忙、複雜的城市 , 由微型機器佔據 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	這些微機械真的是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 能讓世界各地的奈米科技很嫉妒 , 它們是能自我導向、強大、精準、精確的裝置 , 由一串胺基酸所組成 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	而這些微機械能驅動細胞的移動 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們能驅動細胞複製、驅動我們的心臟
they power our minds .	它們能給我們的心靈力量 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以 , 我們想要做的是 , 弄清楚如何把這個故事變成動畫的中心 , 讓它成為哈佛大學biovisions的中心 , 它是一個哈佛大學為分子與細胞生物學學生所設立的網站 , 除了所有的文本資訊 , 外 , 所有教學內容都以視覺呈現 , 這樣這些學生們將細胞內化的真與美呈現出來 , 並且可以用心智來研究這個觀點 , 這樣一來 , 他們就能發掘出新的生命力 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們先來看看這些分子是如何組合在一起的 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們的研究主題是 , 巨噬細胞是從微血管細胞流下來的 , 它們觸碰到了微血管壁的表面 , 它們從微血管壁上取得訊息 , 它們被授予了這些資訊 , 在外面的某處有發炎 , 它們在那裡看不見也聽得到 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但它們得到讓它們停下來的資訊 , 導致它們被內化 , 它們需要製造各式各樣的零件 , 使它們改變它們的形狀 , 嘗試離開這個微血管 , 找出到底發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達我們必須與哈佛的科學家合作 , 與原子力準確分子的數據庫模型合作 , 找出它們如何移動 , 然後找出它們所做的 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	想出辦法 , 用真誠的方式 , 將正在發生的事隱藏起來 , 但不說實話 , 細胞中那些緊密的擁擠 , 避免這種麻煩發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	我現在要給你們看的是我們所製作的這部電影的第一層部份的三分鐘的閱讀它是一個持續進行中的計劃再過四到五年
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	我希望你們看到這些 , 看到細胞製造這些會走路的小機械 , 它們叫做卡因斯 , 用這些巨大的負荷 , 用相對大小的負荷去挑戰螞蟻 。
run the movie , please .	請播放 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些驅動細胞內部的機械真的非常神奇 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機械會彼此互動 。
they pass information to each other .	它們彼此傳遞信息 ,
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們造成細胞內不同的變化 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會真的製造出果蠅需要的部件 , 透過讀取基因的分子 , 從核中得來的資訊 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有任何生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的每一個人 , 若沒有這些小微機械 , 一切都有可能實現 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 沒有這些機器 , 克里斯非常零散 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞的fedex快遞小弟 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這小傢伙叫做驅動蛋白 , 他拉著一顆滿是新型製造出的蛋白質到細胞所需的任何地方 , 不論是到細胞膜、不論是到器官上 , 不論是用來製造東西或修補一些東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人大約有十萬個這種東西在你的一百兆個細胞內運作 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你感覺有多懶惰 , 本質上你並沒有在做任何事 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以 , 我希望你們回家後 , 能想想這一點 , 並想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	並思考一些關於細胞機械學的知識
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們明白了所有正在發生的事情並且相信我 , 我們知道幾乎百分之一發生了什麼 , 一旦我們弄清楚發生了什麼 , 我們將能夠掌控很多事情 , 掌握我們對健康的掌控權 , 用我們和未來世代的做法 , 及我們能活多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能藉此發現更多的真與美 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但非常驚人的是這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 都足夠意識到細胞需要它們來支撐它們 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	它們一起運作 。 它們使這個細胞去執行它所需做的事 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	它們一起運作 , 幫助我們的身體龐大 , 它們永遠無法看到正常功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受接下來的表演 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪•布蘭頓打算在車上住一整年 , 看到國家情勢但沮喪停止後 , 她的自由工作結束了她的露營旅程就變成無家可歸 。 在這場親密的演說中 , 她描述了她變成美國其中一間 「 無家可歸 」 的經歷
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、生活、個人成長、貧窮、社會改變、說故事 。
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	beckyblanton:我當時無家可歸的那一年
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是作家和記者 , 同時也是非常好奇的人 , 所以 , 在我當了二十二年的記者之後 , 我學會了很多新事物 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學會了如何變成看不見的東西 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我變成了在職無家者 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭去了報紙編輯的工作就在我父親同年二月去世之後我決定去旅行
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死亡讓我受到很大的打擊 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	在我這麼做的同時 , 我也想要去感受和處理很多事情 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一生都露營 , 決定在旅行車中謀生一年 , 就像一趟漫長的露營旅行 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以我打包我的貓 , 我的洛威拿包機和露營裝備 , 放進1975年雪佛蘭旅行車 , 開著車去日落 , 完全沒有想到三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:社會將永久居住 , 甚至是小屋 , 劃分爲人物的價值 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	二:我沒有意識到 , 很快地 , 別人的負面看法對我們的現實影響有多大 , 假如我們讓它發生 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	三:我沒意識到無家可歸是一種態度 , 而不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在旅行車很棒 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地洗澡 。 我定期吃飯 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我還有時間可以放鬆和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但接著 , 我父親去世時的憤怒和沮喪 ,
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的 「 自由工作 」 結束了 。 我得要找全職工作來支付這些帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	本來溫和的春天 , 整個夏天都轉變成為冷酷無情 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	不論在哪裡 , 都不可能去公園 , 很明顯我帶了一隻貓、一隻狗來 , 而且真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	那隻貓跑來了 , 穿過箱型車的開窗
the doggy went into doggy day care .	狗送進 " 生化日護理 "
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	任何時候 , 我都可以在辦公大樓裡使用員工淋浴間 , 卡車站也停下來 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或是我在公共休息室洗的
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜間的車廂中很少在華氏80度以下讓人幾乎無法入睡
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱裡腐爛
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	冰箱裡的冰在幾小時之內融化 , 狀況相當悲慘 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我沒錢住進准許的公寓 , 也沒錢住一間公寓 , 這樣我就能有老人院和貓了 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄他們 , 所以我待在旅行車上 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當暖氣讓我連走了50呎到晚上在我的旅行車外的公共廁所我用一個桶和一個垃圾袋當作廁所
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天來臨時 , 溫度下降到零度以下 , 持續在那兒
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我又面對了一整套新的挑戰
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每晚都把不同的地方停下來 , 這樣我才能避免被警察注意到並引起反抗 。
i didn't always succeed .	我不是每次都成功
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我覺得無法掌控自己的生活 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我也不知道何時或如何發生但我從一個才華橫溢的作家和記者變成了一名流浪漢女性住在旅行車上把我的呼吸奪走
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒變 。 我的智商沒變 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的才華、正直、價值觀、一切關於我的一切都仍然保持不變 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我卻以某種方式改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我在沮喪中越做越深入 ,
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後有人把我轉診到無家可歸的健康診所
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我去了 。 我三天沒洗澡了 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我和排隊中任何人一樣臭、一樣沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是沒喝醉或高不喝醉 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當數名流浪漢領悟到 , 包括一位前大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你本非無家 , 你為何落得如此下場 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家者不把我當成無家者 , 但我知道了 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	教授聽了我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家者沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給我的藥物的一個反應讓我有自殺傾向 。 我記得當時心想: 「 如果我自殺 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	不久之後 , 有一個朋友告訴我 , 她聽說提姆•羅素他是全國知名的記者 , 曾經在國際電視節目上談到我 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫過一篇關於我父親的文章在他死前一年寫的在提姆的新書裡
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	當時他在演說節目電路邊談到我的寫作
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到timrussert , 《與傳媒會見》的前主持人 , 正在談論我的寫作 , 當我住在旅行車上停在沃爾瑪停車場時 , 我開始笑了 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑了因為它到達一種程度我是個作家 , 還是一個無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	於是我走進書店 , 找到提姆的書
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 , 重新讀了我的文章
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家 ,
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	不久之後我搬回了田納西 ,
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我在住在旅行車和朋友的沙發之間做個交易 。
and i started writing again .	然後我又開始寫作 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	隔年夏天我又成為一名工作記者
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我獲得獎項 , 住在自己的公寓裡
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	而我不再被忽視 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數以千計的人全職、兼職工作 , 住在他們的車子裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續汙名化 , 並將住在你車上或在街上犯罪化 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以無家者 , 職場無家可歸的人 , 主要是保持在看不見的狀態 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇見了一個 , 鼓勵他們 , 並給他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神可以克服任何如果有希望 ,
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我來這裡不是為了那個無家可歸的海報女孩
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是來鼓勵你們捐錢給你們遇到的下一個乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但是我在這裡要告訴你們 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不是生活的地方、睡哪裡 , 也不是他們生活在哪裡 , 或他們生活在哪裡 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前我住在旅行車上停在沃瑪超市的停車場現在我在ted演講
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是 , 永遠要找到出路 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxange , 泰國的 " 保險套先生 " mechaiviravaidya帶領我們穿越國家大膽的計畫提升生活水準從1970年代開始 , 第一步驟:人口控制 。 這意味著很多法蘭克 , 有趣的 , 也非常有效的關於安全套的演講 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	mechaiviravaidya:保險套先生如何讓泰國變得更好 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	四十年前 , 當我還是個年輕人時 , 這個國家非常非常的窮 , 有許多的人民生活在貧窮的環境中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定要為此做點什麼 , 但我們不是從福利計畫開始 , 也不是從貧窮減輕計畫開始 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭計畫著手 , 遵循著非常成功的孕產婦健康活動 , 組成許多活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	所以基本上 , 沒有人會接受如果他們的孩子沒有存活 ,
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以 , 第一步:先生到孩子 , 去找母親們 , 然後再接再生家庭規劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不僅僅是兒童死亡率 , 你還需要節育計畫 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在讓我帶各位回顧一下為什麼我們需要
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的狀況 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭的7個孩子有極大的成長率有3.3% 。
there was just no future .	根本沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要降低人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 就去做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	婦女們說: 「 我們也同意 , 使用避孕藥 , 但我們需要醫生來開藥 。 」 而我們只有非常非常少的醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有採取措施 , 我們沒有採取任何措施 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去看護士和助產士 , 他們也是女人 , 在解釋如何使用藥丸上 , 我做了一個很棒的工作 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	那很美好 , 但它只佔了國家的20% 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們為另外百分之八十的人做了什麼 ? 然後說: 「 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不行 , 我們決定多做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	於是我們找來了你們看到的普通人
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	在這黃色標牌下面--我希望他們還沒擦到那個 , 因為那裡有 「 可口可樂 」 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	我們當時是比可口可樂還要大很多 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們選的人是我們選的對象 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區中相當知名 , 他們知道顧客永遠是對的 , 他們非常的棒 , 他們自己執行節育計畫 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以供應避孕藥和保險套到整個國家的每個村莊 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 我們在那裡 。 我們去找那些被視為問題的成因的人 , 成為解決方案 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論是哪裡 , 你都能看到船上的女人 , 賣東西 , 這裡是漂浮市場 , 賣香蕉和螃蟹 , 還有避孕用品 , 不論你在泰國哪裡找人 , 你都能找到避孕用品 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	接著 , 我們決定 , 為何不宗教呢 ? 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教會相當堅強 , 泰國人也是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們 , 他們說: 「 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我是藍色的 , 而不是黃色的 , 手持著一碗聖水 , 讓僧侶在避孕藥和保險套上灑滿整個家庭的神聖水 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	這張照片傳到全國各地
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	所以有些村莊的僧侶也自行做同樣的事情 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	女人都說: " 難怪我們沒有副作用 。
it's been blessed . "	被祝福了 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的認知 。
and then we went to teachers .	然後去找老師們
you need everybody to be involved in trying to provide whatever it is that make humanity a better place .	你需要每一個人參與 , 試圖提供任何能讓人類變得更好的東西 。
so we went to the teachers .	所以我們去找老師們
over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過25萬人教導了家庭計劃加上新字母a、b、出生、c、保險套、iud、v為輸精管切除術
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	然後我們有了一條蛇和梯子遊戲 , 來丟骰子 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你在任何理想的規劃上登陸 , 你就往前走 。
like , " mother takes the pill every night .	像是: 「 媽媽每晚服藥 ,
very good , mother . move ahead .	很好 , 媽媽 。 往前走 。
uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	舅舅會買保險套 。 很好 , 舅舅 。 往前走 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	走到 " 舅舅喝醉了 , 不使用保險套 。 再來一次 "
again , education , class entertainment .	同樣是教育、階級娛樂

in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對窮苦人家來說 , 鑽石不算 , 所以保險套就是女孩的好朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年引進微型貸款計畫 , 負責這項計畫的女性說: 「 我們只想借給有執行節育計畫的女性 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 就照顧自己的懷孕 。
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果沒有懷孕 , 就可以從我們這裡取得貸款 。 」
and that was run by them .	而那是由他們經營的
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	過了35/36年仍然持續著
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村莊發展銀行的一部分 ; 它不是真的銀行 , 而是一筆基金小額貸款 。
and we didn't need a big organization to run it it was run by the villagers themselves .	我們不需要一個龐大的組織來運作 , 由村民自己執行 。
and you probably hardly see a thai man there , it's always women , women , women , women .	你可能很少看到泰國男子在那裡 , 總是有女人、女人、女人 。

and this is on the fourth of july .	這是七月四日 。

and then the food is either hamburger or hotdog . "	然後食物要不就是漢堡 , 要不就是熱狗 。 」

but it's everybody's job who can change attitude and behavior .	但這是每個人的工作都能改變態度和行為 。
then aids came along and hit thailand , and we had to stop doing a lot of good things to fight aids .	接著 , 愛滋病也來到泰國 , 我們不得不停止對抗愛滋病 ,

these are primary school kids third , fourth grade going to every household in the village , every household in the whole of thailand , giving aids information and a condom to every household , given by these young kids .	這些是小學三、四年級的孩子 , 去村子裡的每戶人家 , 整個泰國的每戶人家 , 給每戶一個愛滋病的資訊和保險套 , 由這些小孩子提供 。

we had condoms in all the refrigerators in the hotels and the schools , because alcohol impairs judgment .	我們在飯店及學校裡都裝了保險套 , 因為酒精很容易判斷

and then we decided to help people out of poverty , now that we got aids somewhat out of the way this time , not with government alone , but in cooperation with the business community .	接著 , 我們決定要幫助人們脫離貧窮 , 現在我們已經脫離了愛滋病──這次不是政府單獨合作 , 而是與商業界合作 。
because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為貧窮的人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能和信用能力 。
those are the things to be provided by the business community .	那些是由企業界提供的
we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試著把他們變成赤足企業家 , 小生意人 。
the only way out of poverty is through business enterprise .	脫離貧窮的唯一方法就是透過企業
so , that was done .	這樣就完成了 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	公司投入資金 , 透過村莊植樹的錢 ,
it's not a free gift .	這可不是免費的禮物
they plant the trees , and the money goes into their microcredit fund , which we call the village development bank .	他們種植樹木 , 金錢就到他們的小額貸款基金中 , 我們稱它為村莊發展銀行 。
everybody joins in , and they feel they own the bank , because they have brought the money in .	所有人都加入 , 他們覺得自己擁有銀行 , 因為他們把錢帶進去 。
and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	而在你可以借錢之前 , 你需要先接受訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信 , 如果你想要幫助窮人 , 那些生活在貧窮中的人 , 信用能力就必須要成為一種人權 。
access to credit must be a human right .	信用能力必須要成為一種人權 。
otherwise they'll never get out of poverty .	否則他們永遠脫離不了貧窮 。
and then before getting a loan , you must be trained .	然後在取得貸款之前 , 你必須先接受訓練 。
here's what we call a " barefoot mba , " teaching people how to do business so that , when they borrow money , they'll succeed with the business .	這是我們所謂的 「 赤腳企管碩士班 」 , 教導人們如何做生意 , 如此一來 , 等他們借到錢後 , 他們就會成功地做生意 。
these are some of the businesses: mushrooms , crabs , vegetables , trees , fruits , and this is very interesting nike ice cream and nike biscuits ; this is a village sponsored by nike .	這些是一些生意:蘑菇、螃蟹、蔬菜、樹木、水果 。 這是非常有趣的 , nike冰淇淋和nike餅乾 。 這是由nike贊助的村莊 。
they said , " they should stop making shoes and clothes .	他們說: 「 他們應該停止做鞋子和衣服 。
make these better , because we can afford them . "	讓這些變得更好 , 因為我們負擔得起 。 」
and then we have silk , thai silk .	然後我們有泰國絲綢 。

so anyone sitting in and watching tv , get in touch with me .	所以任何坐著看電視的人 , 要和我聯絡 。

and then now , finally in education , we want to change the school as being underutilized into a place where it's a lifelong learning center for everyone .	最後 , 在教育上 , 我們希望改變學校原本沒被充分利用 , 成為每個人一生的學習中心 。

and it's a center , a focal point for economic and social development .	它是一個中心 , 一個經濟和社會發展的焦點 。
