your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧手機可能覺得自己像朋友 , 但真正的朋友 , 偶爾會給你微笑 , 在ted2013年 , 凱勒•里納多•狄摩斯羅摩 , 智慧手機驅動的迷你機器人 , 可以跟你一起散步 , 滑行一下 , 一杯咖啡跨桌 , 用可程式化的表達方式來對你做出反應 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	kellerrinaudo:一個迷你機器人 , 由你的手機驅動 。
so just by a show of hands , how many of you all have a robot at home ?	舉個手 , 有多少人家裡有機器人 ?
not very many of you .	沒多少人
okay . and actually of those hands , if you don't include roomba how many of you have a robot at home ?	好吧 。 其實那些手 , 如果你不包含roomba-有多少人在家裡有機器人 ?
that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這就是我們romotive公司試圖去解決的問題我和其他20位romotive的書呆子都沉迷於解決問題
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以我們真的很想打造一個人都可以用的機器人不管你是八歲還是八十歲
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 那真的是很困難的問題 , 因為要做出一個小巧、可攜式的機器人 , 它不僅是真正負擔得起的 , 而且必須是人們真的想要帶回家 , 繞過孩子的 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這個飛行器不能令人毛骨悚然或不可思議 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該是友善和可愛的
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo這個機器人 , 使用一種你已經知道且很愛你的iphone , 做為他的大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	藉由iphone處理器的力量我們可以創造出一個機器人 , 無線上網可以完成電腦視覺辨識的能力 , 大約是過去這類機器人的150美元所花費的百分之一 。
when romo wakes up , he's in creature mode .	當romo被喚醒時 , 他也在生物模式中
so he's actually using the video camera on the device to follow my face .	所以他其實在使用裝置上的錄影機來追蹤我的臉 。
if i duck down , he'll follow me .	如果我蹲下 , 他會跟著我 。
he's wary , so he'll keep his eyes on me .	他很警戒 , 所以他會一直盯著我看 。
if i come over here , he'll turn to follow me .	如果我走到這邊 , 他會轉身跟著我 。
if i come over here he's smart .	如果我來到這裡他很聰明
and if i get too close to him , he gets scared just like any other creature .	如果我太靠近他 , 他會感到害怕 , 就像任何其他生物一樣 。
so in a lot of ways , romo is like a pet that has a mind of his own .	所以在很多方面 , romo像是一隻有自己想法的寵物
thanks , little guy .	謝謝 , 小傢伙 。
and if i want to explore the world uhoh , romo's tired if i want to explore the world with romo , i can actually connect him from any other ios device .	如果我想要探索世界--呃-哦 , romo累了--如果我想要和romo一起探索這個世界 , 我真的可以和任何ios的設備做連結 。
so here's the ipad .	所以這裡是ipad
and romo will actually stream video to this device .	romo會真的把視訊串流到這個設備上 。
so i can see everything that romo sees , and i get a robot'seyeview of the world .	所以我可以看見romo看到的一切 , 我得到機器人的視野 。
now this is a free app on the app store , so if any of you guys had this app on your phones , we could literally right now share control of the robot and play games together .	這在appstore中是一個免費的應用程式 , 所以如果你們有人在手機上安裝這個應用程式 , 我們現在可以共同控制這個機器人 , 並且一起玩遊戲 。
so i'll show you really quickly , romo actually he's streaming video , so you can see me and the entire ted audience .	所以我很快地秀給你們看 , romo實際上他在串流影片 , 所以你們可以看到我和全部ted觀眾 。
if i get in front of romo here .	如果我來到romo這邊
and if i want to control him , i can just drive .	如果我想要控制他 , 我就開車 。
so i can drive him around , and i can take pictures of you .	所以我可以開車載他到處走 , 我可以幫你拍照 。
i've always wanted a picture of a 1 , 500person ted audience .	我一直都想要有一張有1 , 500人的ted觀眾的照片 。
so i'll snap a picture .	所以我拍了一張照片 。
and in the same way that you scroll through content on an ipad , i can actually adjust the angle of the camera on the device .	就跟你在ipad上滑動操作時一樣 , 我真的可以調整這裝置上攝影機角度 。
so there are all of you through romo's eyes .	所以你們全部透過romo的眼睛
and finally , because romo is an extension of me , i can express myself through his emotions .	最後 , 因為romo像是我的延伸 , 我可以透過他的情緒表達我自己 。
so i can go in and i can say let's make romo excited .	所以我可以進去說 , 讓我們來讓romo興奮一下 。
but the most important thing about romo is that we wanted to create something that was literally completely intuitive .	但關於romo最重要的事是我們想要創造完全直覺的東西 。
you do not have to teach someone how to drive romo .	你不需要教人如何駕駛romo 。
in fact , who would like to drive a robot ?	事實上 , 有誰願意來駕駛機器人呢 ?
thank you , scott .	謝謝你 , 史考特 。
and even cooler , you actually don't have to be in the same geographic location as the robot to control him .	更酷的是 , 你其實不必和機器人處在同一個地理位置來控制他 。
so he actually streams twoway audio and video between any two smart devices .	所以他實際上是任意兩個智慧型設備之間做雙向音訊和視訊串流 。
so you can log in through the browser , and it's kind of like skype on wheels .	所以你可以透過瀏覽器來登入 , 這有點像skype在輪子上操作 。
so we were talking before about telepresence , and this is a really cool example .	所以我們之前談到遠端臨場感 , 這是一個很酷的例子 。
you can imagine an eightyearold girl , for example , who has an iphone , and her mom buys her a robot .	舉例來說 , 你可以想像一個八歲大的女孩 , 她有iphone , 而她媽媽買給她一個機器人 。
that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那個女孩可以拿著她的iphone , 把它放在機器人上 , 寄一封電子郵件給住在國家另一端的奶奶 。
grandma can log into that robot and play hideandgoseek with her granddaughter for fifteen minutes every single night , when otherwise she might only be able to get to see her granddaughter once or twice a year .	奶奶可以登入那個機器人 , 和她的孫女一起玩捉迷藏 。 每晚十五分鐘 , 否則她一年可能只能去看她的孫女一兩次 。
so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	所以這些是romo今天能做的幾個很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但最後我要談的是我們在未來正在努力的方向
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這是我們其中一位工程師 , dom , 週末建成的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它是建立在google一個叫做blockly的開放框架上的 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這可以讓你拖拉這些部分的語義代碼 , 創造任何你想要這個機器人的行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何編碼才能創造romo行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	你實際上可以在瀏覽器中去模擬這個行為 , 這是你看到romo在左邊做的事情 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以下載到你的機器人 , 在現實生活中執行它 , 在現實生活中執行該程式 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	接著 , 如果你有什麼值得讓你驕傲的你可以和世界上其他擁有機器人的人分享 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所以 , 所有這些有線網路的機器人 , 其實會彼此學習 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們之所以這麼專注於製造出能訓練所有人的機器人 , 是因為我們認為在個人機器人中 , 最能引人注目的用途是個人的 。
they change from person to person .	它們會因人而異 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以 , 我們認為 , 如果你要在你的家中有一個機器人 , 那個機器人應該是你個人想像力的一種表現 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	所以我希望我能告訴你們個人機器人的未來是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我也不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們確實知道的是 , 它不是十年、十年 , 或一百億美元 , 也不是一個大型的人型機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	個人機器人的未來就在發生 , 它取決於體積小且敏捷的機器人 , 像romo這樣還有像你們一樣的人的創造力 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以我們等不及把你們全部的機器人送進來 , 我們也等不及要看看你們所建造的成果 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和社會運動家伊莎貝爾.阿言德討論女性、創意、女性主義的定義 , 當然 , 還有在這場演說中充滿熱情的議題 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂 , 全球議題 , 愛情 , 養育孩子 , 說故事的女人 , 世界文化
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾.阿言德講述關於熱情的故事
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常謝謝你們 。 真的很害怕在這位最聰明的人當中 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我在這裡要告訴大家幾個關於熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有個猶太人說我喜歡
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	比真理更真誠的是什麼 ? 答案就是:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是一個說故事的人 。 我想要傳達一個比事實更真誠的東西 , 關於我們共通的人性 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都引起我的興趣 , 有些故事直到我寫下它們為止 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	有些主題不斷出現:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治及社會議題 , 自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我意識到我們周圍的神秘之處所以我書寫巧合、預兆感情、夢想、大自然的力量、魔力
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年裡 , 我出版了幾本書 , 但是我一直活在匿名中 , 直到2006年2月 , 那時我背負著義大利冬季奧運時的奧運旗幟 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我成了名人 。 現在人們認可我在梅西百貨 , 我的孫子們都覺得我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	讓我告訴你們我的名氣的四分鐘
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	一名籌辦奧運開幕式的籌辦人打電話通知我獲選成為護旗者之一
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回覆說 , 這當然是一個錯誤的身分認同案例 , 因為我是你從運動員那頭到尾的 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	事實上 , 我甚至不確定自己能在球場中穿梭不用助行器 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	有人告訴我這不是開玩笑
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這將是第一次 , 只有女性會帶著奧運旗幟 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五位女性 , 代表五大洲 , 三位奧運金牌得主 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我第一個問題是 , 很自然地 , 我會穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	她說制服 , 要求我的量測 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我對我自己有遠見 , 穿著蓬鬆緊身衣 , 看起來像個米其林人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了二月中 , 我在杜林 , 那裡充滿熱情的群眾歡呼當80個奧運代表隊出現在街頭 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些運動員犧牲了要在遊戲中競爭的一切 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	都值得贏 , 但還是有好運的元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	雪上的一小塊 , 一英吋的冰 , 風的力量 , 可以決定比賽的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 什麼比訓練或運氣更重要 , 就是心臟 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼且堅定的心才能獲得金牌 。
it is all about passion .	這一切都與熱情有關 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	杜林街上滿是紅色海報上面印著奧運標語 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情就在這裡 。 不見得都是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心是驅動我們、決定我們的命運的動力
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這就是我書中角色所需要的:充滿熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要 「 獨行俠 」 , 異議者 , 冒險家 , 外人和叛亂者 , 他們會問問題 , 他們會規則並冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座各位一樣的人們
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	常識的好人並不會做有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	他們只會作出好的前配偶 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育場的綠色房間裡 , 我遇見了其他護旗手:三位運動員 , 還有演員蘇珊薩蘭登和蘇菲雅羅蘭 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	還有兩位心中充滿熱情的女性:來自肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主 , 栽種了三千萬棵樹 。 如此一來 , 她改變了土壤、天氣 , 在非洲的某些地方 , 當然也改變了許多村莊的經濟狀況 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	還有柬埔寨活動家索瑪利•瑪瑪 , 他以熱情的方式對抗童工妓女 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	14歲時 , 她祖父把她賣到妓院
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 小女孩在那被男人強暴那些人相信跟年紀很小的處女做愛可以治好愛滋病
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	而小妓院裡 , 孩子們被迫每天接客5、15個 , 如果他們反叛 , 就會被用電折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在我收到制服的綠色房間裡
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	那不是我平常穿的那種服裝 , 但那服裝離我預期的米其林男裝還很遠 。 其實不錯 , 真的 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像個冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	但其他護旗手也一樣 , 除了蘇菲雅羅蘭它是美麗與熱情的普遍象徵
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲雅超過70歲 , 她看起來也很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她性感、渺小、身高過、帶著深長的劍 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	現在 , 你怎麼可以有一支深色皮膚而且沒有皺紋呢 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當電視記者問: 「 她怎麼能這麼好看 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回: 「 保持好的姿勢 。 我的背總是直的 , 我不發出老人的噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	這裡有一些免費的建議 , 來自地球上最美的女性之一 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	不貪婪、咳嗽、氣喘不自言自語、不放屁
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她並沒有說完全如此 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	到了約午夜時分 , 我們被叫到體育場的翅膀上 , 擴音器宣佈了奧運會旗 。 順帶一提 , 音樂也是從這裡開始的 , 阿依達遊行 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲雅羅蘭就在我面前--她比我高一呎 , 不算輕便的頭髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她優雅地走著 , 就像非洲草原上的長頸鹿將旗子的一角舉在肩上 。 我則在後面小跑步 , 手臂舉著國旗 。 這樣我的頭其實在那面該死的旗子下面 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	所有的相機當然都是在蘇菲雅上
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	這對我來說很幸運 , 因為在大部分我出現的照片中 , 雖然常常是出現在蘇菲雅的雙腿之間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	一個多數男人都很想待的地方
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最精彩的四分鐘就是那些在奧運體育館裡的人 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	我老公很生氣 , 當我說這句話時雖然我曾向他解釋 , 我們私下作的事通常花不到4分鐘 , 所以他不應該親自動手 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我擁有那四分鐘的所有剪報因為我不想忘記他們當年老時腦細胞壞了
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想永遠背負著熱情的關鍵字
so here's a tale of passion .	以下是個充滿熱情的故事
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	時間是1998年 , 地點為剛果的圖西族難民營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順帶一提 , 世界上80%的難民及流民都是婦女及女童 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以在剛果稱這個地方為死亡集中營 , 因為沒有被殺的人 , 將會死於疾病或飢餓 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	故事的主角是一名年輕女性蘿絲•瑪班多和她的孩子們
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕了而且還是寡婦 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵迫使她目睹她的丈夫被虐待和殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知怎麼的 , 她竟然讓她7個孩子活了下來 , 幾個月後 , 她就生下雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用棍子自己割斷臍帶然後用頭髮把斷口綁起來
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她用營地的指揮官的名字取名字 , 以取得他們的恩惠 , 再用黑色茶餵他們 , 因為她的牛奶無法維持 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵闖進她的牢房以強暴她大女兒時 , 她緊抓著她 , 拒絕放手 , 即使他們拿著槍抵著她的頭 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎的 , 這家人存活了16個月然後 , 靠著絕佳的運氣和美國年輕男子薩夏•查洛夫的熱心他成功地將她送上美國救援機蘿絲和她的九個孩子最後到了亞利桑那州鳳凰城在那裡生活、成長茁壯
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	瑪班多在斯瓦希里語中 , 意味著偉大的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我書中的主角都是堅強且富熱情的女性就像蘿絲•瑪班多
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不編造它們 , 不需要這些 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 隨處可見 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一生都在研究女性和女性 。
i know them well .	我對他們很了解 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生在遠古時代 , 在世界末日 , 在一個父權天主教及保守家庭中 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪到了五歲我是個狂熱的女權主義者雖然這個名詞還沒到智利因此沒人知道我到底怎麼了
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就發現 , 為我的自由付出極大代價 , 以及質疑父權制度 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我高興地付出代價 , 因為每當我被擊中一擊 , 我就能夠遞送兩次 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有次 , 我二十多歲的女兒寶拉她對我說女權運動過時了 , 我應該繼續走下去 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們經歷了一場令人難忘的戰鬥 。 女權主義約會嗎 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 對於像我女兒這一類的有特權的女性 , 今天在這裡的我們所有人 , 但不是給世界上大部分的姊妹們 , 她們仍然被逼著婚前、妓女、強迫勞動她們要的孩子不要 , 或她們不能養育 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們無法掌控自己的身體或人生 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有受過教育也沒有自由
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們會被強暴、毆打 , 有時還會因為懲罰而被殺 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	對於現今大多數西方年輕女性來說 , 被稱為 「 女性主義者 」 是種侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女權從來沒有很性感 , 但讓我保證我從來沒有因此停止調情過 , 我也很少有缺乏男性的陪伴 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女性主義沒有死 , 絕對不會 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	已經進化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個名詞就改了它 , 換成女神之名 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱它為芙若蒂 , 或維納斯 , 或bimbo , 隨便你想得到的名字都無所謂 , 只要我們了解它的本質 , 且我們支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	這裡還有另一個關於熱情的故事 , 也是悲傷的故事 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	這地方是孟加拉的一個小婦女診所
the year is 2005 .	這一年是2005年
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是個年輕的美國衛生專家 , 她到診所當義工 , 在度假期間 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她已經準備好要乾淨牙齒了 , 但當她到了那裡 , 她發現那裡沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所只是滿是蒼蠅的小屋 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	外面站著排隊的一堆婦女等了好幾個小時才接受治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一個病人痛苦難當 , 因為她好幾顆腐爛的臼齒 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮發現唯一的解決方案就是拔掉壞牙 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她沒有執照 , 她從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她常常去冒險 , 她很害怕 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她沒有合適的儀器 , 幸好她帶來了一些麻醉藥 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有顆勇敢而熱情的心
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她默默禱告 , 然後開始營運 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 病患吻了她的手 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天衛生人員多拔牙
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	第二天早上 , 當她再次來到所謂的診所時她的第一個病人跟丈夫在那邊等她
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	這位女士的臉看起來像是個西瓜 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	腫到看不見眼睛
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	老公 , 憤怒 , 威脅要殺害美國人 ,
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮被自己造成的後果嚇壞了 , 但翻譯解釋說病人的狀況和手術無關 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她丈夫因為她沒有準時回家為他準備晚餐 。
millions of women live like this today .	現今有數百萬名女性都這樣生活 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是窮人中最窮的
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然全世界有三分之二的勞動力 , 但卻擁有不到1%的全球資產 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	她們與男人同工 , 薪資卻較低如果她們有薪水可領 , 而且她們仍然是脆弱的因為她們沒有經濟獨立性而且經常受到剝削、暴力和虐待的威脅
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	這是一項給予女性教育、工作、掌控自己收入的能力、繼承及擁有財產的事實 , 對社會有益 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一個女人有力量 , 她的孩子和家人就會過得更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家庭繁榮 , 村落也會繁榮 , 最終整個國家也是如此 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	旺加里•瑪太到肯亞的村落
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她跟婦女談話並解釋土地已經貧瘠因為他們砍了樹賣了
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓女人們種植新的樹木 , 然後澆水 , 一滴接著一滴 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	在短短的五或六年之內 , 他們有森林 , 土壤豐富了 , 村落也拯救了 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮及最落後的社會總是那些壓迫女性的社會 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	但這個顯而易見的事實卻被政府忽略同時也被慈善家所忽視
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	女性相關計畫每得到1美元就有20美元給男性相關計畫
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性佔人類總數的51%
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	給予他們力量 , 不僅是科技、設計和娛樂 , 還能改變一切 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以保證 , 女性合作的女性會連結、通知 , 及受過教育 , 能為這個被告知的星球帶來和平與繁榮 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	在今天的任何戰爭中 , 大部分的傷亡者是平民 , 主要是婦女和兒童 。 她們是附帶損壞 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人掌控世界 , 再看看我們現有的亂象
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要怎樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是我們大多數人都在問的基本問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	參加現有的世界秩序合理嗎 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們要一個保存生命的世界一個生活品質能夠豐富每個人 , 不只是特權
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	一月時我看到費南多•巴特羅的畫展在柏克萊大學圖書館
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	在美國 , 沒有任何博物館或畫廊 , 除了紐約畫廊 , 那些畫攜帶著巴特羅的作品 , 大膽地展示這些畫作因為主題是發生虐囚事件的阿布格雷布監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	他們是大量的折磨及權力濫用的畫作 , 在大型的botero風格中 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我從來沒有辦法把那些影像從我心中或我的心中清出來 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最擔心的是無障礙的力量 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力 , 以及濫用權力
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們這個物種中 , 雄性領袖定義了現實 , 並迫使其餘的群體接受那樣的現實並遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則常常在改變 , 但總是對他們有好處 , 在這種情況下 , 「 下滲透效應 」 在經濟上行不通 , 效果完美 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	從上到下 , 一層層又一層 , 一觸即發 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	婦女和兒童 , 尤其是窮人 , 在最底層
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是最貧困的男人也有人可以虐待女人或小孩
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我受夠了少數幾個人透過性別、收入、種族和階級來消耗的力量 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為現在時機已經成熟 , 可以為我們的文明做出根本改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但 , 若要真正改變 , 我們需要女性的精力 , 在世界的管理當中 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要有權力地位的女性來教導男性中具女性力量的女性
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	我說的當然是年輕男性
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老男人毫無希望 , 我們必須等他們離世
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	沒錯 , 我很想擁有蘇菲雅羅蘭的長腿以及傳奇乳房 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但若要選的話 , 我寧願得到戰士的心臟是旺加里•瑪太、蘇曼麗•瑪雅、珍妮、蘿絲•瑪班多 。
i want to make this world good .	我想讓這個世界變得美好
not better , but to make it good .	不是比較好 , 而是要把它做好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不 ? 這是可能的 。 看看這間房間 , 所有的知識、能量、才華和科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	咱們來脫離我們的粉絲 , 捲起袖子上下工作 , 熱情地創建一個近乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在倫敦這麼大的城市中 , 三千萬份餐是從哪裡來的 ? 建築師卡羅琳•柯爾在每日討論如何養活一座城市的奇蹟 , 並顯示古代食物路線如何形塑現代社會 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	carolyn鋼鐵:食物如何塑造我們的城市
how do you feed a city ?	如何餵飽一個城市
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代最偉大的問題之一
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但很少被問到:
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們視為理所當然如果我們走進一家店或餐廳 , 或著是走進這間劇院的門廳 , 大概一個小時 , 那裡就會有食物在等著我們 , 魔法般地從某處出現 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你想像每天為倫敦這麼大的城市每天要有足夠的食物被製造、運輸、購買、販賣、煮、吃掉、丟棄 , 那類似的事情 , 每天都要發生 , 為了每個城市 , 都要有很大的差異 , 城市得以供應食物 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在這樣的地方 , 彷彿牠們是世界上最自然的東西 , 忘了這點 , 因為我們是動物 , 我們需要吃 , 其實跟我們的遠古祖先一樣依賴大自然 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著更多的我們搬進城市 , 越來越多的大自然被轉變為像是我身後的景色──在巴西馬托格羅索的大豆田 , 為了餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些非比尋常的景色但少有人見識過
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	越來越多的風景不只是用來餵飽我們 ,
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	更多人搬到城市裡 , 更多人在吃肉 , 所以全球每年的農作物有三分之一是拿去餵養動物 , 而不是拿來餵我們人類 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	而考量到需要三倍的穀物事實上是十倍的穀物如果用動物穿過的話這是很有效率的餵飽我們的方法
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是一個日趨嚴峻的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	估計到了2050年 , 我們居住的數量將會是城市的兩倍 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	同時估計也將有兩倍的肉品及乳製品消耗
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以 , 肉類和都市主義手握在手中 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將是個巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	要餵飽六十億個肉食性動物到2050年
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 。 如果我們繼續走下去 , 那會是一個我們無法解決的問題 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有一千九百萬公頃的熱帶雨林消失造成新的可耕地
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	雖然我們同時也失去相當大量的可耕地 , 讓土地鹽化和土地侵蝕 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也非常渴望石化燃料 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	在西方 , 每製造一卡路里的食物要耗去十卡路里的能量 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	儘管有些我們以極高成本生產出來的食物 , 卻不重視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	半數在美國生產的食品是會被丟掉的
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	要結束這一切 , 在這漫長過程的最後 , 我們甚至沒有管理好要讓地球有適當的食物 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	有十億人過胖 , 卻有十億人挨餓 。
none of it makes very much sense .	這一切都不太合理
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為現在全球百分之八十的食物交易只由五大跨國企業所控制那是個嚴峻的景象
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	隨著我們搬進城市 , 世界也在擁抱西方的飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看向未來 , 這是不永續的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	所以 , 我們怎麼會變成這樣 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們對此該怎麼辦 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	嗯 , 先回答稍微容易一點的問題 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說是這個過程的開端 , 在古老的近東地區 , 也就是所謂的肥沃新世代 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它是近代的形狀 。
and it was also fertile .	而且它很肥沃 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約在一萬年前 , 在這裡有兩項非凡的發明農業和城市的產生大約在同一地點同一時間
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這並非偶然 , 因為農業和城市緊密相連 。 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為這是我們遠古祖先第一次發現穀物的來源足以維持永久居住的食物來源
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看這些居住地的樣子 , 我們會發現它們很緊密 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們的周圍有農田並以一大型神殿為中心例如這一個在烏爾的神殿在當時是神聖化的中央食物分配中心
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為是神殿安排好收成 , 收集在穀物上 , 將之送給神 , 接著提供了那些神不吃回來的穀物 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 若你願意 , 這些城市的精神和實體生活都是由養育它們的穀物和收成所支配 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 每個古代的城市都是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但並非全部都這麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	著名的是 , 羅馬在西元一世紀前大約有一百萬的公民
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以 , 像這樣的城市是怎麼來的 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案就是我所謂的 「 古代食物里程 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬得以進入大海 , 這使得羅馬能夠從很遠的地方 , 食指進口食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是在遠古時期 , 唯一可能做到這一點的方式 , 因為用公路運送食物是非常困難的 , 不太可能 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	而且食物很快就壞掉 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以羅馬有效地對地方發動戰爭 , 像是在他們的穀物保護區和埃及發動戰爭 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 整個帝國的擴張其實是個長期有計劃的軍事化的購物活動 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上我喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提到羅馬事實上是用來進口 " 牡蠣 " 來自倫敦的一個階段我覺得這很不平凡
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬靠著食慾塑造了它的內陸 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 另一件事也發生在工業化前的世界 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看十七世紀的倫敦地圖 , 我們可以看到 , 它的穀物是從泰晤士河運進來的 , 在這張地圖的下方 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以穀物市場到了城市的南方 ,
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	而通往廉價的道路也是主要市場的穀物市場
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看看其中一條街道的名稱 , 麵包街 , 你可以判斷三百年前那裡的狀況 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	當然 , 魚也是一樣 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚也是河裡來的 。 同樣的道理 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然比林斯門很有名的是倫敦的魚市場一直到1980年代中期都還在使用
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	仔細想想 , 這很不尋常 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	其他人都跟著手機閒逛 , 看起來像磚塊一般 , 有點像港口裡有魚的臭味 ,
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是另一個與城市有關的食物:一旦它的根基被建立起來 , 它們幾乎不會移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉類是非常不同的 , 因為 , 當然 , 動物也能走進城市 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	所以倫敦的大部分肉品是從西北方來的從蘇格蘭及威爾斯
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以它來了 , 抵達西北部的城市也就是為什麼史密斯菲爾德倫倫敦著名的肉市場 , 便在那裏
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	家禽類從東安格利亞諸如此類到東北方
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得有點像天氣女子 , 不管怎樣 , 鳥兒也來了 , 腳上還帶著小畫布的鞋子 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	接著 , 當他們撞到廉價商品的東端時 , 那是他們被賣掉的地方 , 這就是為什麼它叫做 「 波爾特里 」 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看任何城市的地圖在工業化前就可以看到食物跑出來的痕跡
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你可以確實地看到它是如何被食物所塑造的 , 不論是看過街道的名稱 , 這給你很大的線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 在以前是你在星期五去買魚的地方 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但你也必須想像 , 它充滿了食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街上和公共空間是買賣食物唯一的場所
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看1830年史密斯菲爾德的圖片你會發現 , 生活在這樣的一個城市裡是非常困難的並且不清楚你的食物從哪裡來
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你在吃禮拜日午餐時 , 很可能在你的窗戶外面大便或流血 , 大約三天前 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	所以 , 這顯然是個有機城市 , 有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	十年後一切都改變了
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年大西部的圖像
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	你可以看到 , 最早的火車旅客中有一些是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	所以 , 突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	牠們在眼不見心為淨的情況下被屠宰在鄉下的某處
and they're coming into the city by rail .	而且是用鐵路帶進城市
and this changes everything .	而這會改變一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	從頭開始 , 第一次種植城市 , 任何大小和形狀 , 在任何地方都是如此 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	過去城市受限於地理的限制 ; 過去它們必須用非常困難的身體手段來取得食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 它們從地域上被大量地分解了 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	從倫敦的這些地圖可以看出在火車到來的九十年後倫敦從一個容易餵飽的小區塊看出去由動物走進來餵飽的食物例如 , 一個很大的場所那裡很難養活任何人不是動物或人
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然這只是個開端 。 火車之後又來了汽車 , 這真的讓這過程結束了 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	它是城市最終的解放完全由大自然所組成
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這種城市沒有嗅覺 , 沒有混亂 , 沒有人肯定會失去人 , 因為沒有人會夢想能走在這樣的地景上 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們獲得食物的做法是他們上車 , 開車到郊區的一個箱子 , 帶著一個星期的購物回來 , 想知道要用它來做什麼 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	這是我們與食物及城市的關係完全改變的時刻 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡我們有以前是中心的食物 , 是城市的社會核心 , 在邊緣地帶 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	以前是社交活動 , 買賣食物、
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們曾經做菜 ; 現在只要加水 , 或加點卵 , 如果你要做蛋糕之類的 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們聞不到食物 , 看東西有沒有用 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只是讀了包裝背上的標籤 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	而且我們不重視食物 , 我們不信任
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不再信任它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	我們不再重視它 , 而是把它丟掉 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代飲食習慣有個很棒的諷刺就是他們承諾要讓事情變得更容易 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	透過在任何地方、任何地方 , 都有可能建造城市 , 它們其實已經把我們和最重要的關係保持距離 , 即 「 我們 」 和 「 自然 」 的關係 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	而且它們也使我們依賴只有它們能傳遞的系統 。 正如我們所見 , 它們是無法永續的 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	所以 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是個新的問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前湯瑪斯•摩爾就在問他自己
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他的書《烏托邦》的首集 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	那是一系列半自給自足的城邦 , 如果聽起來很熟悉的話 , 每天走的路 , 基本上每個人都是耕種人 , 在他們的後院種蔬菜 , 一起享用餐點等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我想大家可以爭辯說 , 食物是烏托邦的根本原則 , 即使更多人從未這樣形容它 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	還有另一個著名的 「 烏托邦 」 的願景是埃本内則•霍華德 , 「 花園城市 」 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的想法:一系列半自給自足的城邦 , 小小的都會區 , 周圍有可耕地的土地 , 通過鐵路連接彼此 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	再一次地 , 食物可以被說是他視覺的原則
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至已經建好了 , 但與霍華的願景無關 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	那就是這些烏托邦理念的問題他們是烏托邦
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦的確是湯瑪斯.摩爾刻意使用的字眼
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	這是個笑話 , 因為它有著希臘文的雙重導向 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可以是好地方 , 也可以是不存在的地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為它是理想的、想像出來的、我們無法擁有它
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 作為一個概念 , 用來思考人類居住的深刻問題 , 使得它沒什麼用處 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以 , 我提出了一個替代方案 , 也就是希托邦 , 來自古希臘的 「 sitos 」 , 即 「 食物 」 , 以及 「 topos 」 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經生活在希托邦
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個由食物形狀的世界 , 如果我們意識到 , 我們能用食物來當作強大的工具--一個概念性的工具 , 設計工具 , 用不同的方式來塑造這個世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以如果我們這樣做 , 希托邦會是什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	我覺得它看起來有點像這樣 。
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我必須用這張投影片 , 只是看到狗的臉
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	總之 , 這是生命的中心食物是家庭生活的中心 , 被讚頌、被享受 , 人們花時間在這上面 。
this is where food should be in our society .	這才是我們社會中食物應有的地位 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但你不能有這樣的場景 , 除非你有人這樣 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順帶一提 , 這些也可以是男性
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	而是一些人會想到食物 , 他們會預先思考 , 他們會盯著一堆最生食的蔬菜 , 實際認出它們 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 , 我們是某網路的一部分
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為如果沒有這一類的人我們不可能有這樣的地方
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	在這裡 , 我故意選這個 , 因為這是男人在買菜 。
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但是網絡 , 那些地方食物正在成長的市場
it's common . it's fresh .	很常見 , 很新鮮
it's part of the social life of the city .	是城市社交生活的一部分
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為如果沒有了 , 你就無法擁有這樣的地方 , 本地種植的食物 , 同時也是景觀的一部分 , 不只是一個零和的商品脫離了一些看不見的地獄 。
cows with a view .	牛的視角
steaming piles of humus .	堆積如山的蜂巢 ,
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	這基本上是把整個東西結合在一起
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近在多倫多參觀的一個社區計畫 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	這是一座溫室 , 孩子們會被全部關於食物的知識 , 及自己種的食物 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有一株叫做凱文的植物 , 或許它是屬於 「 凱文 」 的孩子的植物 。 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	但無論如何 , 這類企圖要把我們與大自然再度連結的計畫極其重要 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 希托邦 , 對我來說 , 真的是一種看待的方式 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上認知到希托邦已經存在於任何地方的小口袋裡了 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	秘訣是要加入他們 , 用食物當作一種觀看的方式 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這樣做 , 我們將不再將城市看成是大的、都會的、沒生產力的區塊 , 就像這樣 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們會更常看到它們 , 把它們當作有生產力、有機框架的一部分 , 將它們無可避免地連結在一起 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	當然這也不是很好的形象因為我們不需要再這樣生產糧食了
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要多考量栽培 , 這也是為什麼我認為這張圖為我總結出我們需要做的那種思考 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	是對食物塑造我們生活的方式重新概念化
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道最棒的圖像來自650年前 。
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	是安布洛吉歐.羅倫澤提的 " 良好政府的寓言 "
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	和城市和鄉間的關係
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這件事的訊息是非常清楚的 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市照顧城市 , 國家會照顧城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	我現在想問問安布洛吉歐.羅倫澤提如果他今天畫了這張圖會用什麼顏料 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	當今的優秀政府的寓言會是怎樣的 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這個問題很迫切
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	這是我們得要問的 , 我們得要開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們吃的是
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要意識到 , 我們所吃的世界 ,
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們把這樣的想法 , 我們可以用食物來作為真正強大的工具 , 來改善世界 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	在《同情憲章》發表的幾週之後 , karenarmstrong研究了21世紀宗教的角色:它的教條會分裂我們嗎 ? 或者它會因為共同的利益把我們團結起來 ? 她會修改那些催化劑這些催化劑驅使世界信仰重新發現黃金法則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝、ted大獎、全球議題、政治、宗教、tedglobal2009 , 暴力、
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenarmstrong:讓我們重振黃金法則
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來我一直感到沮喪 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我敏銳地意識到同情心的核心 , 在所有主要世界的信仰中 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個都演化出他們自己的版本所謂的 「 黃金法則 」 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時候它的版本是正面的 「 全面的對待別人 」 , 如同你想被對待自己一樣 。
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面的版本 「 不要對他人做你不希望他們對你做的事 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看自己的心 , 發現痛苦是什麼 , 然後在任何情況下拒絕 , 在任何情況下 , 將這樣的痛苦加諸其它人身上 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	人們強調憐憫的重要性不只因為聽起來很好也因為它很有用
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們實施了黃金法則 , 如孔子說的: 「 不分日復一日 。 」 這個問題 , 不僅僅是做好自己一天的好事 , 還回到貪婪和自尊的生活中 , 而是一整天都在做 , 你把自己從世界的中心扮演出來 , 把另一個扮演出來 , 你超越了自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它把你帶到一個叫做神的東西 , 一個叫做nirvana , rama , 一個tao的樣子
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	一種超越我們熟知的自我存活的東西 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你從來都不知道這是宗教生活的核心
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有一些美好的例外 , 當宗教人士聚在一起 , 宗教領袖會聚在一起 , 他們會爭論到廢除的教條 , 或反駁仇恨的議會 , 或反對同性戀或同性戀的話題 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常人們不太願意有同情心
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到 , 當我在向一眾聚會的宗教人士致意時 , 一種互相矛盾的表情 , 橫跨他們的臉 , 因為人們通常會想要對的 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	這當然也違反了運動的本體 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	我為什麼感激ted ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們溫和地帶領我離開我的書房研究 , 帶我進入21世紀 , 讓我能夠和更廣大的觀眾說話 , 遠遠超過我所能想像的 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我覺得這件事情的急迫性
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們不設法在全球實行黃金法則 , 這樣我們就對所有人 , 不管他們在哪裡 , 不管他們是誰 , 只要他們跟自己一樣重要的話 , 我懷疑我們還能有一個可行的世界來傳遞給下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務 , 這個時代的偉大任務之一 , 就是建立一個全球性的社會 , 如同我所說的 , 人們可以和平共處 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而應該要做出重大貢獻的宗教卻被視為問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然 , 不只是有宗教信仰的人也相信黃金法則 。
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的源頭 , 這種富想像力的同理心 , 讓你自己置身於另一個人之處 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以我們有選擇 , 在我看來是這樣 。
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們可以繼續宣揚或強調我們信仰的教條或不寬容面向 , 或者我們可以回到拉比席勒爾 , 古老的耶穌的猶太教堂 , 當被異教徒叫來總結猶太教的教義 , 當他站在一條腿上 , 他說: 「 真恨你 , 別管你的鄰居 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	「 這就是教義 , 其他都只是評論 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	教堂的拉比和早期父親都說任何對經文的解讀只要帶有仇恨和鄙視的意味都是不正當的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	而我們需要復甦那精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	這不只會發生因為愛的精神喚醒了我們
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須讓這件事實現 , 而且我們可以跟ted介紹的現代溝通一同實現 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	對於我們所有夥伴 , 我已經感到無比振奮 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有個團體要用憲章來治癒新加坡社會最近出現的分歧 。 議會的一些成員也想要在政治上實施 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 將來會有一場藝術展 , 讓有領頭的藝術家帶領人們 , 年輕人 , 讓他們看到 , 同情心也是一切藝術的根源 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在整個歐洲 , 穆斯林社區舉辦活動和討論會 , 正在討論伊斯蘭教中的同情心中心 , 以及所有信仰中 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能停在這裡 。 它不能停止發射 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教的教誨 , 是我們錯了的地方 , 僅僅因為我們相信深奧的教義 ,
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教的教義必須一直引導著行動
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	而我打算在我快要死掉的時候繼續這一天工作 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	我也想繼續與我們的夥伴一起做兩件事 , 來教育及刺激同情心的思考 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育是因為我們如此地退出同情心 。
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們常覺得對不起
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但你當然不會理解同情心如果你只想著同情心
you also have to do it .	你也必須去做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望媒體能參與其中 , 因為媒體很重要 , 協助消除別人的成見 , 使我們彼此分化 。
the same applies to educators .	同樣的適用於教育家
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望青年能夠感受到一種有同情心的生活方式的活力和挑戰 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	同時也看到這需要敏銳的情報 , 而不是僅僅只是一種討厭的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想呼籲學者勇於探索自身和他人傳統中慈悲的主題 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	也許最重要的是 , 去鼓勵一種沒有同情心的敏感度 , 這麼一來 , 因為有這種憲章 , 不論他們的信仰為何 , 或缺乏他們的信仰 , 他們都覺得有能力去挑戰那些沒有同情心的言論 , 對他們的宗教領袖、他們的政治領袖 , 來自產業界的船長 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們可以改變世界 , 我們有能力
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我從來沒想過憲章會放在網路上 。
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我還困在舊世界裡 , 一大群人坐在房間中 , 同時又發出另一種神秘的聲明 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	ted讓我認識到一種全新的方式來思考和呈現想法 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為這是ted美妙的地方 。
in this room , all this expertise , if we joined it all together , we could change the world .	在這個房間裡 , 所有的專長 , 如果我們聯合起來 , 我們就可以改變世界 。
and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然 , 這些問題有時也無法解決 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	不過 , 我想引用一個英國作家一個牛津的作者 , 牛津的作者--我不太常引用--c.s.路易斯 。
but he wrote one thing that stuck in my mind ever since i read it when i was a schoolgirl .	但他寫的一件事 , 一直牢牢記在我讀到學校時的心靈 。
it's in his book " the four loves . "	在他的《四種愛》這本書中
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說 , 他區別出了愛情 , 當兩個人凝視彼此 , 為對方的眼神著迷 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	接著他把這與友情比較 , 當兩個人肩並肩地肩並肩 , 用雙眼固定在一個共同目標上 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不需要愛上彼此 , 但我們可以成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	我深信不疑
i felt it very strongly during our little deliberations at vevey , that when people of all different persuasions come together , working side by side for a common goal , differences melt away .	我強烈的感覺到它 , 在我們在veny的小小刻意下 , 當各種不同說服的人聚在一起 , 肩並肩地工作 , 為了共同的目標 , 差異就會消失 。
and we learn amity .	而我們學著 " 仁愛 " ,
and we learn to live together and to get to know one another .	而我們學著一起生活和認識彼此 。
thank you very much .	非常感謝 。

macarthur grant , art , arts , book , cities , communication , culture , design , entertainment , humor , storytelling	macarthur獎助、藝術、藝術、書、城市、溝通、文化、設計、娛樂、幽默、說故事 。

there's a very thin blue line of exhaust that sort of runs through this thing that would be kind of the trail that holds it all together .	有一條很細的藍色鐵線 , 它會貫穿整個東西 , 把所有東西連結在一起 。
then i thought , " wait a minute , what am i doing ? "	接著我想: 「 等等 , 我在做什麼 ? 」
a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	書不單是用整齊的方式來收集和儲存資訊 , 也要用一系列的層次 。
i mean , you always peel one layer off another ; we think of them as pages , doing it a certain way .	我的意思是 , 你總是把其中一層剝掉 ; 我們把它們看作頁面 , 以某種方式去做 。
but think of them as layers . i mean , rome is a place of layers horizontal layers , vertical layers and i thought , well just peeling off a page would allow me to if i got you thinking about it the right way would allow me to sort of show you the depth of layers .	但把它們看成是層次 。 我的意思是 , 羅馬是個有層次的水平地層 , 垂直地層 。 我心想 , 如果把頁面剝掉的話 , 可以讓我用正確的方式來思考 , 可以讓我向你們展示一些層次的深度 。
the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	羅馬的大多數建築物的牆面覆蓋著疤痕 ; 數世紀以來這些結構所適應的傷痕 , 而不是被拆掉 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左邊做一個摺疊頁 , 讓你可以將它展開 , 你就會看到我所謂的傷疤組織 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到在1635年 , 製造小窗戶的必要性 , 因為壞人要來了 , 或是其它種類 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	所有的適應作用都埋在粘核下
i could peel out a page of this palazzo to show you what's going on inside of it .	我可以從這張大猩猩的頁面透出讓大家看看裡面到底發生了什麼事
but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	更重要的是 , 我還可以讓你看看在這些壯麗的建築物的角落裡 , 有巨大的石塊 , 或用磚頭和石塊做成的假石塊 , 這些石塊更加常見 。
so it becomes slightly threedimensional .	因此 , 它變得略為立體 ,
i could take you down one of those narrow little streets into one of those surprising piazzas by using a double gate fold double foldout page which , if you were like me reading a popup book as a child , you hopefully stick your head into .	我可以把你從一條狹窄的小街上帶到一條令人驚訝的廣場 , 只要用一個雙扇摺疊頁 , 如果你和我一樣小時候看過立體書 , 你就會把你的頭伸進去 。
you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	你把頭上的紙包住 , 就在那短暫的時間裡 ,

here's a book completely wide open .	這裡有本書完全的開放
ok , if i don't open the book the whole way , if i just open it 90 degrees , we're looking down the front of the pantheon , and we're looking sort of at the top , more or less down on the square .	好 , 如果我不把書整個打開 , 如果我只是把它打開90度 , 我們沿著萬神殿的正面看著 , 正上方 , 或多或少在廣場上 。
and if i turn the book the other way , we're looking across the square at the front of the pantheon .	如果我把書換個角度來看 , 我們就在廣場的正面看著 。
no foldouts , no tricks just a book that isn't open the whole way .	沒有摺疊 , 沒有任何把戲--只是一本沒有完全打開的書 。
that seemed promising . i thought , maybe i'll do it inside and i can even combine the foldouts with the only partially opened book .	這看來很有前景 。 我想 , 也許我可以在裡面做 , 甚至可以把摺疊頁和唯一一部分開放的書結合起來 。
so we get inside the pantheon and it grows and so on and so forth .	我們進入萬神殿內部 , 它生長著 , 諸如此類 。
and i thought , maybe i'm on the right track , but it sort of lost its human quality .	我在想 , 也許我是站在正確的軌道上 , 但它好像失去了人類的特質 。
so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以我回頭看故事的概念 , 要是你試圖讓別人注意一本書 , 沿途取得資訊 , 一定是件好事 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進度 」 讓我印象深刻 。
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果牠是隻信鴿 , 牠就會被稱為 「 荷馬的奧德賽 」 。
but it was the journey of the . . .	但這卻是這趟旅程......
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我的意思是 , 如果一個頭銜有用 , 但它會是一趟旅程 , 穿越羅馬展示所有我喜歡的羅馬的東西 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	一隻鴿子坐在教堂的上方
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天起飛 , 做一些正常的鴿子 。 回來 , 整個地方都被鷹架和綠色防護網包覆 , 完全沒有辦法讓這只鴿子回家 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	所以現在是無家可歸的鴿子 , 牠還得找另一個住處 , 這讓我得以從我喜歡的東西的目錄下來 , 我們從高一些開始做起 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許牠必須回去和家人同住 ; 那不見得是好事 , 但牠的確會帶鴿子在一起 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我覺得這有點意思 , 但或許有一個人應該要以某種方式來參與這個活動 。
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想出了一個傢伙 , 終其一生都在照顧生病的鴿子 。
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會到任何地方 , 去把他們帶到危險的地方他們會和這個傢伙變成朋友並在午餐時間幫他做些把戲
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	有一個真實的鍵結在這個老人和這些鴿子之間發展出來
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但不幸的是 , 他病得很重 。 他病的很重 。
he's taught them to spell his name , which is aldo .	他教他們拼他的名字aldo
they show up one day after three or four days of not seeing him he lives in this little garret and they spell his name and fly around .	有一天 , 在三四天沒見到他之後 , 他住在這個小垃圾桶裡 , 他們拼他的名字 , 然後飛來飛去 。
and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於有了足夠的力量可以一起爬上梯子爬到屋頂上 , 所有的鴿子 , 一只洛杉磯紅氣球 , 都在那邊等著他 , 他們把他帶到城墻上去 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘了提到:每當他失去了一隻鴿子 , 他就會把那隻鴿子帶到城墻外面 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在羅馬的舊習俗中 , 死者從來不埋在牆下 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我覺得這真是個令人高興的故事 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	這真的會走很長的一段路 。
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	所以 , 總之 , 我經歷了...如果包裝沒有用 , 且如果故事沒有用 , 我只要想出頭銜 , 希望書名就會把我往正確的方向踢掉 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時候它的確把我集中精神 , 我甚至會畫一個標題頁 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	這些書頁最終引領我找到解答 , 這是一位年輕女子的故事 。 她在羅馬城外 , 將信息傳遞給這個城市的一個人 。
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	這隻鴿子飛到阿匹手的上方
you can see the tombs and pines and so on and so forth along the way .	你可以看到墳墓和松巴等這些東西 。
if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看見這條紅線 , 你看到的是鴿子的行徑 ; 如果你看不見紅線 , 你就是那隻鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	在這個時點 , 它變得非常必要 , 也有可能 , 試圖傳達那種無需實際移動就能飛越城市的感覺 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	過了賽斯提烏斯金字塔--你們應該都很熟悉 , 即使你們最近沒去過羅馬 。
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這個有一點不尋常 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這隻鴿子做了一件事情 , 大部分都不會做的:它採取了一條景色路線 。 我覺得這種裝置是一定要將這本書延伸到四頁之外的 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	所以 , 我們在羅馬競技場周圍繞 , 穿過在宇宙中的聖瑪利亞教堂 , 和海克力士走向河流的神殿 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們差點撞上法蘭奇羅設計的palazofarnese這個結晶體是由羅馬競技場拆下來的結晶
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們俯瞰鮮花廣場
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我給我學生看的其中一樣東西 , 因為它完全是違背了所有觀點的規則 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我覺得唯一重要的透視法則 , 就是只要看上去可信 , 你就成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你會試著找出消失在哪裡 ; 一對在克雷莫納的人在火星上 , 還有另外一些在克雷莫納的人 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但在和平聖母堂前面的廣場 , 那裡無可避免地有一場足球比賽正在上演 , 我們被一顆足球擊中 。
now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	這張圖說明了被足球擊中的情形很糟 。
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有所有的片段:這裡是聖母堂 , 那裡有足球 , 那裡有小小的鳥翅膀 , 所以不得不重新思考 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你想要看清楚聖母堂 , 這些書很靈活 , 非常互動 , 只要把它翻過來 , 就會用另一種方式來看 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	穿過巷子 , 我們可以看到衝擊被記錄在紅線中 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	接著 , 鳥兒們經過了這個中世紀的高樓 , 來了幾棟剩下的中世紀塔樓 , 來到聖雅納州的教堂邊緣 , 往下看進去 , 來到了亞那瓦納州 , 我們已經看過且飛過好幾次了 ; 這裡有四條河流的伯尼雕像 , 接著經過了很棒的博羅米諾絕妙的聖依華堂 , 足夠長的時間 , 直到26英呎的卡索 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	接著 , 我們可以在裡面飛來飛去 , 因為我們是在飛 , 在這個特定的時刻 , 我們不用太擔心重力 , 所以這幅圖可以用在頁面上 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	當我們通過gesu , 我們會變得很繁複 ; 一點也不意外地模仿建築物 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	一面牆上佈滿了我前面提到的相對位置的美麗雕刻 , 貼在尼隆上方的 " ristorante " 招牌上方的美麗雕刻 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最後我們來到了palazzo的前庭也就是目的地 。
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	穿過庭院 , 進入一扇小窗戶 , 進入閣樓 , 有人在畫板上工作 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	他從鳥的腿上移除訊息 ; 這是它說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看這個畫板時 , 我們看到他正在寫的東西 , 事實上 , 是一張鴿子剛走過的旅程地圖 , 紅線延伸出去 , 穿過所有視野 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要資訊 , 所以我們完成理解的循環 , 你只需要讀讀這些段落 。
thank you very much .	非常感謝 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院的skylartibbits的工作原理是自行組合的這個想法我們不用去建造某樣東西 , 反而可以創造一些材料來一起組建材料 , 用一股dna短股dna在初期階段組裝起來是很大的概念 ; tibbits向我們展示了三種以上的計畫 , 暗示著自行組裝的未來可能會變成什麼樣子 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	skylartibbits:我們可以做出讓自己的東西嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天 , 我想向你們展示未來我們製造東西的方式 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信不久後我們的建築物和機器就會自行組合、複製和修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以 , 我要給你們看我相信是當前的製造業狀態 , 然後和一些自然系統比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	所以 , 在當前的製造業狀態 , 我們有摩天大樓--兩年半的時間 , 五十萬到一百萬個部分 , 相當複雜 , 令人振奮的新技術 , 在鋼鐵 , 水泥 , 玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人振奮的機器 , 可以帶我們進入太空五年的時間 , 250萬個部分 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但在另一邊 , 如果你看一下自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種類型的蛋白質 , 可以在一萬納秒折疊 , 或dna有三十億個鹼基對 , 我們可以在大約一小時複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 我們的自然系統有這麼多的複雜性 , 但它們效率很高 , 遠遠超過任何我們可以建立的東西 , 遠遠超過任何我們可以建立的複雜性 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	他們在能源方面的效率遠高於
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎沒有犯過錯誤 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	而且他們可以自我修復長壽 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以自然界的系統有些超級有趣的東西 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們能將它翻譯到我們的建築環境中 , 那麼就有一些令人振奮的潛力可以讓我們製造東西的方法 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵是自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以 , 如果我們想要使用我們的物理環境中的自組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	首先 , 我們需要解碼我們所要建設的複雜性 , 所以我們的建築物和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要解碼成簡單的序列基本上就是我們建築物如何運作的dna
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編程的部分 , 可以用該序列來摺疊起來 , 或重新配置 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能讓它啟動的能量 , 讓我們的部分能夠從程式當中折疊起來 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型的糾錯冗餘 , 以保證我們已經成功地建立起我們想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以我要給你們看一些項目 , 是我在麻省理工學院的同事和我正在努力實現這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	前兩個是macrobot和decibot 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	所以這些項目都是大規模的可重構機器人--8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	都嵌入機械式的電子設備 , 傳感器
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你想要解碼什麼便折疊成什麼 , 成序列的角度--負120 , 負120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , 負120--類似的東西 , 一連串的角度 , 或輪流 , 你就把序列送過了弦 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每一個單位都需要它的消息--負120它的旋轉 , 檢查它是否到了那裡 , 然後把它傳遞給它的鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些傑出的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師 , 在這個項目上工作 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我認為它真的會帶出光線:它真的可以擴展嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美元 , 數小時的人為了製造這8英尺的機器人而努力 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們可以擴大規模嗎 ? 我們真的可以把機器人技術嵌入每一個部分嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題 , 並著眼於被動的天性 , 或被動地試圖重新配置可編程 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它更進一步 , 它嘗試以實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	它基本上是最基礎的計算基礎 , 即數位邏輯閘 , 直接嵌入到你的零件中 。
so this is a nand gate .	所以這是一座nand邏輯閘
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一個正四面體 , 它是門 , 會做你的計算 , 你有兩個輸入的正四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中一個是來自用戶的輸入 , 當你在堆你的磚時 ,
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另一個則是從前一個被放置的磚
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它給你在3d空間中的輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	所以這表示 , 使用者可以開始在他們想要磚塊的位置上塞進去 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算它是之前做什麼 , 和你說你想要它做什麼 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在立體空間內移動--向上或向下 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	所以 , 在左手邊 , [1 , 1]輸入等於輸出0 , 它就會下降 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , [0 , 0]輸入1輸出 , 它會向上
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	那真正的意思就是 , 我們的結構現在包含了我們所要建設的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以 , 他們有了所有建構出來的資訊 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	那就表示 , 我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這種情況下 , 我稱它為自我導向的複製 , 因為你的結構包含了確切的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你就可以替換零件 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有局部嵌入的資訊會告訴你如何解決它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可以擁有攀登的東西將它讀取 , 然後在一對一輸出 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它直接嵌入 ; 沒有任何外部的指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	我將展示的最後一個項目被稱為偏置鏈 , 它可能是我們現在被動自組裝系統最令人興奮的例子 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以它採取了可重構性和可編程性 , 使它成為一個完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	所以基本上你有一連串的元素
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素是完全相同的 , 而且它們偏頗 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以 , 每一條鏈 , 或每一項元素 , 都想要向右或向左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈 , 基本上就是在編程 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你是在告訴每個單位是否應該向右或向左轉 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你搖晃鏈 , 它便折疊成任何你編程的配置 , 在這種情況下 , 一個螺旋 , 或在這種情況下 , 兩個彼此相鄰的立方體 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	所以基本上你可以編寫任何立體的形狀--或是一維的 , 二維--完全被動地進入這條連接線 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們什麼關於未來的訊息 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我想 , 它告訴我們 , 自我組裝、複製、修復的新可能性 , 存在於我們的物理結構、建築物、機器當中 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	在這些部分中有新的可編程 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從而有新的計算可能性 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們將會有空間的計算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物 , 橋樑 , 機器 , 我們所有的磚其實可以計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	那是驚人的並行和分佈式的計算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	因此 , 它是令人振奮的潛力 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為 , 我在這裡所展示的這些計畫 , 只是對這個未來的一小步 , 如果我們實施這些新技術 , 為一個新的自組裝世界實現 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們去過月球 , 繪製出大陸的地圖 , 甚至兩次海洋深處 。 下一個世代還有什麼需要探索 ? 生物學家和探險家內森•沃爾夫提出這個答案:幾乎所有一切 。 然後我們從不可見的小事物開始 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	內森.沃爾夫:還有什麼需要探索 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我去了威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市 。
