developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展出思維的靈活性 , 使觀點流利 , 取決於情境的需求 , 這才是你要學的 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 什麼是最佳時光檔案 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	高度 " 正面懷舊 " , 適度 " 未來 " 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	及適合現代主義的調節 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	而且總是低於消極及非法主義 ,
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最佳的節奏混合是你從過去積極向上獲得的 , 給予你的根基 。 你把你的家人、身份和自我連結起來 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	從未來獲得的 , 是翅膀飛向新的目的地 , 新的挑戰
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現在的享樂主義得到的就是探索自己、地點、人、感性所在的能量 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何過度時光的觀點 , 都比正面來得更多負面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	為了成功而犧牲未來 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	犧牲家庭時光 , 犧牲友善時光
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	犧牲快樂時光 , 犧牲個人歸宿
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	犧牲業餘愛好 ; 犧牲睡眠 。 所以會影響他們的健康
and they live for work , achievement and control .	並且為工作、成就和控制而活 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我敢肯定 , 和一些ted會員產生共鳴
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	這引起我共鳴 。 我成長於一個貧窮的孩子 , 生長在南布朗克斯貧民窟 , 一個西西里島的家庭 , 大家都活在過去與現在 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我在這裡 , 是個未來優秀的人 , 跑到頂端 , 做出這麼多犧牲 , 因為老師介入 , 讓我成為未來的導向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我別吃那顆棉花糖 , 因為如果你等一下你會得到兩顆 , 直到我學會平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加上 「 享樂主義 」 , 加上了正面積極的關注 , 所以 , 在76歲時 , 我比以往更有活力、更有生產力 , 而且我比以往都更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只想說我們正應用在許多世界問題上:改變學校學童的輟學率 , 打擊毒癮 , 增強青少年健康 , 用時間隱喻法治療退伍軍人創傷後壓力症候群的症狀 , 促進可持續性發展與保育 , 減少身體康復的比率 , 此外 , 會有50%的退出率 , 改變自殺式恐怖分子 , 改變家庭關係 , 修正家庭關係 , 修正時間區域衝突的時間 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	最後 , 我想說 , 許多生命的謎題 , 都可以藉由了解你的時間觀和其他的觀點來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這想法既簡單又顯而易見但我認為後果是很深遠的
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	一百年後 , 有多少今天的新聞標題會被重視 ? 一百年後 ? kirkcitron的 「 長遠新聞 」 專案收集了現今不只重大 , 還會在接下來的數十年產生共鳴 。 在ted2010 , 他強調近期的標題 , 有潛力可以形塑我們的未來 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來、全球議題、媒體、新聞、科學、科學
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:現在 , 真正的新聞 。
we are drowning in news .	我們都淹沒在新聞中 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	單是路透社一家一年就發佈三百五十萬則新聞
that's just one source .	那只是一個來源 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:這些新聞會有幾則用長期的角度來看是重要的 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這是背後的好消息 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這個計畫是 「 長遠當代基金會 」 由ted成立 , 包括凱文凱利和史都華布蘭德 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	我們在尋找的是在五、十或一萬年後 , 可能仍然重要的新聞 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	而當你透過那過濾器看新聞時 , 很多事情會掉下來 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	以去年a.p.的上層故事為例 , 這在十年內會很重要嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這在50或100年後重要嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 還滿酷的 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但去年的頭條是經濟 , 我只賭上這個 , 遲早 , 這波經濟衰退新聞就會消失 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	那麼 , 什麼樣的故事會對未來造成影響呢 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 就科學來說 ,
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小機器人會穿過我們的血液管道 , 修理東西 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	如果你是老鼠的話 , 這有一天早就到了 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	最近一些故事:奈米蜜蜂用真蜂毒液把腫瘤傳送到腦部 , 所製造出來的一個機器人 , 可以在人體上爬行 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	資源方面呢 ? 我們要如何養活九十億人 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	今天我們有高達60億的糧食問題 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	如同我們昨天聽到的 , 有超過十億人在挨餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	不用基因改造作物 , 英國就會餓死 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾蓋茲投入了十億在農業研究上 。
what about global politics ?	全球政治方面呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	這個世界將會大不相同 , 如果讓中國來設置議程 , 他們可能會這麼做 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們超過美國成為世界上最大的汽車市場 , 他們已經超過德國成為最大的出口國 , 他們開始在兒童身上做dna測試 , 來選擇他們的職業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們找到各種途徑 , 推開我們所知的極限
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	一些最近的發現:從阿根廷有一個蟻群 , 散播到每一個大陸 , 但南極洲 ; 有一個自導式的機器人科學家 , 很快就有了發現 , 科學可能不再需要我們 , 生命可能也不再需要我們 ; 一個在120 , 000年後醒來的微生物 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	似乎有沒有我們 , 生命就會繼續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但去年 , 我選擇了很長一則新聞 , 就是這個:水在月球上找到了 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	讓蟻群相當容易放上去 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果美國太空總署不行 , 中國也有可能 , 或在座的人 , 可能就會寫一張大支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長遠來看 , 某些新聞故事比其他新聞更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	行星科學家carolynporco展示了從卡西尼航海到土星的影像 , 著重在它的最大衛星泰坦 , 和在結冰的土衛二上 , 它似乎把冰噴射出來 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	nasa , 設計 , 探索 , 科學 , 空間 , 科技 , 宇宙 , 視覺化 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	carolynporco使我們飛往土星
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我將帶你們踏上一段旅程 ,
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這段旅程是你和我已經踏上許多年的旅程 , 它開始於五十年前 , 人類第一次踏出我們的星球 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在這50年中 , 我們不僅對月球有了雙腳 , 我們還對其中八個星球有了分散的機械太空船 。 我們著陸在小行星上 , 我們使用彗星 , 在這個時點 , 我們有一艘太空船正向冥王星駛去 , 這是我們所知的地球 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機器人的任務 , 都是人類旅程的一部分:一趟旅行 , 要了解某樣東西 , 要了解我們的宇宙 , 要了解我們的起源是什麼 , 以及地球、地球 , 我們 , 要活在上面 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在太陽系中所有我們可能去到的地方尋找答案 , 例如像這樣的問題土星 。 我們去過土星 。 在1980年代早期我們造訪土星之前 , 我們去過土星 。 但我們對土星的調查從卡西尼號太空船開始更加深入土星 , 穿越星際空間 , 長達七年之久 , 在2004年夏天穿梭於土星運行軌道 , 成為人類最遠的機械裝置 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	現在 , 土星系統是個豐富的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘的、科學的見解 , 以及明顯的前景看好的前景 , 而這個系統的調查有著巨大的宇宙能力 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 單單研究光環 , 我們就能瞭解很多恆星和氣體的磁片 , 我們稱之為螺旋星系 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這裡有一張仙女星雲的漂亮圖片 , 這是離銀河系最近 , 體積最大的螺旋星系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	這裡有個美麗的複合體由哈伯太空望遠鏡拍攝
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 回到土星的這段旅程 , 其實也是人類旅程的一部分 , 也是一種比喻 , 用來了解我們身邊所有事物之間的相互關係 , 以及人類如何融入這張圖片 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	我很痛苦 , 我無法告訴各位 , 我們已經學過卡西尼號 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我無法向你們展示我們在過去兩年半所拍攝的所有美麗照片 , 因為我沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	接下來我要講的兩個最令人興奮的故事 , 是這次重大探索之旅中發生的兩個 。 我們正在土星周圍進行的 。 並且已經有兩年半之久了 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星伴隨著非常大且多樣的衛星收藏 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們的大小範圍從幾公里寬到整個美國那麼大 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	我們拍攝過土星的大多數美麗照片 , 事實上 , 土星和它的一些衛星在一起 。 這是土星和土星的是土衛二 , 然後這裡是土星 , 土星則是光環 , 展示了它的垂直薄度 , 土衛二和土衛二 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	現在 , 土星47顆衛星中 , 有兩顆是豎立行星 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	那些是土衛六泰坦和土衛二恩克拉多斯 。 泰坦是土星最大的衛星 , 並且 , 在卡西尼號到達之前 , 它是我們在太陽系中最大的一個未經勘探的地帶 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	它是長期以來研究這些行星的人們 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它有很大很厚的大氣層 , 事實上 , 它的地表環境被認為它更像是我們在地球上的環境 , 或者說 , 至少在過去 , 比其它太陽系中的身體 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣層主要是分子氮分子 , 就像你在這裡吸入的氮氣一樣 , 只不過它的大氣層被簡易的有機物質所混合 , 像是甲烷、丙烷、乙烷 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	這些在土衛六大氣層中高處的分子被分解了 , 它們的產品結合在一起 , 形成霧狀顆粒 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這個霧狀物無所不在 , 完全是全球性的 , 籠罩土衛六 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這也是為什麼在光譜上 , 我們的眼睛無法看到表面 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些霧狀顆粒 , 在卡西尼號到達之前 , 在數十億年之前 , 先被它們輕輕飄到水面上 , 將表面覆蓋成厚重的有機廢物 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	就像泰坦一樣 , 泰坦相當於焦油 , 油或者我們不知道的是什麼
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這是我們猜測的 。 而這些分子 , 尤其是甲烷和乙烷 , 在泰坦的地表溫度下 , 可以是液體 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷是土衛六地上的水 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	它在大氣中是會冷凝的 , 所以認知到這種情況 , 會帶到一整個世界 , 奇異的可能性 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , ok , 在那些雲上方 , 你有數百公里的霧狀霧狀物 , 它會防止陽光到達地表 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	地表的溫度大約是華氏零下350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	但儘管那樣的寒冷 , 你也可能有降雨落在土衛六表面 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在土衛六上下雨的做法是:它刻著海鷗 , 形成河流和白內障 , 它能形成峽谷 , 大型盆地和隕石 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以把泥巴從高山上和山丘上沖到低窪地帶 。 停下來想一想 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像土衛六的地表會是什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	那裡很黑 。 土衛六上的中午時間跟地球上灰暗一樣 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	那裡很冷 , 陰森 , 陰森 , 迷霧重重 , 可能正在下雨 , 而你可能正站在密西根湖岸邊 , 用油漆薄漆著 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這就是在卡西尼號到達之前泰坦星表面的觀點 , 我可以告訴各位 , 我們在泰坦上發現的 , 雖然在細節上不盡相同 , 但它的確和故事相當迷人 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 這就像卡西尼號的居民──這就像是跳躍式的凡爾納冒險一樣 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	我說過 , 它有很厚、廣闊的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這是泰坦星的照片 , 太陽的背光 , 光環是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	而另一顆衛星--我甚至不知道是哪一顆 。 它是一個非常廣闊的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們在卡西尼號上有可以透過大氣層觀測到地表的儀器我的相機系統就是其中之一
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們也拍了這樣的照片
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	你所看到的是明亮、黑暗的區域 , 這區也為我們帶來了好多好處 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	它是如此的讓人迷惑:我們無法知道我們在泰坦上看到了什麼 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你靠近一點看這個區域 , 你會看到像無數通道的東西--我們不知道 。 你看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	這個 , 後來我們發現 , 事實上是一個坑 , 但是土衛六表面的隕石坑數量很少 , 意味著土衛六的地表非常年輕 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	還有些特徵看起來像地殼一樣 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	看起來牠們被拉開了 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你看到行星上的任何東西 , 都代表有個裂痕 , 像是一個斷層 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以它已經在結構上改變了 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道六個月後 , 許多人都認為它是卡西尼號對於土衛六的重要發現 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	那就是惠更斯號探測器的部署 , 歐洲建立的惠更斯探測器 , 卡西尼號載了七年的太陽系 。 我們把它部署到土衛六的大氣當中 , 要花兩個半小時才能下降 , 它在地表著陸 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我只想強調一下這個事件有多重大 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類製造的裝置它第一次登陸在外太陽系於人類歷史上
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	在我看來 , 這實在是太顯著了 , 這事件本應在美國和歐洲的每個城市 , 舉行這個遊行活動 , 可悲的是 , 這並非事實 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這很有意義 , 另一個原因 。 這是一個國際性的任務 , 這個活動在歐洲、德國受到讚頌 , 發表了令人振奮的演說 , 用英式口音 , 美國口音和德國口音 , 法語、義大利語 , 和荷蘭口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	這是在動人的演示 , 示範 「 聯合國 」 一詞的意義:一個真正的國家團結一起為 「 好 」 努力 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個案例中 , 要探索一顆星球是件很大的事 , 並漸漸了解行星系統 , 在人類歷史上 , 一直都是不可靠的 , 現在人類真的接觸到了它 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我說的就是起雞皮疙瘩 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是一個極度情緒化的事件 , 它是我個人永遠無法忘記的 , 你也不應如此 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	但 , 探測器在下降過程中對大氣進行了測量 , 拍攝了全景照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴各位 , 從探測器上看到泰坦表面的第一張照片是什麼感覺 。 這是我們看到的 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	這真是太震驚了 , 因為那是我們希望從軌道上拍攝的所有照片 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	這是很明顯的圖案 , 地質圖案 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	是可由液體流動形成的樹突狀圖案 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以沿著這些管道 , 看看它們是如何匯合的 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	他們匯聚到這裡的通道 , 流入了這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你看到的是一條海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是液體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這是一條海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是在16公里高的地方拍的 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這是拍攝於8公里高度的海岸線
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里--這大約是個航空的高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要飛機穿越美國 , 你就要飛到這些高度 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這張照片是你在泰坦航空公司的車窗 , 飛越泰坦星的表面 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器在地表上安息 , 我要給你們看 , 女士們 , 先生們 , 這是第一張從外太陽系拍攝月球的照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這裡是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是冰鵝卵石 , 對嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很明顯 , 它落在了其中一個平坦、黑暗的區域 , 沒有因為視覺而下沉 。 所以它沒有落在液體中 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	探測器基本上就是泰坦--相當於一座泥土平地 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是液態甲烷供應不固定的土地 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	這種材料可能已經通過我們所看到的這些管道把土衛六的高地沖洗掉了土衛六上的高地 , 讓土衛六不斷地累積 , 來填補低窪的空地 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是惠更斯號探測器著陸的地方 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但 , 我們的影像仍然沒有標誌 , 甚至惠更斯的影像 , 沒有大型液體的開放原體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	他們在哪裡呢 ? 當我們發現沙丘時 , 更讓人費解了 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們拍攝土衛六赤道區域的電影 , 展出這些沙丘 。 這些沙丘有100公尺高 , 被幾公里的高度拆散 , 然後再繼續好幾英里 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	高達1000或1200英里的沙丘
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是土衛六的撒哈拉沙漠
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	顯然是個非常乾燥的地方 , 不然就不會有沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	所以同樣的 , 讓人困惑的是沒有任何液體 , 直到最後 , 我們看到了極地的湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	而土衛六南極的一個湖 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	和安大略湖差不多大 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	然後 , 僅僅一個禮拜半前 , 我們飛過北極 , 發現土衛六的面積 , 在這兒我們發現了一個特色 , 大小和加斯比亞海一樣大 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	由於某些原因我們不明白的原因 , 或至少在這個季節 , 很明顯地是泰坦的兩極 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你會同意我們發現土衛六是一個了不起、神奇的地方 。 它很奇特 , 它很奇特 , 但又很奇怪 , 很像地球 , 且有著像地球般的地質形成 , 以及一個巨大的地質多樣性 , 且是個迷人的世界 , 它在太陽系中唯一能為複雜性而戰的 , 富有性就是地球本身 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以現在我們來到土衛二看看 。 土衛二是一個小型衛星 , 大小只有土衛六的十分之一 。 你可以看到它就在英國旁邊 , 只是想讓你們看看尺寸 。 這不是一個威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	而土衛二很白很明亮 , 它的表面很明顯有裂痕 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是非常地質活動的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但土衛二的母親大聲發現土衛二是在南極找到的 , 我們現在看到的是南極的地帶 , 我們在那裡發現了這一系統裂痕 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們的顏色不同 , 因為它們的組成不同 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們是塗層的 。 這些裂縫會覆蓋有機物質 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 整個南極地區的溫度升高了 。 這裡是整個星球上最熱的地區 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這就如同發現地球南極比熱帶地區還熱一樣
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	接著 , 當我們拍攝了額外的照片 , 我們發現從這些斷裂中 , 有精細的冰粒噴射出來 , 向太空延伸了數百英里 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們用顏色標記出這幅圖片時 , 將微弱的光度帶出 , 我們看到這些噴流在土衛二的上空投入數千英里 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊檢視了像這樣的圖片 , 思考了卡西尼號的其他成果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得到的結論是 , 這些噴射現象可能是由土衛二地表下的液態水所噴發出來的 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以我們可能有液態水、有機物質和過剩的熱能 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們可能偶然發現了現代行星探索的聖杯 , 或者說 , 一個可能適合生物生存的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	而我不認為我需要告訴你們在太陽系其他地方生物的發現 , 不管是在土衛二或其它地方 , 都會有巨大的文化與科學含義 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能顯示出創意的發生次數 , 不只一次 , 而是兩次 , 獨立地 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 那就表示 , 按照推論 , 在整個宇宙和它137億年的歷史上 , 它已經發生了很驚人的幾次 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球仍是唯一一顆充滿生命的星球 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它很珍貴 , 它是獨一無二的 , 到目前為止 , 它仍是我們唯一的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果在座的各位在1960年代時有警覺和連貫性的話 , 請原諒你們 , 如果沒有的話 , 你們應該還記得1968年阿波羅八號太空人拍的這張著名照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是第一次地球從太空中拍攝出來 , 且它對我們在宇宙中的位置造成了巨大的影響 , 以及我們對於保護地球的責任感 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	我們在卡西尼號上拍攝了等同於人類眼睛從未見過的照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	這是日全食的從土星的另一側觀測到的
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這張美麗的圖片裡 , 你看到背光的主光圈 , 看到太陽折射的影像 , 還可以看到這個光圈 , 事實上由土衛二的表面積所創造 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但 , 彷彿這還不夠精彩 , 我們可以發現 , 在這個美麗的圖像中 , 看到我們自己的星球 , 夾在土星光環的臂彎中 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 有種很讓人感動的東西 , 就是從遠處看我們自己 , 並捕捉到在其他世界的天空中 , 我們這個小藍色的星球 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	那 , 以及我們從那獲得的觀點 , 最終可能就是我們從這次探索旅程中獲得的最佳獎勵那是半世紀前的最佳獎勵 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	截至2005年 , 全世界只有15%的地區被標記出來 。 這使災難發生後的分娩過程緩慢並隱藏未使用的土地和未知的道路 。 在這簡短的簡短的演講中 , 谷歌的筆跡製作者 , 一個團體繪製工具 , 正在使用地圖來繪製他們的世界 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、科技、
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	拉利蒂什卡特達:製作地圖來對抗災難 , 建立經濟體系 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , 氣旋納基斯摧毀緬甸 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人都非常需要協助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要把人民及物資趕到當地
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但是沒有地圖標示道路沒有顯示醫院的地圖也沒有幫助受害者到達氣旋
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看看洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信到2005年 , 只有15%的世界的地圖被詳細的呈現 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國反對了一個問題 , 全球大部分的人口面臨的問題:沒有詳細的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但 , 協助來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在google有40位志願者使用了一套新軟體標註了12萬公里的道路3000間醫院 , 運送和救災所
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天的時間
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們使用的新軟體 ? googlemapmaker
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	googlemapmaker是一個技術 , 它賦予我們每個人能力 , 繪製出我們所知的地區性地圖 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這個軟體繪製所有東西 , 從公路到河流 , 從學校到當地的企業 , 還有視頻商店 , 到轉角的商店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎被提名人hernandodesto認可 , 要讓大多數發展中國家經濟的關鍵 , 就是要掌握大量未破的土地 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 光在印度就有一兆美金的房地產保持資金
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光是在去年170個國家數以千計的使用者就標註了數以百萬計的資訊並建立了一張從未想過能達到的細節地圖
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	這一切得以實現 , 靠的是熱情使用者無所不在的力量 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	我們來看看目前使用者製作的一些地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 在我們講話的同時 , 在這170個國家中 , 人們也在繪製世界 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到在非洲的bridget剛為塞內加爾標註了一條道路
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	離這裡近一點 , 位於班加羅爾的一個n.g路口
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算機幾何學動作識別和機器學習的結果
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數以千計用戶的勝利 , 在數百個城市 , 一個用戶 , 一次編輯一筆資訊 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是一個向我們尚未開發的百分之七十星球的邀請
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	2003年 , 巴勒斯坦村莊發動一場長達10個月的非暴力抗議 , 阻止一把障礙圍牆蓋在他們的橄欖上 。 你們聽說了嗎 ? 不這麼認為 。 巴西製片朱利亞•包夏問為什麼我們只注意在以色列和平的衝突裡的暴力 , 而非暴力的領袖 , 他們也許有一天會帶來和平 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、慈悲、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	juliabacha:注意非暴力事件
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去8年來 , 我致力於記錄以色列人與巴勒斯坦人的作品他們試圖終結這衝突用的是和平的手段
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲及美國各地旅行時 , 有一個問題總是出現:巴勒斯坦甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不用非暴力的方式抵抗 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	我聽到這個問題時 , 所面臨的挑戰是 , 通常我才從中東回國 , 我在那裡度過時間 , 拍攝了數十位巴勒斯坦人在用非暴力的方式來保衛他們的土地和水資源 , 不受以色列士兵及居民的侵襲 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導人試圖要讓一場大規模的全國性非暴力運動結束了該區域的佔領並建立和平
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	然而你們中的大多數人可能從未聽說過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	區分出在國外發生的事和國外的認知是其中一個關鍵的原因為什麼我們還沒有一場巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動成功過
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以我今天在這裡要談的是注意力的力量、你的注意力的力量、以及非暴力運動在西岸、加薩及其他地方的出現和發展 , 但今天我的案例研究將會是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 大多需要非暴力才能成長的 , 並不是要讓巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力手段 , 而是我們要開始注意那些本來就有的人們 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	容我帶你們到這個名為布德魯斯的村莊來闡明這一點 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前他們面臨滅絕 , 因為以色列宣佈要築起一個隔離屏障而部分的障礙會建在村落的上層 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地並且被包圍住 , 所以他們會失去管道去接觸其他的西岸 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過當地的領導 , 他們發動了和平抗爭活動來阻止這件事情發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些短片 , 所以你們可以瞭解 , 它在地面上的樣子 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女人:我們被告知牆將分隔巴勒斯坦與以色列
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德鲁斯村我們意識到這道牆會偷走我們的土地
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列男子:圍籬事實上創造了一種解決方案
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男:今天你被邀請來一場和平的遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你的加入有數十位你的以色列兄弟姐妹
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列社會運動人士:軍隊害怕的就是非暴力的反對 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女性:我們看到男人試圖推開那些士兵 , 但沒有一個能那樣做 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我覺得女孩子可以做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔赫黨員:我們必須清空腦中的傳統思維 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯黨員:我們是完全和諧的 , 我們希望將它推廣到全巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	陳述:一個聯合國
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔赫、哈馬斯、人民陣線 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	主播:圍籬持續的衝突 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊界警察被派來驅散群眾
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量
man: these are live bullets .	男:這些是活彈
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	就像wujah一樣 , 到處開槍
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列活動家:我很確定我們都會死
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但我身邊還有許多人甚至不畏懼 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗議無法阻止這【聲音模糊不清】
protester: this is a peaceful march .	抗議者:這是一場和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	口號聲:我們辦得到 ! 我們辦得到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱利亞•巴夏:當我第一次聽到布德鲁斯村的故事時我很驚訝國際媒體竟然沒有報導這一連串驚人的事件在七年前發生在2003年
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是布德鲁斯村成功了 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民抗爭十個月後說服了以色列政府將這道牆從他們的土地上移開到綠線上也就是國際公認的邊界線以色列與巴勒斯坦人之間
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德鲁斯村的抗爭自此傳遍全約旦河西岸的村莊以及耶路撒冷境內巴勒斯坦社區
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	然而媒體仍然對這些故事保持沉默
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默帶給非暴力事件發展的可能性帶來深遠的後果 , 甚至可能在巴勒斯坦生存 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭都有一個非常重要的共通點他們同時也是劇院尋求觀眾的原因
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果只有使用暴力的人才能上頭版並引起國際關注巴勒斯坦的議題非暴力領導者就很難向他們的社區證明公民不服從是一個可行的選項來解決他們的困境
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的力量可能對在場的父母親一點也不意外 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	能讓你孩子逐漸發出高聲的脾氣 , 最好的方式就是讓他第一次對他發出適合的注意力 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	脾臟就會變成兒童心理學家所謂的功能性行為 , 自從孩子學到他能從中得到父母的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以透過給予孩童注意力或不給予孩童注意力來鼓勵或抑制這樣的行為 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成年人也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為可以被影響 , 取決於國際社會選擇聚焦的地方 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 終止中東地區的衝突並帶來和平的核心是要把非暴力行為轉變成功能性的行為 , 做法是要讓非暴力領導人更重視現今的非暴力行為 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	拍攝我的影片到約旦河西岸的村子、加薩及東耶路撒冷的村子我看到了連一部紀錄片的影響也能影響到整個轉變
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在瓦拉杰村一個名為耶路撒冷的村莊這個社區面臨著與布德鲁斯村非常相似的困境
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被包圍 , 失去很多土地 , 且沒有取得自由 , 不論是約旦河岸或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	他們已經使用非暴力手段兩年了 , 但已經逐漸失去注意力了 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們安排了一個篩選
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一週後 , 他們舉行了至今最精彩、最有紀律的展示會 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	籌辦人說村民見到布德鲁斯村的故事被記錄在一部電影裡 , 感覺到確實有人在跟隨他們的行為 , 人們在乎 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續向前 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列那邊則有新的和平運動 , 名叫soldariot , 在希伯來語意思是團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這項運動的領導者一直以來都在使用布德鲁斯村作為主要的工具之一
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報告說從未參與過活動的以色列人看過影片後了解到非暴力的力量也開始加入他們的活動
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	瓦拉杰村和索里德拉爾特的例子顯示即使是小額預算的獨立製片也能在將非暴力轉變成功能性行為上發揮作用
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	現在 , 想像一下大型媒體球員能夠擁有的力量 , 如果他們開始報導每個禮拜都在村莊進行的非暴力示範 , 像是畢爾、尼、瓦拉杰、耶路撒冷的社區 , 在像謝克•傑拉瑞及絲這樣的非暴力領導人 , 在他們的工作上會變得更加明顯、更有價值、更有效 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的是要了解如果我們不注意這些努力它們是看不見的 , 就好像它們從來沒有發生過一樣
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但是我親眼目睹過 , 如果我們做到了 , 他們將會繁衍下去 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們繁榮起來 , 他們的影響力會在以色列衝突的總體中成長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	而他們的影響力就是那種能夠終於解開局面的影響力 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人已經證明了非暴力是可行的在布德鲁斯村這樣的地方
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓我們集中注意力 , 讓他們能證明它在各地都行得通 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙奈克有一個簡單但強而有力的領導模式 , 靈感的領導階層 , 都從黃金圈及 「 為什麼 」 開始 , 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁路德金 , 和萊特兄弟......
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bullseye、商業、企業家、領導者、銷售、銷售、成功
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	simonsinek:偉大的領導人如何啟發行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你要如何解釋當事物不如我們所想的一般時 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或者更好的是 , 你該如何解釋當其他人有能力實現看來與所有的假設時 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	比如:為什麼蘋果電腦這麼有創意 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 日復一日他們比全部的競爭對手都要有創意
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 它們只是一家電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們和其他人一樣 ,
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有相同的人才、相同的機構、同樣的顧問、同樣的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	為什麼他們似乎有什麼不同 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁•路德•金恩主導民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一一個在美國公民權利受苦的人他肯定不是當時最偉大的演說家
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	而為什麼是萊特兄弟能夠想出有控制權、有力量的人飛行 , 當有其他團隊更有資格、更好的資金......
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有達成動力飛行的目標 , 萊特兄弟打敗了他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有其他東西在玩 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我有一個發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	而這個發現深深地改變了我對世界運作方式的看法而它甚至深深地改變了我在運作的方式
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有個規律
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果是 , 世界上所有偉大且具啟發性的領導者和組織不管是蘋果、馬丁路德金或萊特兄弟他們都認為、行動與溝通的方式完全相同
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	而且它完全與其他人相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的就是將它編碼 , 這可能是世界上最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱它為金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 怎麼做 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小小的想法解釋了為什麼有些組織和有些領導者能夠激勵別人不去的地方 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義一下這個詞 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	每個人 , 地球上的每一個組織都知道他們在做什麼 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些知道如何辦到 , 不管你用不同的價值主張或你的本體流程或你的usp 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但很少人或機構知道他們為什麼要做他們所做的事 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	所謂的 「 為什麼 」 , 「 我不是指 「 做一個利潤 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	這就是結果 。 它永遠都是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	所謂的 「 為什麼 」 , 我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的目的是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	為什麼你的組織會存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼你早上要起床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	而且為什麼有人要在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	嗯 , 結果呢 , 我們思考的方式 , 我們行動的方式 , 我們溝通的方式來自外部 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	這是顯而易見的 。 我們從最清楚的事物到最模糊的 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但鼓舞人心的領導者和激勵人心的組織 , 不管它們的規模 , 不管它們的產業都以內在的方式思考、行動與溝通 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果電腦 , 因為它們很容易理解 , 且大家都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果電腦和大家一樣 , 一則他們發來的市場訊息可能會聽起來像這樣: 「 我們製造很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	它們被設計得很漂亮、簡單、容易使用 , 以及友善的使用者 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想要買一台嗎 ? 「 嗯 。 」
and that's how most of us communicate .	而這就是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這就是多數行銷的方式 , 多數銷售的方式也是如此 , 也是我們多數人溝通交流的方式 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們做了什麼 , 我們說我們如何不同或我們如何比較好然後我們期待某種行為 , 購買、投票等等
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新律師事務所:我們有最好的律師和最大的客戶 , 我們總是為和我們做生意的客戶服務 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車它有很好的汽油里程它有皮革製的座椅 , 買我們的車
here's how apple actually communicates .	這裡有蘋果真正溝通的方式:
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信要挑戰現狀 ,
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信用不同的方式思考
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是使產品有美好的設計性 , 簡單的使用者和使用者友善 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們只是恰巧製造了很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想買一台嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不一樣吧 ? 你已經準備好向我買一台電腦了 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的 , 只是倒轉資訊的順序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它向我們證明了人們不會買你做什麼 ; 人們買你為什麼做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在場的每個人都對買蘋果電腦感到很自在 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也非常欣慰 , 購買蘋果電腦的mp3播放器、蘋果電腦的手機 , 或蘋果電腦的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但是 , 如同我之前說過的 , 蘋果只是一家電腦公司 ,
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	結構上 , 並沒有什麼能區別它們的競爭者 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者都有同樣資格製造這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試過
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , gateway推出平面電視
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很明顯有資格製造平面電視 ,
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	他們製作平面監視器好幾年了 ,
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	戴爾電腦推出mp3播放器與pda.他們的品質很棒 , 他們能做出完美設計的產品 , 沒有人買 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 現在談到它 , 我們甚至無法想像從戴爾電腦買一台mp3播放器
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你會從一家電腦公司買一台mp3播放器 ?
but we do it every day .	但是我們每天都這麼做
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是和每個需要你有什麼的人在做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目的是要跟那些相信你所相信的人們做生意
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最棒的部分是:我所說的都不是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	都以生物學的教義為基礎
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學 , 生物學
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果從上往下看人腦的橫切面 , 會發現人腦其實是分成三個主要部份 , 與黃金圈完美地相關 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的腦、我們的智人大腦、我們的新皮層對應的是 「 什麼 」 的層次 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮層負責我們所有的理性、分析的想法和語言
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個部份組成我們邊緣的腦而我們邊緣的腦是負責所有的感覺像是信任和忠誠
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也同時負責所有人類的行為 , 所有的決策 , 它沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外而內地溝通時 , 是的 , 人們可以理解很多複雜的資訊 , 像是特徵、福利、事實和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	只是不推動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能從內而外溝通時我們就直接對著控制行為的大腦說話然後我們允許人們將它合理化用我們說出和做的有形的東西
this is where gut decisions come from .	這就是腸子決策的由來 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道 , 有時候你會給別人所有的事實和數字 , 他們會說: 「 我知道所有事實和細節說了什麼 , 但就是感覺不對 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們要用這個動詞 , 它不會 「 感覺 」 呢 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為控制決策過程的腦這個部分無法掌控語言
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	而我們最多能整理出的是: 「 我不知道 , 那感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者 , 有時你說你帶著你的心在領導 , 或者你跟你的靈魂同在 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我很不想對你打破它 , 那些不是其他身體部位控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	都發生在你邊緣的腦裡 , 大腦控制決策而非語言的區塊 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道為什麼要做你所做的事 , 大家會回應為什麼你做了什麼事 , 那麼 , 你要如何讓大家投票給你 , 或是向你買東西 , 或向你買東西 , 更重要的 , 要忠實而且想成為你所做的事情的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	再一次地 , 目標不是僅僅是賣給需要你的東西的人而已目標是要賣給那些相信你所相信的人們
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是要雇用需要工作的人而是要雇用那些相信你所相信的事的人
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是這麼說 , 你知道 , 如果你雇用人僅是因為他們可以做事 , 他們將為你的錢工作 , 但如果你雇用那些相信你所相信的人們 , 他們將為你工作 , 帶著血汗和淚水 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	除此之外 , 沒有其他地方比萊特兄弟更好的例子了 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大多數人不知道samuelpierpontlangley
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	在二十世紀早期 , 追求的人飛行就像當時的網路公司一樣 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	而samuelpierpontlangley曾經擁有 , 我們假設的成功的秘訣
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我的意思是 , 即使現在 , 你問別人: 「 你的產品為何會讓你的公司失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是會給你相同的三個條件:低度控制住 , 錯誤的人 , 市場狀況不佳 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	總是相同的三樣東西 , 所以 , 讓我們來探索一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley捐贈了5萬美元這家戰爭部門要搞清楚這架飛行機器
money was no problem .	錢沒有問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛拿了一席之地 , 在史密森尼工作 , 他非常有連結性 , 他認識當時所有大頭腦 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他雇用最好的人才資金 , 市場狀況也很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報跟著他到處跑而且每個人都為langley加油
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那麼為何我們從來沒有聽過samuelpierpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	距離俄亥俄州 , 幾百英里遠 , 奧維爾和威爾伯萊特 , 他們完全沒有我們認為的成功秘訣 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 , 他們用他們的腳踏車店支付他們的夢想 ; 沒有萊特兄弟的團隊 , 沒有接受大學教育 , 甚至沒有奧維爾或威爾堡 ; 紐約時報也跟著他們到處跑 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	不同的是 , 奧維爾和威爾伯是由一個理由 , 一個目的 , 由一個信念來驅使 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能想出這架飛行機器 , 這將改變世界的軌道 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley不同
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想變得富有 , 他也想成名
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他追求財富
and lo and behold , look what happened .	瞧 , 看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	那些相信萊特兄弟的夢想的人用血汗與淚水和他們一起工作 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	另一些人則只是為薪水工作 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	而且他們說的故事是每次萊特兄弟出門他們都得帶上五套零件因為這是他們會墜機的次數在他們進到供應商前
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最後在1903年12月17日萊特兄弟起飛而在場甚至沒有人去體驗
we found out about it a few days later .	我們在幾天後發現了
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步的證明langley因為錯誤的動機在萊特兄弟起飛的那天 , 他退出了
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可能說: 「 那是個驚人的發現 , 各位 , 我會改進你的技術 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一個 , 他沒有變有錢他沒有變有名 , 所以放棄了
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你相信什麼 , 你就會吸引那些相信你所相信的人們
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼吸引那些相信你所相信的人們很重要 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	有種東西叫創意的散播法則如果你不知道這個法則 , 你一定知道這個術語
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	我們人口的前2.5%是創新者
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%是我們早期的採用者
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是早期的大多數晚期和落後者
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人買觸控式手機的唯一理由 , 是因為你不能再買轉子電話了 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都在這個尺度上不同時間坐在不同的位置 , 但創意的散播法則告訴我們的是 , 如果你想要大眾市場的成功或是大眾市場接受一個想法的接受 , 你就不可能擁有它 , 直到你達到了15%到18%之間的市場滲透點 , 然後系統就會到達頂端 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我喜歡問企業: 「 你對新事業的轉變是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很愛告訴你: 「 喔 , 大概是10%吧 。 」 很驕傲地說:
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以讓超過10%的顧客失馬
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有10%的 「 拿到 」
that's how we describe them , right ?	這就是我們如何描述它們 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	那就像是那種直覺 , 感覺 , 「 喔 , 他們就是懂了 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:要如何找到那些在你做生意之前拿到的 , 而不是那些沒拿到錢的人呢 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	所以 , 就是這裡 , 這個小小的差距 , 是你必須要填補的 , 如同jeffreymoore稱它為 " 跨越隔閡 " , 因為 , 你看 , 早期大多數的人不會嘗試 , 直到其他人先嘗試 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	而這些人 , 這些發明家以及早期的採用者他們對做那些腸道的決定感到很自在
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們對做這些直覺的決定感到更加自在他們是被他們對世界的相信所驅使而不只是可得的產品
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些是排隊排了六個小時買一部iphone的人當他們第一次出來的時候你可以在下個星期走進店裡從架子上買一支
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些是平面電視剛上市時花四萬美元的人雖然科技已經問世了
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順帶一提 , 他們這麼做並不因為這項科技太棒了 , 他們靠的是他們自己 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	是因為他們想先成為
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼而你做什麼 , 只證明你相信什麼
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做那些證明他們所相信的事
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	一個人買iphone的原因在最初的六個小時排隊排六個小時是因為他們所相信的這個世界以及他們希望每個人看到的東西他們是第一
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	所以讓我給你一個有名的例子一個有名的失敗以及有名的成功關於創意的散播法則
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 知名的失敗
it's a commercial example .	這是個商業的例子
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	如同前面說過的 , 一秒鐘前 , 成功的秘訣就是金錢、對的人、對的市場狀況 , 對吧 ? 那時你應該會有成功的 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從tivo上市的時候到現在約8、9年前 , 到現在這一天 , 他們是市場上唯一的高品質產品 , 手放下 , 沒有糾紛 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們極其受資助 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場狀況非常棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們把tivo當作動詞
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我tivo東西在我的垃圾時間vr
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo的商業故障
they've never made money .	他們從沒賺過錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們去ipo , 他們的股價約是30到40美金然後一落千丈 , 從來沒有在10美元以上交易
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我想它從沒在6號以上交易除了幾次小漲幅
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo推出他們的產品他們告訴我們他們有的是什麼
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一項產品可以暫停現場的電視節目 , 跳過商業廣告 , 現場的電視節目 , 並且記住你的觀看習慣 , 連你都不問 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	那個憤世嫉俗的大多數說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 , 我們不喜歡它
you're scaring us . "	你嚇著我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 若你是那種喜歡完全掌控生活各方面的人 , 孩子們 , 我們有一樣產品嗎 ?
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它可以暫停現場電視節目 , 跳過商業廣告記下你的收視習慣等等
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼而你做什麼僅僅是你相信什麼的證明
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在讓我給你一個成功的例子關於創意的散播法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	在1963年的夏天 , 25萬人在華盛頓的商場上 , 來聽金恩博士演說 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們沒有寄出任何一張邀請函而當時也沒有網站去查看日期
how do you do that ?	怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	金恩博士不是在美國唯一一個偉大的演說者
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是在美國唯一一個在美國受到折磨的人
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的想法有些壞主意 。
but he had a gift .	但他有一個天賦 ,
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有到處告訴人們在美國什麼需要改變 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他四處走走告訴人們他相信什麼
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 。 」 他告訴人們 。
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	而那些相信他所相信的人們把他的成因歸功於他們的成果 , 他們也告訴人們
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	有些人創造了結構 , 讓這些字眼能傳遞給更多的人 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	然後你瞧 , 25萬人出現在對的日子裡聽著他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人為了他而出現 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為自己出席
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	這是他們所相信的美國使他們能夠搭公車在八月中站在華盛頓的陽光下
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	那是他們所相信的 , 重點不是黑人對白人:25%的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信在這個世界上有兩種類型的法律那些由較高權威制定的法律那些由人所制訂的法律
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	直到所有的法律都由人類所定與法律一致那些由較高權威所制定的法律我們才會活在一個公平的世界
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	正是如此 , 民權運動才是幫助他把自己的理想帶到生活的完美點 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們追隨 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順帶一提 , 他給了他 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 而不是 「 我有一個計畫 」 的演講 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	聽從政客現在 , 用他們全心全意的12點計劃 ,
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們沒有激勵任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者也有領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者持有權力或權威的位階但那些領導的人啟發我們
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織 , 我們跟隨那些領導的人 , 不是因為我們必須 , 而是因為我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們跟隨那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們而是為了我們自己
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	而且是那些以 " 為什麼 " 開頭的人有能力激發他們周圍的人或者找到那些激勵他們的人
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你怎麼會記得你把車子停在哪裡 ? 你怎麼知道你是朝著正確的方向前進 ? 神經科學家尼爾柏格研究我們周遭空間的神經機制 , 以及他們如何連結記憶與想像 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學 。
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	尼爾伯斯:你的大腦如何告訴你你在哪裡 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們停在一個很大的停車場 , 要怎麼記住我們停的車子的位置 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	荷馬面臨的問題是
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	而我們將會嘗試去了解他的大腦到底發生了什麼事情 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們先來看看海馬體 , 以黃色顯示 , 這是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你有所損害 , 像是阿茲海默症你就記不住事情包括你把車子停哪
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它的名字是拉丁文 " 海馬 " , 和海馬相似
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	和大腦的其他部分一樣 , 它是由神經元所構成的 ,
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	所以 , 人腦中有大約好幾百億的神經元
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元之間彼此溝通的方式是透過電脈衝或者是電突刺激通過彼此的聯繫來傳遞訊息
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩片細胞彼此之間非常緊密的連結組成
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家們已經開始了解空間記憶是如何運作的 , 藉由記錄老鼠在覓食或是探索一個環境中尋找食物時的單獨神經元 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	我們將會想像我們記錄一個單一神經元在這隻老鼠的海馬體裡面
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	而當它發出一丁點電時 , 就會有一個紅點和一個點擊 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以 , 我們看到的是 , 這神經元知道 , 只要老鼠進入環境中的某一個特定的地方 ,
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	並藉由電的突波來訊號到大腦的其他地方 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以我們可以讓神經元的傳送速率如動物所在位置的傳送 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們紀錄很多不同的神經元我們會看到當動物走到不同區域的環境中會有不同的神經發出訊號像是圖中是這個方形的盒子
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	它們一起組成地圖供給大腦 , 持續地告訴大腦: 「 我現在在環境中的哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	人類身上的位置細胞也會被記錄下來
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以癲癇患者有時需要用到他們的大腦活動來監測
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病患會玩一個電玩遊戲讓他們在一個小鎮上開車
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	河馬體內的位置細胞會被激發 , 開始發射電子脈衝 , 只要他們開車經過那個小鎮的一個特定位置 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	所以 , 位置細胞要如何知道老鼠或人是在環境中的哪個位置 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們環境的界線是特別重要的
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	上方那張圖是老鼠放在盒子之間的中間
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	而當你將箱子擴大時 , 激發的位置也會跟著擴張 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面那張 , 每當南方靠近一面牆時 , 都喜歡被激發 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你在盒子裡放置另一道牆那細胞在南方兩處都會被激發只要這個動物在盒子裡頭探索
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以 , 這預測到 , 在你周圍的範圍內 , 偵測到邊界的距離和方向 , 及其他範圍的範圍 , 對海馬迴特別重要 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 輸入海馬體的資訊會被發現哪些細胞進入海馬體 , 海馬體會對特定的邊界或是邊緣作出反應 , 老鼠會在四周探索 , 偵測到界線或邊緣 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	所以在左邊的細胞 , 你們可以看到 , 當動物接近墻或是一條向東邊的界線時 , 它都會被激發 , 不管是邊緣或是邊緣 , 不管是方形的方塊或圓形的兩面牆 , 或甚至是桌緣的邊緣 , 動物會跑來跑去 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞會在南邊的界線被激發 , 不論是桌子或牆壁的邊緣 , 或甚至是兩張桌子中間的縫隙 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	這也是我們認為位置細胞可以決定動物四處探索的原因之一
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也可以測試我們認為物體的位置 , 像是這個目標旗 , 在簡單的環境中或是你的車在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以我們可以讓人們去探索一個環境 , 並觀察他們需要記住的位置 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	然後 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 一般來說 , 它們可以很好地標記它們原本以為是旗幟或車子的地方 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在一些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和大小 , 就像我們對位置細胞所做的一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在那樣的情況下 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟位置的改變是改變你如何改變環境的形狀和大小 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 你看到的旗幟在小方形的環境中那個交叉點的地方 , 如果你問人們身在何處 , 但你讓環境變大 , 他們認為旗幟的形象和位置細胞被激發的方式完全相同 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	彷彿你記住旗子的位置 , 藉由在你所有位置細胞的儲存模式 , 你便能藉由四處走動 , 找到符合位置細胞被激發時的狀態 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	那會引導你回到你想要記住的位置 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們透過動作的位置 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以如果我們採取一些出乎意料的路徑──也許我們會停車、停車、閒逛──我們會因為自己的動作而整合──大致上就是回頭的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也會從一種叫做網格細胞的細胞得到這種路徑融合 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	目前網格細胞又再次被找出在海馬體上的輸入上 , 它們有點像位置細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠四處探索時 , 每個個體細胞會激發一系列不同的位置 , 分佈在整個環境中 , 以非常規的三角形網格為基礎 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	若你用數個網格細胞記錄下去 , 在這裡以不同的顏色顯示 , 每個細胞的網格狀激發模式 , 相對於其他細胞 , 會稍微改變 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	所以 , 紅色的會在這個網格被激發 , 而綠色的會在這個上面 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	綜合起來 , 就好像老鼠可以在周圍的環境中放置一個虛擬的網格 。 有點像你在地圖上找到的緯度和長度線 , 但用的是三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它四處移動時 , 電流的活動會從其中一個細胞傳遞到下一個細胞 , 以便追蹤到它的所在位置 , 讓它可以用本身的動作 , 知道它在環境中的位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有沒有網格細胞 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	嗯 , 因為所有網格狀的發射模式都有相同的對稱軸 , 相同的網格 , 橘色標出的位置 , 這表示網狀細胞在網格中的一個特定區域應該會根據我們在這六個方向之間的移動而變化 。 或從中間的六個方向奔跑 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以我們可以把人放進磁共振成像掃描儀 , 讓他們來做一個小小的電玩遊戲 , 就像我剛剛給你們看的那個 , 並且去找那個訊號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 在人類的前額葉皮質你會看到在老鼠身上的網格細胞
so back to homer .	所以 , 回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他大概還記得他車子的位置 , 就距離和方向 , 來延長建物和界線 , 在他停車的地方 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	可以用邊界偵測細胞來表示 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他也想起了從汽車停車場取出的路徑這會在網格細胞激發時呈現出來的樣子
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	這兩種細胞都可以使位置細胞被激發
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以藉由移動而回到他停車的位置找到目前位置與他大腦中儲存的位置與他停車的地方對應的位置細胞
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	這可以引導他回到那個位置 , 不用用用視覺提示 , 像是他的車是否真的到達那裡 。
maybe it's been towed .	或許已經是高塔上了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去抓它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以除了空間記憶之外 , 如果我們尋找整個腦內的網格狀激發模式之外 , 我們看到一連串的位置會一直活躍 , 當我們做各種自傳記憶任務時 , 比如記得你上次參加婚禮時的樣子 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 可能就是 , 代表我們周圍空間的神經機制也被用來產生視覺影像 , 讓我們能夠重現空間的場景 , 至少 , 當我們想要想像它們時已經發生在我們身上的事件 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以 , 如果這正在發生 , 你的記憶可以開始是位置細胞透過緊密的相互連結彼此啟動然後重新啟動邊界細胞來創造出你觀點周圍的空間結構
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以在空間中移動這個視野 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種我還沒提到的細胞頭部方向細胞 , 它們就像指南針一樣會根據面的不同方向而發射 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義你想要為你的視覺影像產生的方向 , 所以你可以想像當你在這場婚禮上發生了什麼事 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是認知神經科學中的一個新世代的一個例子 , 我們開始了解心理的過程 , 如你如何記住、想像 , 或甚至思考數十億個獨立的神經元所產生的行為 。
thank you very much .	非常感謝 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一個全球安全的推動 , 由各種機構間的合作、政府、私營機構和民眾共同推動 。 這不僅僅是開放原始碼的粉絲們的遠景 , 還包括jamesstavridis的最高指揮官 , 北大西洋公約組織的最高指揮官 , 他們都在近期的軍事歷史中分享了生動的時刻 , 解釋了為什麼未來要用橋來建造 , 而不是用牆 。
